# THE BOOK OF ECCLESIASTES

If there were two books in the Bible, extracted from the sixty‑six, that would have a special application to [America ]{.class_1790}in the twentieth century, those two books would be [Colossians ]{.class_1790}(in the New Testament) and [Ecclesiastes ]{.class_1790}(in the Old Testament). The reason for this is obvious if anyone knows anything about the spiritual condition of America since the days of Billy Sunday (ending in 1933). The masses of unregenerate Americans (Biblical term: ["heathen"]{.class_1791}), today, need what Solomon had to say ["under the sun," ]{.class_1791}and the mass of apostate Fundamentalists (especially the Christian educators) would need what Paul had to say in the epistle to the Colossians (see [The Bible Believer's Commentary on Galatians‑Colossians, ]{.class_1790}1997).

The curse on the unregenerate Americans came through the mass promotion of materialism and humanism, via television. The curse on the Christian educators, entrusted with training "Champions for Christ," came from emphasizing philosophy and tradition (Col. 2:8) at the cost of Biblical authority (see [King James Onlyism versus Scholarship Onlyism,]{.class_1790} 1992). The Conservative and Fundamental Christian colleges, universities, and seminaries decided that ["all the treasures of wisdom and knowledge" ]{.class_1791}could NOT be found in Jesus Christ (Col. 2:3). They decided that the "treasures" were to be found in Hebrew and Greek lexicons; therefore, their "calling" was to get rid of the [Authorized Version ]{.class_1790}of the Holy Bible by correcting it twenty-four hours a day with the preferences, opinions, and traditions of destructive Bible critics. Most of these apostates vowed allegiance to a lost pile of papers (humorously called "the original autographs"), which none of them had ever seen in a lifetime. (As far as that goes, no man, living or dead, in 1,800 years, had [ever ]{.class_1790}seen them.) The curriculum at these schools was designed to teach the Christian "leader" that it was the Holy Spirit, operating under the directive will of God (Rom. 8:27), who was "revealing treasures of wisdom and knowledge" each time the faculty altered a word or a verse in the [King James Bible. ]{.class_1790}This became (and is) the standard "curriculum" of Bob Jones University, []{#6z0vNAIsTD_RezYjRLYFFA63.xhtml_page_4}Pensacola Christian College, Liberty University, Tennessee Temple University, Baptist Bible College, Moody, Fuller, Wheaton, Pillsbury, Maranatha, Stetson, Judson, Howard, and the seminaries at Dallas, New Orleans, Denver, Louisville, etc.

Oddly, the leaders of these schools (with their faculty members) all [pretended ]{.class_1790}it was the Holy Spirit who was leading them in their preferences and opinions, yet none of them---not ONE in one hundred years---left any testimony, verbal or written, as to WHEN or WHERE or HOW or under WHOM their faith in the Holy Bible ([AV]{.class_1790}) was destroyed.

For five years, in the [Bible Believers' Bulletin, ]{.class_1790}we[ ]{.class_1790}tried to get just one of these leaders \[the list included Curtis Hutson, John R. Rice, Doug Kutilek, Robert Sumner, John MacArthur, Chuck Swindoll, Jerry Falwell, Harold Willmington, Sumner Wemp, Pastor Schettler (Arlin Horton: PCC), et al.\] to give a word of testimony. None of them did. Nor did Donald Waite, James Price, James Dobson, Zane Hodges, Arthur Farstad, Wilbur Pickering, Gary Hudson, or James Combs. They allowed (and still allow) the Body of Christ to think it was the Holy Spirit who showed them the errors in the Book. Since we have already documented these matters to the tune of more than two hundred pages ([How to Teach the "Original" Greek, ]{.class_1790}1992), we will not waste the reader's time with it now.

When speaking of the destruction of America on a national level, we deal with a nation that magnified the flesh (via TV) and substituted materialism for the Lord Jesus Christ (see [The Damnation of a Nation, ]{.class_1790}1991). A little spicy "spiritual" flavor was added to this manure pile by the National Education Association (1964--1984) to give it a semblance of something worthy about which to get religious. This topping (called Humanism), as anyone knows, is simply a polite term for Atheism. (The NEA, CBS, NBC, CNN, [Life, Time, ]{.class_1790}and [Newsweek ]{.class_1790}are always very "sensitive" and "caring" when propagating Atheism; they don't wish to offend their readers and viewers unnecessarily.) Naturalism is the basic root for both philosophies (Materialism and Humanism), as it is also the basis for Empiricism, Pragmatism, and Phenomenology (see [The Christian's Handbook of Science and Philosophy]{.class_1790}, 1985). It is simply the jungle paganism of 800--100 B.C. dressed up in "double speak": []{#6z0vNAIsTD_RezYjRLYFFA63.xhtml_page_5}i.e., misleading terminology to make you think it is something else. It was the Athenian philosophers (Acts 17:32) who rejected the physical resurrection. The old Frisco-faggot, Socrates, had to reject it. The way he lived, he could not afford to be personally accountable to any "god," not even the snake god to whom he sacrificed a [rooster ]{.class_1790}before killing himself. All of the Athenian philosophers believed you got it HERE; there was no "hereafter" unless, possibly, a Hindu transmigration of "souls" to animals or people. Accountability for sin, to a Creator, was not in the deck.

The basic philosophy behind all secular education, from the First Grade to Graduate School, is this: what cannot be detected by the five physical senses is not real; it can be rejected.

The [Book of Ecclesiastes]{.class_1790} was written by a Deist whose "life‑style" was total devotion to ultra-materialism. This man confessed that he had devoted a lifetime to experimenting with the flesh, in all of its manifestations: sex, music, wine, food, hobbies, works, introspection, physical rest, and sleep. He did not major in worshipping God. To the contrary, he disobeyed three commandments of God that deal with kings (Deut. 17:16--17), while taking on 1,000 women to satisfy his "sexual orientation" (or "alternate life‑styles." The NEA and the press are always very sensitive about these matters!). He wound up as one of the greatest materialistic, sexual IDOLATORS in the Bible (1 Kings 11:1--10).

The utility in King Solomon's "diary" lies in the fact that Solomon had access to every "god" that modern Americans worship: the first three being money, sex, and education. Furthermore, Solomon was excessively acquainted with all three in a way that no modern news media "god" (Bobby and Jack Kennedy, Nelson Mandela, Ted Turner, the Rockefellers, Howard Hughes, Errol Flynn, Madonna, Michael Jackson, Jesse Jackson, Magic Johnson, Bill Cosby, Eddie Murphy, M. L. King Jr., et al.) could match. If you are looking for historical "facts" learned by personal experience, then Solomon, without a doubt, is "king of the mountain" when it comes to Playboy‑Penthouse-Hedonistic-Wealthy-Pleasure. In the days of Madonna, Michael Jackson, and Bill Cosby, copper was so rare the government had to stick zinc into the pennies; and silver was so rare they had to mint copper quarters and half‑dollars. Conversively, in []{#6z0vNAIsTD_RezYjRLYFFA63.xhtml_page_6}Solomon's day, gold was so common (1 Kings 10:21) that no one bothered even to collect silver. Some amateur like Liz Taylor (with five or six husbands) would go down in Solomon's book as an amateur. Solomon had as many women at his disposal, in any year, as Wilt Chamberlain or Magic Johnson had; and no one else had access to them, no one could sue him for fooling with them, none of them could leave him for someone else, and he didn't have to worry about birth control or VD. Chamberlain, Johnson, and Co. were greenhorns. They couldn't get into Solomon's league with the backing of TV, the Justice Department, and the District Court judges.

A modern, millionaire, American "swingee" is not in Solomon's league.

The objections to the authorship of the Book (see Introduction) come from the flesh; specifically, the fleshy nature of the fleshy critic who doesn't want you to believe that there actually lived (3,000 years ago) a real king who did everything that any twentieth-century millionaire did, when it came to the flesh, and, at the same time, was three times as rich as any executive connected with Wal‑Mart, Exxon, General Motors, and AT&T. But King Solomon DID and he WAS.

You see, if you are an evolutionist---all commercial TV outlets are evolutionists, and so are the editorial policies of the twenty top dailies---you must believe that there not only have been advances in communications and transportation since 100 B.C., you must believe that a twentieth-century American surely knows something "new" about sex and the flesh that Solomon could not have known. Your religion requires this of you.

Wrong again; with a thousand wives, princesses, and concubines (Ecc. 7:28) taken from Europe, Asia, Africa, and the islands of the sea (1 Kings 11:1), ranging in age from sixteen years old to sixty, there is nothing---I say, absolutely nothing---about fleshy pleasures that you know (or any of your friends or associates) that Solomon did not know about more than 2,000 years before Columbus set sail for the Bermuda Triangle. The trouble lies in the fact that after experiencing all of these things, Solomon came to the wrong conclusion, at least in the eyes of every dope‑headed, fornicating materialist in the United States---including all the atheists and []{#6z0vNAIsTD_RezYjRLYFFA63.xhtml_page_7}humanists. You see, according to every swinger, from the White House and the Senate down to the junkies in Queens, N.Y. (plus every habitual fornicator in the movie and TV industries), Solomon was [supposed]{.class_1790} to have come to the following conclusion (which he did not come to):

"Let us hear the conclusion of the whole matter. When you are dead, you are dead, like a dog (Ecc. 9:5), and nothing follows (Ecc. 9:6); therefore, eat, drink, and be merry (Ecc. 8:15). Let it all hang out, because in the 'Gusto' life you need to 'go for broke'!"

Solomon---in absolute defiance of everything taught (and believed) in the public school system, both houses of Congress, the UN, and all the news media---says the conclusion is that God will judge you for what you did in the dark that no one saw.

["Fear God, and keep his commandments\...For God shall bring every work into judgment, with every secret thing, whether it be good, or whether it be evil" ]{.class_1791}(Ecc. 12:14).

Wrong conclusion. No teacher in the Federal School Soviet, from Kindergarten to Postgraduate School, is allowed to tell any student that he (the student) is personally accountable to God Almighty after death. The instructor cannot even hint that there is a possibility that such a thing might happen. No teacher in the NEA is allowed to tell any student anything about life beyond the grave other than it is either unconscious annihilation or a chemical absorption into eternal matter: MATERIALISM.

The Commandments (referred to above) cannot even be printed or posted on the school grounds of any school in the USA. Teaching them would cause such an emotional panic among Americans (who talk about being "modern" men) that there would be a riot in the classroom. So out they went. And in came the rock music, drugs, condoms, abortions, rapes, and bulletproof vests (literally). The ferocious and "insensitive" teaching that God will judge every American schoolboy (or girl) for what he did with his hands and feet, his eyes and mouth, his mind and his time, is absolutely unthinkable. No B.C. Athenian (Acts 17:31--32) believed that, and the American Federal Educational System has remained at this B.C. level (500 B.C. to 100 B.C.) since World War I. This pagan primitivism is due, not to scientific advancement or "great strides in knowledge of human []{#6z0vNAIsTD_RezYjRLYFFA63.xhtml_page_8}nature" or "breakthroughs in understanding personality," but is due, purely, to EMOTIONAL PANIC on the part of the news media, judges, and teachers.

In the National Education Association, God doesn't know what [anyone]{.class_1790} is doing, saying, or thinking. They are only accountable to themselves. In the Book, God knows the thoughts that come into any man's mind (Ezek. 11:5): ["every one of them." ]{.class_1791}Solomon says that these "secret things" will be judged, and Paul says they will be judged ["by Jesus Christ" ]{.class_1791}(Rom. 2:16). This is the wrong conclusion for any dissertation on philosophy for a Ph.D. degree; at least, if you are a twentieth-century, worldy‑wise humanitarian. Solomon will not line up with the American news media and the UN. He insists that there is individual accountability to God, in an individual judgment, dealing with individual sins, and it takes place [after ]{.class_1790}death.

So this is THE book, par excellent, for a modern, unregenerate American to study if he really is searching for the truth or for truths. Since ["the fear of the LORD is the beginning of wisdom" ]{.class_1791}(Psa. 111:10), then wisdom will begin at the end of [Ecclesiastes ]{.class_1790}(Ecc. 12:13). If the truth seeker then continues, he would eventually find ["all the treasures of wisdom and knowledge" ]{.class_1791}(Col. 2:3) in the New Testament. They are found in ONE man; not in any set of encyclopedias, college curricula, scientific journals, or even the Library of Congress itself, which contains more than 12,000,000 books. ["He that feareth God shall come forth of them all" ]{.class_1791}(Ecc. 7:18).

King Solomon had more money ([literally]{.class_1790}) than he knew what to do with. Like Arlin Horton (PCA and PCC), he had to sit around and think up odd ways to get rid of it, without putting it to use winning souls.

Americans worship sex. Solomon had more wives than one hundred men could handle reasonably (that would be ten wives apiece). He had a fresh new wife every morning for over two and one‑half years before he went back to number one, and none of his wives could step out on him. If any of them got pregnant, they would produce [his kids, ]{.class_1790}not someone else's.

Americans worship intellectual wisdom. They are literally "bugs" on education (see [The Anti-Intellectual Manifesto,]{.class_1790} 1992). Solomon []{#6z0vNAIsTD_RezYjRLYFFA63.xhtml_page_9}was the wisest man who ever lived and he wrote more "sententious sayings" and profound proverbs than Einstein, Clarence Darrow, George Bernard Shaw, Ernest Hemmingway, Ben Franklin, Bertrand Russell, and Paul Tillich combined. Furthermore, he wrote from direct experience, not just reading and meditation. In addition to this, he enjoyed choral groups, odd musical instruments, works of art, chariots and horses, politics, fanning, gardening, landscaping, husbandry, and philosophy. On top of that, he was in a position that no man, before or since, ever occupied. He reigned as a millionaire monarch over a Bible-believing people.

The book of [Ecclesiastes ]{.class_1790}was recorded for the benefit of an American humanist or materialist, or any other modern man stupid enough to think that "man is the measure of all things" or that "death ends it all." It is written for every rich man who thinks that success lies in stockpiles of cash and bonds or bevies of movie stars and professional models. I know of no other book in the sixty‑six that speaks out as loudly and clearly (and as forcibly and persistently) against the gods of America as [Ecclesiastes. ]{.class_1790}It is the recorded experience of a man who tried everything that the "natural man" wants to try, by turning himself over to every impulse of flesh and mind that reside in the unregenerate nature of the sinner. He then came to the conclusion that: no man can understand life apart from God, no man can know about life after death apart from supernatural revelation; no man can learn from his troubles and sufferings by natural reasoning, and no man can find out ALL the answers this side of the grave.

The wisest man who ever lived winds up as an [anti-intellectual]{.class_1790} when he gets through covering the field that fifty philosophers tried to cover between 600 B.C. and A.D. 1990 (2,590 years!), after Solomon finished plowing the field. See Ecclesiastes 12:12. The "peroration" of the preacher's sermon is:

1\. Find the words of truth (John 17:17).

2\. Don't waste time messing around with a lot of books (Col. 2:3).

3\. Fear God, instead of man (Matt. 10:28) or circumstances.

4\. Get ready to give an account to God on an individual basis (Rom. 14:12) after you "pop off" (as the British say).

We hope you enjoy this study of life ["under the sun."]{.class_1791}

# Introduction {.heading_69}

The book of [Ecclesiastes ]{.class_1790}has 12 chapters, 222 verses, and 5,584 words. The author of the book---notwithstanding the opinions of the majority of Christian scholars---is Solomon, ["the son of David" ]{.class_1791}(1:12, 16). The efforts by the majority of Conservative scholars to get rid of this authorship by assigning it to an anonymous "Qoheleth" (or "Koheleth"), is just one more coffin nail in the casket of the Scholars' Union; they have been driving them since the days of Origen (A.D. 184--254). These same "unimpeachable" scholars tried, many years ago, to get Isaiah run out of the book of Isaiah by allotting the last twenty-seven chapters (40--66) to a "Deutero-Isaiah." The same "Doubting Thomases" also decided that an anonymous presbyter wrote the book of Revelation, instead of the apostle John. (See the discussion below.)

Someone has aptly remarked that in [Job ]{.class_1790}we have "The Unhappy Man," in [Psalms ]{.class_1790}we have "The Happy Man," in [Proverbs ]{.class_1790}"The Wise Man," in [Ecclesiastes ]{.class_1790}"The Worldly Man," and in the [Song of Solomon]{.class_1790} "The Heavenly Man."

The theme of the book of Ecclesiastes is life ["under the sun." ]{.class_1791}The expression occurs twenty‑nine times in twelve chapters. The term ["Preacher" ]{.class_1791}(Koheleth) occurs seven times in the book: three times at the beginning (chapter 1), three times at the end (chapter 12), and one time in the middle (chapter 7). The correct title of the book---notwithstanding the opinions of the Scholars' Union---is ["Ecclesiastes,"]{.class_1790} coming from a Greek word meaning "a member of a congregation" or a speaker for a congregation, who is addressing an assembly. (Our word for church \[ekklesia\] comes from this; it refers to a "called out" assembly.) It is the Old Latin, written 200 years before Sinaiticus and Vaticanus (the Septuagint manuscripts) that applied the term to the book. Here, Jerome correctly followed the Old Latin (as he did in several places in the New Testament). For a detailed discussion of the mythological LXX, which never existed before A.D. 180, see chapter 4 in [The Christian's Handbook of Manuscript Evidence, ]{.class_1790}1970.

Three objections to the book are registered by Conservative and []{#6z0vNAIsTD_RezYjRLYFFA102.xhtml_page_11}Liberal scholars in the Alexandrian Cult---same clique when it comes to rejection of absolute truth and absolute authority. First of all, since the Alexandrian Cult are all "educationolaters" or "manuscriptolators," they worship [teachers. ]{.class_1790}None of them can [preach, ]{.class_1790}and none of them ever submitted to the authority of any Bible‑believing preacher, so you can forecast their reaction to the title ["the Preacher."]{.class_1791} They consider themselves vastly [superior ]{.class_1790}to preachers, and their lives are largely taken up with trying to bring local churches into submission to faculty members of Christian seminaries, colleges, and universities. If any of these august gentlemen---we will list more than forty in this commentary---were ever called to "preach," they were knocked slap out of their calling within two years after they went off to school. You will find the details of how this was done in our work on [How to Teach the "Original" Greek ]{.class_1790}(1992). It is true that in the last half of the twentieth century the slickest of the destructive Fundamentalists have learned how to copy the evangelistic style and have adapted it to their "rapping" and "teaching." But any experienced evangelist can spot the professional speaker giving his audience "the shaft." Men like Swindoll, MacArthur, Stanley, Schuller, and Robertson are professional speakers; [preaching ]{.class_1790}is as far out of their field as Jai‑Alai.

For this reason, you will find Wayne Peterson ([Broadman Bible Commentary, ]{.class_1790}1971, p. 100) saying that ["the Preacher"]{.class_1791}[ ]{.class_1796}will not do; "teacher" is more appropriate. To reinforce this direct move towards apostasy, Jerry Falwell's crew ([NKJV]{.class_1790}), with the aid of the editor of the [Sword of the Lord ]{.class_1790}(Curtis Hutson) and Elmer Towns, has given scholars credit for finding the ["words of truth"]{.class_1796}[ ]{.class_1790}(Ecc. 12:10) and "nailing them down" (Ecc. 12:11). Observe how, in this context, that Jesus Christ gives the words of truth to scholars, instead of preachers (Ecc. 12:11), for the ["one shepherd" ]{.class_1791}is capitalized in the [NKJV. ]{.class_1790}Typical. Absolutely consistent with such corrupt translations as the [NKJV]{.class_1790}, which also capitalizes ["he,"]{.class_1791} in 2 Thessalonians 2:7, to force you to accept the private interpretation of the destructive critic who removed the command to ["study" ]{.class_1791}the Bible (2 Tim. 2:15) from the Bible ([NKJV]{.class_1790}). Absolutely standard degradation, uniform apostasy, canonical corruption, regulation []{#6z0vNAIsTD_RezYjRLYFFA102.xhtml_page_12}rottenness. That's the Alexandrian Cult.

In addition to this, the Cult finds the theology of the book extremely distasteful to the "good, godly scholars," so they insist it had to be written later than Solomon's time; most of them force it up into a post-exilic date (500 B.C.), more than four hundred years after Solomon is dead. This is the same coalition that decided Daniel wrote his prophecies on Babylon, Persia, and Greece [AFTER ]{.class_1790}they ceased to be empires. The ancestors of these muddled Merry‑Andrews taught that someone wrote [Deuteronomy ]{.class_1790}and [Leviticus]{.class_1790} after the time of David and Saul. To follow through with this bizarre nonsense, the [Broadman Bible Commentary ]{.class_1790}cancels Solomon as the author by retranslating Ecclesiastes 1:12 as "I HAVE BEEN KING" instead of ["I was king." ]{.class_1791}To make sure that this perverted, private misinterpretation is rooted and grounded in your mind, Peterson quotes his own mistake four times on the first two pages of his work. This is to make you think that since Solomon was king over Israel until he died (1 Kings 11:42), he could not have written "I HAVE BEEN KING." It doesn't ever seem to occur to these bewildered, shallow‑thinking Alexandrians that Solomon is writing a "last will and testament" to be read (and studied) [after his death.]{.class_1790} He mentions his coming death in the last chapter of Ecclesiastes, and the judgment that is sure to follow it.

The critics who deny Solomon's authorship say simply that an anonymous nobody "assumed the identity of Solomon" (Peterson, ibid., p. 108). Hence, in a typically corrupt commentary (L. D. Johnson, [Layman's Bible Commentary,]{.class_1790} Broadman Press, 1982), you will find the phrase "Qoheleth" recurring again and again, without any article attached to it. This makes it "a [koheleth" ]{.class_1790}or "a [qoheleth" ]{.class_1790}or "a teacher." The word has the article on it (["the preacher"]{.class_1791})[ ]{.class_1791}in every Hebrew text extant of Ecclesiastes 12:8. Volume III of the [Hebrew‑Greek‑English Interlinear ]{.class_1790}(Assoc. Publishers, 1978) uses the article throughout. (It also uses the word ["Preacher"]{.class_1791} throughout, even where no article is present (Ecc. 1:1). An unidentified nobody, lying about his own father---see Ecclesiastes 1:1---and his calling (same text), and then coming up with the material found in this book, is a teaching that requires one to stretch his imagination from here to the moon and back. An unidentified []{#6z0vNAIsTD_RezYjRLYFFA102.xhtml_page_13}"blank" who covers Fascism, Communism, Idealism, Existentialism, Naturalism, Pragmatism, Skepticism, Agnosticism, Materialism, Stoicism, Fatalism, Deism, and Empiricism, in less than forty pages (more than 300 years [before ]{.class_1790}the first Greek philosopher shows up!), cannot pass by [unnoticed ]{.class_1790}by anyone who can see thirty feet. Imagine (if you can!) an unknown philosopher called a "teacher," who was the greatest king Jerusalem ever had (Ecc. 2:9, 1:12), and no one, one thousand years either side of him, even knew his [name, ]{.class_1790}although he built houses, planted trees and gardens, built aqueducts and swimming pools, owned more cattle than any king in Jerusalem, cohabited with 1,000 different women (Ecc. 2:4--9, 7:28), and remained INCOGNITO! As the British say: Balderdash, or Tommyrot. (I always liked the German: "QUATSCH!")

You can see why the Alexandrian Cult wishes to move things up to A.D. 300 and A.D. 400. They want to salute their Athenian colleagues (Acts 17) so ["the]{.class_1791} [wise" ]{.class_1791}(1 Cor. 1--2) can get "a cut of the action." They (like the apostates who wrote the Septuagint, long after the New Testament was completed) wanted the Greeks to get some credit for wisdom. This also explains the ill‑timed appearance of the Apocryphal ["Ecclesiasticus," ]{.class_1790}found in the Septuagint. The dim-sighted and scatterbrained Alexandrian scholar, who forged this counterfeit, simply tried to copy Solomon to make you think that someone like him (the dim‑witted and scatterbrained) wrote [Ecclesiastes ]{.class_1790}after Greece became a world power. Alexandrians are as transparent in their felonies and frauds as a plate glass window. Only Hebrew and Greek scholars seem to have any difficulty in catching them in the act. [Ecclesiasticus is ]{.class_1790}as phony as a three dollar bill.

To prove the late date of [Ecclesiastes]{.class_1790}, an appeal is made to Persian words "which could not have been known in Solomon's time" (see Sir Robert Anderson's [Daniel in the Critic's Den ]{.class_1790}for more of this nonsense). The word ["end"]{.class_1791} (Ecc. 3:11) is supposed to be one of these late words that Solomon couldn't have known. However, it appears in Joel 2:20 (Heb.: [soph]{.class_1790}), which was written before Esther's mother was born. Again, the word for ["event," ]{.class_1791}in Ecclesiastes 2:14, is said to be late. The word, however, is found in 1 Samuel 6:9 and Ruth 2:3 (Heb.: [mikreh]{.class_1790}). Still, it is rumored that the word for ["purpose," ]{.class_1791}in Ecclesiastes 3:1 (Heb.: [hephez]{.class_1790}), is too late for []{#6z0vNAIsTD_RezYjRLYFFA102.xhtml_page_14}Solomon. Do you see, yet, what is going to happen? Can't you guess? Why, bless my soul, in order to get rid of Solomon as the author, you are going to have to say that whoever wrote Ruth, Joel, and 1 Samuel had to write them AFTER the captivity, after Ezra and Nehemiah returned to Jerusalem. That is the result of trying to drag the Book down to your level of ignorance.

Peterson tells us, "The evidence, above, indicates a date in the late Persian, or early Greek, period of history" (ibid, p. 103). The above evidence is based on the hypothetical guesswork that the skepticism in Ecclesiastes is a NATIONAL skepticism, based on the experiences of Israel after the captivity. This national skepticism is supposed to have turned the nation against the book of [Proverbs.]{.class_1790}

There is nothing national in the entire book.

The book doesn't mention ONE of the three major feasts of Israel.

The writer of [Ecclesiastes ]{.class_1790}says ["my son"]{.class_1791} (Ecc. 12:12), which is the expression used throughout the book of Proverbs (see 2:1, 3:1, 5:1, 6:1, and 31:2).

Delitzsch, the Hebrew scholar, says that there is a strong influence of the Phoenician in this book, which "points to a date between the 7th and 3rd centuries B.C." Nonsense. Solomon was all over Phoenicia (2 Chron. 2:11, 14). Delitzsch has mistaken the individual style of an educated, sophisticated, worldly‑wise man for the average style of writing found in Solomon's time. You are to believe that the wisest man who ever lived (2 Chron. 9:6), who had trade routes all over the known world (2 Chron. 8:18), and was visited by philosophers (1 Kings 4:31) and royal dignities from other nations---who went back and reported to their own people what they had heard---would know only the current words of his own language during his lifetime. This demands a fantastic naivete that could only be matched by the followers of Janet Reno, Jimmy Bakker, Oral Roberts, or Jim Jones.

Scott says that the "Aramaic characteristics" indicate a post‑exilic date. Why? The "Aramaic" is in Genesis 31:47, and a Jew had to confess that Jacob was a Syrian (Deut. 26:5. Syriac) when he appeared before the Lord in Jerusalem. Solomon's kingdom went to Syria, on the Euphrates River (2 Sam. 8:3); that is where Aramaic came from. What Scott meant was, that having found large Aramaic []{#6z0vNAIsTD_RezYjRLYFFA102.xhtml_page_15}portions in Daniel, he assumed---without any reason for doing so---that Ecclesiastes had to be written AFTER Daniel. Fruitloops in the Twinkies.

"All that is known about the author is what is stated in Ecclesiastes 12:9--10, and what can be inferred from allusions in the book" (Peterson, ibid, p. 102). ("Don't call us; we'll call you.") Peterson's allusions are ILLUSIONS. What are actually found in the book of Ecclesiastes are facts, and these facts identify the author as the richest and wisest king Jerusalem ever had---it had been ruled by David and Melchizedek, as well as Adonizedek---and he calls himself ["the son of David." ]{.class_1791}These allusions (see above) are just hallucinations or illusions to the critical commentators, for they are not facts. Having settled the matters of scholarship and date of writing (contrary to the majority of "recognized scholars"; see [The Anti‑Intellectual Manifesto,]{.class_1790} 1992), let us see why God wanted this book written and preserved, and why He put it into the canon, over the objections of the Rabbinical School of Shammai and others.

The truth of the matter is that the entire book (with the exception of a few verses on the end) is aimed at two classes of people: intellectual agnostics and educated humanists who are engaged in trying to figure out life and death on this earth, apart from divine revelation. The gullible (and unhinged) commentators try to read into the book "Koheleth's convictions," leading you to believe that he is at work trying to rid himself of his doubts about things that really bother him. To the contrary, Solomon is simply recording the thoughts that went through his head when he took the same approach to life that all educated philosophers take, apart from []{#6z0vNAIsTD_RezYjRLYFFA102.xhtml_page_16}Scriptural revelation.

Solomon has, before him, more than half of the Psalter, the book of [Job, ]{.class_1790}and several hundred proverbs which he had collated. When he makes statements in [Ecclesiastes ]{.class_1790}that do not line up with Job's views (Ecc. 9:5 vs. Job 19:26, for example), or makes statements that don't line up with [Proverbs ]{.class_1790}(Ecc. 8:14 vs. Prov. 10:3, 24, for example), he is not stating his own religious convictions at all. He is merely recording what any naturalistic, rational philosopher would THINK while trying to unravel the great mysteries of life and death. 1\. The vanity of selfish living (4:7).

2\. The vanity of dedication to pleasure (7:6).

4\. The vanity of becoming famous (9:15).

5\. The vanity of labor and work (1:3).

8\. The vanity of hoarding money (5:10).

9\. The vanity of worldly wisdom (2:13).

10\. The vanity of optimism (11:8).

George C. Hendry (Princeton University) says, "It is a mistake to brand Ecclesiastes as a skeptic, or an apostle of despair. The melancholy refrain 'vanity of vanity, all is vanity,' is not his verdict upon life in general, but only upon the misguided human endeavor to treat the created world as an end in itself. He knows all the time []{#6z0vNAIsTD_RezYjRLYFFA102.xhtml_page_17}that it has a positive significance\...the significance of the world, is that it can become a MEDIUM for the revelation of God's goodness, wisdom, and righteousness. # Chapter 1 {.heading_69}

1:1 The words of the Preacher, the son of David, king in Jerusalem.

2 Vanity of vanities, saith the Preacher, vanity of vanities; all is vanity.

3 What profit hath a man of all his labour which he taketh under the sun?

4 One generation passeth away, and another generation cometh: but the earth abideth for ever.

5 The sun also ariseth, and the sun goeth down, and hasteth to his place where he arose.

6 The wind goeth toward the south, and turneth about unto the north; it whirleth about continually, and the wind returneth again according to his circuits.

7 All the rivers run into the sea; yet the sea is not full; unto the place from whence the rivers come, thither they return again.

The first verse identifies the writer beyond any dispute (exactly as James 1:1 and Rom. 1:1 identify [their ]{.class_1790}authors). The word "Koheleth" is a [feminine ]{.class_1790}word, but it can apply to a masculine "gatherer of assemblies." The word is not a "name"; it is a word that designates [an office.]{.class_1790} It is a feminine participle from the verb ["Kahal," ]{.class_1790}and the feminine form has no affect on the sex of the person calling the assembly, exactly as many words in Spanish and German have genders (knife, fork, horse, etc.), although the object is [sexless]{.class_1790}. Observe how Martin Luther made the sun (feminine: ["Die Sonne"]{.class_1790}) become a type of Christ (Psa. 19:6), as a [male ]{.class_1790}bridegroom (["Brautigam"]{.class_1790}). It is "HIS bridechamber (German: ["seiner"]{.class_1790}) for a female "sun" (["Die Sonne"]{.class_1790}).

It is King Solomon who assembles the elders of Israel (1 Kings 8:1), and preaches to them. The writer, therefore, is not some anonymous "Koheleth," but as a king (present tense: not "I have been"), he is the ["son of David" ]{.class_1791}(cf Matt. 1:1 and 22:45). Having received this clear‑cut, definite information (which no one could []{#6z0vNAIsTD_RezYjRLYFFA172.xhtml_page_27}possibly misinterpret, and which needs no updating whatsoever), the majority of you‑know‑who insist it is some nobody writing incognito and using Solomon as a lying pseudonym for himself, without having enough guts to tell you his name. This fictitious Alexandrian idiot claimed to be David's son and also claimed to have reigned in Jerusalem. The fact that he would have been a bald‑faced liar in doing this means nothing to the "good, godly, dedicated scholars." If you tend to disbelieve this and attribute it to Ruckman's abrasive nature or "sarcastic attitude," read their analysis of the authorship of 1 and 2 Timothy in [The Bible Believer's Commentary on the Pastoral Epistles, ]{.class_1790}1990).

The author is King Solomon; he is the only man in Hebrew history (1 and 2 Kings) who could match HALF the requirements laid down in Ecclesiastes. There are no other near competitors on the field. At least, there are no others if you are an honest man and believe the Bible is the word of God, etc.

The [theme ]{.class_1790}of the book is now given. Its theme is Psalm 39:5, which is ["A Psalm of David,"]{.class_1791} Solomon's father. David lived [before ]{.class_1790}Solomon, certainly not after the exile of 598--586 B.C.

The word ["vanity" ]{.class_1791}is from ["hebel" ]{.class_1790}(which comes from "habal"), meaning "breath, exhalation," or "vapor." It can also refer to a mist or darkness; hence, something "in vain" or "to no purpose." For this reason, the [King James ]{.class_1790}expression, ["vanity," ]{.class_1791}is vastly superior to the [NASV's]{.class_1790} "futility" (Ecc. 8:14), for again, the "King's English" contains two meanings which the [NASV]{.class_1790} does not contain. ["Vanity," ]{.class_1791}in the King's English (see Ecc. 8:14), reveals two things: 1. A thing is useless and without profit if it is ["vain" ]{.class_1791}(Judg. 9:4, 11:3). 2. If it is in "vain," it must be connected with self‑love (2 Tim. 3:1--2): i.e., "vanity." In the New Testament sense, works done for self constitute errands run for a corpse (Col. 3:3), so they burn up at the Judgment Seat of Christ (1 Cor. 3). [Not one essential item ]{.class_1790}that your founding fathers considered to be of value will be restored by [any ]{.class_1790}political group in the next ten years.

"There is no remembrance of former things."

Do you have any idea of how many "forgotten champions" this world has hosted in the last fifty years? Have you any idea how quickly record breakers are forgotten, and their records confined to the limbo of the elephants' graveyard? For example: do you remember the name of the champion onion peeler of 1980? What! Do you mean to tell me that in less than fifteen years you have forgotten Alfonso Salvo of New York, who peeled fifty‑two onions in five minutes? How could you!? And who could ever forget Daley Thompson (Great Britain) who scored 8,847 points in the Olympic Games of 1984 (Los Angeles)? Think of ole' David Coburn, who []{#6z0vNAIsTD_RezYjRLYFFA172.xhtml_page_41}stacked 291 dominoes on one supporting domino (Aug. 19,1988)! How could you forget him so quickly? And what about Lori Deanne Adams of Iowa (Aug. 21, 1979), who held the world's record for throwing a rolling pin? She threw it 175 feet, 2½ inches.

Do you see what has happened? The "NEWS" has gotten such an overkill on its material that you are simply being bombarded, twenty‑four hours a day, with either trivia or propaganda. You are not finding out what is going on at all. You have already forgotten Steve Cram, who broke three world records in one year. And let's hear it for Bob Beamon, who made a historic broadjump of 29 feet, 2½ inches in 1968 at the Olympics. And don't forget that champion of champions (who ate Jack Armstrong's "breakfast of champions"!), Jan Van Deurs Froman of Copenhagen, Denmark, who set a world's record by blowing 355 consecutive smoke rings in one inhalation (Aug. 1979)!

["There is no remembrance of former things," ]{.class_1791}not even for a few years.

Suppose Nolan Ryan does strike out two dozen men. Roger Clemens (April 29, 1986) beat "Tex" all hollow. This pitcher (for the Boston Red Sox) fanned twenty batters in one game. But who has thought about Roger Clemens today? The longest career in three major leagues was held by James "Deacon" McGuire (1865--1936). I never met anyone in America who knew who "Deacon" was, where he came from, when he lived, or what he did while he was here. I have never talked with anyone in fifty states (in fifty years) who knew that Marvin Hart was the world's champion heavyweight boxer in 1905 or that Ingemar Johannson was in 1959 or that John Tate was in 1979 or that Tim Witherspoon was in 1984. They are no more remembered than John Wilkinson of Luling, Texas, who (on June 28, 1980) spit watermelon seeds 65 feet, 4 inches: a world record. There won't be anyone reading these lines who can tell you what professional football player completed the most passes, which one had the most interceptions, which one ran the farthest on a kickoff return or a punt return, or even which one made the most touchdowns in one game. Who won the Super Bowl in 1970? How about 1974? Who on earth, with one ounce of sense, would care?

Not one item I have mentioned in the last two paragraphs has []{#6z0vNAIsTD_RezYjRLYFFA172.xhtml_page_42}any importance to any human being on the face of this earth, and has no bearing on anything that will ever happen in the lifetime of 6,000,000,000 of its inhabitants. The whole rack of news media trivia is of no more significance than the world record set between July 29 and August 8 of 1986, by John D. Joyce of Bryan, Texas. He swung in a hammock for 240 consecutive hours. You are being swamped and drowned in a tidal wave of erratum and trivia that would inundate five continents. Any yearly [Almanac ]{.class_1790}will show you what has happened to America since World War I. There (take the one of 1982 as fairly representative), you will find a two‑page listing of famous past Americans, a page and a half of black Communists and blacks trained by whites, three pages of famous political leaders, one page for military leaders, three pages of famous writers, two pages for artists, and two pages of philosophers and educators. The noted scientists only cover 1½ pages; the composers, industrialists, historians, and economists are all encompassed in five pages. Then there follows [thirteen pages ]{.class_1790}of ENTERTAINERS.

[That]{.class_1790} is the news media approach.

1:12 I the Preacher was king over Israel in Jerusalem.

A little boy in grade school was told that the world was round. He denied it, saying that his daddy had taught him differently. "Well," said his teacher, "It has been proved that the world is not flat; it is round." The boy shook his head and said firmly, "My daddy said it was CROOKED."

After a scathing address against the IRS, ACLU, NEA, NAACP, and CFR, plus a blistering attack on the Illuminati, the Bilderbergers, both political parties, and the Federal Reserve System, a pastor concluded his message as follows: "This world is in a [mess ]{.class_1790}and is going to stay in a [mess." ]{.class_1790}After this service, I heard the church janitor talking with him. The janitor said, "Pastor, you are wrong. This world is [not ]{.class_1790}in a mess. I've been cleaning up messes all my life, but nobody can clean this world up, and nobody can straighten it out!"

"That which is crooked cannot be made straight."

In 1,000 B.C., a Hebrew king recorded two absolutes that are relative to nothing. They are universal truths that are as well established (and settled) as sun "rise" and sun "set."

1:16 I communed with mine own heart, saying, Lo, I am come to great estate, and have gotten more wisdom than all they that have been before me in Jerusalem: yea, my heart had great experience of wisdom and knowledge.

17 And I gave my heart to know wisdom, and to know madness and folly: I perceived that this also is vexation of spirit.

18 For in much wisdom is much grief: and he that increaseth knowledge increaseth sorrow.

Here we find one of the "switches" mentioned in the Introduction (p. xxviii). This section might be separated from the first section by as much as five years. We are not dealing with a continuous "thought flow" in [Ecclesiastes. ]{.class_1790}Solomon has jotted down the thoughts that match the worldly way of thinking things through; he is now collating them. Ah enjoys talkin' wid a smart man, and den again, ah enjoys hearin' a smart man talk!") The verse (vs. 16) is true, according to 1 Kings 3:13. Our unknown, post‑exilic "Koheleth" (see the Introduction) could no more claim either verse than he could claim Goliath's sword. Verse 16 is a philosophy called Empiricism. You experiment, so you learn through actual experience. Those before him, in Jerusalem (see 2:9), included Adonizedec, Melchisedec, and David, plus the Jebusites of 2 Samuel 5:6. Having fulfilled the desire expressed in verse 13 (see vs. 17), he came to the same conclusion he had stated in verses 2 and 14. (Note the long interval of time that took place between []{#6z0vNAIsTD_RezYjRLYFFA172.xhtml_page_47}verses 13 and 17.) He had been at work on the problem. After years of study and giving himself up to the project, he concluded that if you increase wisdom you will find ["much grief."]{.class_1791} If[ ]{.class_1790}you increase knowledge (see Dan. 12:4), you will increase sorrow.

The [NASV ]{.class_1790}immediately misreads the Hebrew and the English and mistranslates ["sorrow" ]{.class_1791}as "PAIN." One of them is ["pure, then peaceable," ]{.class_1791}while the other one [is "earthly, sensual, devilish." ]{.class_1791}How did Jamieson miss the New Testament comment on Solomon's wisdom? Pure, peaceable wisdom is not distressing, nor does it bring grief. The wisdom of Ecclesiastes 1:18 is the wisdom of Ecclesiastes 1:13, 15, and 16. (See the definitions given to wisdom, knowledge, and understanding in [The Bible Believer's Commentary on Proverbs,]{.class_1790} Prov. 1, 1982.)

# Chapter 2 {.heading_69}

2:1 I said in mine heart, Go to now, I will prove thee with mirth, therefore enjoy pleasure: and, behold, this also is vanity.

2 I said of laughter, It is mad: and of mirth, What doeth it?

3 I sought in mine heart to give myself unto wine, yet acquainting mine heart with wisdom; and to lay hold on folly, till I might see what was that good for the sons of men, which they should do under the heaven all the days of their life.

Note another gap, following the one registered in 1:16. This will be something about which he thought, after becoming engulfed for a long time in ["sorrow" ]{.class_1791}and ["grief"]{.class_1791} (see 1:18). He will now try "Hedonism" (the [Playboy, Penthouse ]{.class_1790}magazine philosophy): he will ["enjoy pleasure." ]{.class_1791}He is going to immerse himself in four things in which "modern man" likes to immerse himself (2 Tim. 3:1--2).

1\. Mirth 2. Pleasure 3. Laughter 4. Folly

The ["mirth" ]{.class_1791}is "simchah," as found in Genesis 31:27 and Nehemiah 8:12. It means "to celebrate" ("Cheers! Pro‑sit. Gemutlekeit, Skoal! Drink her down. Chug‑a-lug. Down the hatch," etc.). The ["pleasure" ]{.class_1791}would include massages, steam baths, fornication, adultery, highs on drugs, good food, expensive wines, sports, betting, listening to good music, hunting, fishing, and, in some cases, sex perversion, sadism, and masochism ["The depths of Satan" ]{.class_1791}(Rev. 2:24) have to do with enjoying watching someone being tortured (Ezek. 32:31 describes this as Satan's only "comfort" in Hell).

["Laughter" ]{.class_1791}is obvious. He would load up on "platters" (or cassettes or CDs) by Jack Benny, Burns and Allen, Amos and Andy, Bob Newhart, Dave Gardner, Jonathan Winters, Eddy Murphy, Redd Foxx, Allan King, Shelley Berman, and Anna Russell; then he would watch "videos" of Red Skelton, the Marx Brothers, the Three Stooges, Laurel and Hardy, Abbott and Costello, Road Runner, Bugs []{#6z0vNAIsTD_RezYjRLYFFA310.xhtml_page_52}Bunny, Popeye, Our Gang, the Keystone Cops, I Love Lucy, and Donald Duck. Then he would obtain the cartoon books on [Krazy Kat, Pogo, Calvin and Hobbes, the Wizard of Id, Lil' Abner, Tumbleweeds, Hagar the Horrible, Dennis the Menace, Peanuts, Cracked Magazine, Mad Magazine, Garfield, Ziggy, ]{.class_1790}and ["Herman."]{.class_1790}

What would this come to, eventually? ["The crackling of thorns under a pot" ]{.class_1791}(Ecc. 7:6).

America has been laughing its way to hell since the days of Harold Lloyd and Fatty Arbuckle. When you consider it, from a Biblical standpoint, the only human being on this earth who would have any real right to laugh would be a saved sinner or a [child. ]{.class_1790}Any unsaved man could have a stroke (or a "clot"), right in the middle of a hearty laugh, and die of a heart attack. Or he might get a bullet in the belly, right in the middle of a belly laugh, and wake up in hell. Either way, the line separating an unsaved man from an eternity in a lake of fire is as thin as a piece of tissue paper.

But laughter is part and parcel of human nature. This explains why professional comedians (Bill Cosby, for example) are some of the highest paid people in the world. Bob Hope and Bing Crosby never had to worry about "time payments" on anything. The same man who wrote ["sorrow is better than laughter" ]{.class_1791}(Ecc. 7:3) wrote ["A merry heart doeth good like a medicine" ]{.class_1791}(Prov. 17:22); but even in that treatise, he penned Proverbs 15:13 and 14:13, which see.

Why is laughter ["mad"]{.class_1791}?

1\. It often ends in a catastrophe (see Psa. 2 and 2 Chron. 30:10). "He who laughs last (Psa. 2:4) laughs best."

2\. It solves nothing; it is a temporary "steam valve." (Infantrymen understand this perfectly. As far back as 1917, the German "Stoss" trooper Paul Baumer says, "We joke to keep from going MAD."

3\. Sometimes it is [uncontrollable ]{.class_1790}(James 3:8), and betrays the moral character of the "dirty minded."

4\. As a response, it often edifies no one, and at the wrong time it can [infuriate ]{.class_1790}someone to the point of killing.

5\. Sometimes it is symptomatic of [hysteria]{.class_1790} or a complete loss of mind. The prisoners that Ghengis Khan boiled alive in huge kettles often [laughed]{.class_1790} hysterically[ ]{.class_1790}after they had been [screaming ]{.class_1790}[]{#6z0vNAIsTD_RezYjRLYFFA310.xhtml_page_53}for thirty minutes. The same thing happened to "escapees" from German concentration camps, who were brought back to camp. They were incarcerated in wooden boxes 3 feet by 2 feet by 4 feet, which had a wire screen on the front of it. The top and bottom of the box exhibited the points of eight penny nails driven through from the outside; about ten rows of twenty nails each. Prisoners captured by the Gestapo often died laughing hysterically as ten inch needles were inserted up their rectums into their intestines. In Vietnam, it happened when boys were eaten alive by ants or rats, through a period of two or three days. ["For in much wisdom is much grief." ]{.class_1791}The more you know about what actually goes on down here (["under the sun"]{.class_1791}), the more sorrowful you become.

Nonetheless, laughter (as crying) is part of your Adamic inheritance. Sam Jones would double them up with laughter before knocking them flat on the floor. (More accurately, flat on their face at a "moumer's bench.") Billy Sunday used a sanctified humor which drove the straightlaced, pious, ecclesiastical dignitaries of his day "up the wall." Spurgeon's sermons are laced with gentle sarcasms and bits of buffoonery. Charlie used to say to his ministerial students: "When you preach about heaven, smile and let your face light up. Let your eyes twinkle. When you preach about Hell, your [natural expression ]{.class_1790}will do."

My own besetting sin in regards to ["jesting" ]{.class_1791}(Eph. 5:4; the words "laugh" and "laughter" don't appear one time in thirteen Pauline epistles) is musical parodies. To me, PDQ Bach and Spike Jones are much funnier than Laurel and Hardy or Johnny Carson. No sit‑com or slap stick comedy team has ever affected me like one old record recorded back around 1958 somewhere, titled "Music for Non‑Thinkers." This was produced in Iowa by five German‑Americans who called themselves ["The Guttenheimer Band." I ]{.class_1790}have listened to it as many times as ten times a year, for over thirty years. I still nearly have a heart attack when I hear it. The work is by five very talented professionals who are engaged in deliberate "hamming" of [Liszt's Hungarian]{.class_1790} (no. 2), [The Star Spangled Banner, Weber's Invitation to the Dance,]{.class_1790} and some German folk tunes. On several occasions, I have found myself flat on []{#6z0vNAIsTD_RezYjRLYFFA310.xhtml_page_54}the floor kicking at chairs. (Unfortunately, I have gone through almost the same "aesthetic experience" when listening to some of the Fairies and Twinkies from BJU and PCC performing Christian music: and I mean "performing." "Ministering" was out of the question.)

On Solomon's road to ["pleasure," ]{.class_1791}he naturally ran into the booze (vs. 3). He was "given to it" (vs. 3) like a junkie given to "fixes." He got hooked. (See the extensive comments on Prov. 20:1 and 23:20, in that Commentary.) Unlike the Bible drunkards who got carried away with the excess (Eph. 5:18)---Noah, Lot, Benhadad, Belshazzar, et al.---Solomon, by the grace of God, was able to maintain a cool objectivity toward his own "boozing." He made notes on it. In verse 9, you are told that he survived. Occasionally a man does, but it is the [exception]{.class_1790}, not the rule, as anyone knows who has had any experience working with alcoholics; especially those of the rescue mission variety.

Verse 3 is what we call a remark on "Epistemology." In Philosophy, this means, "how do we obtain knowledge?"; "what are the means by which real truth is obtained?". Solomon got his information by giving himself up to it, acquainting himself with it, and laying hold on it. Epistemology deals with what we call "The Criteria for Truth and Error." Some people arrive at what they call "truth" by intuition or guesswork; others take it from a religious authority or go by a "majority" opinion. Many use custom and tradition as final authorities and some go by revelation. False epistemology would include information that comes from ambiguities, figures of speech, abstractions, feelings, propaganda, amphibology, and deliberate perversion. The faculties and staffs of Christian colleges and universities are constantly entrapped in falsehood by honoring "majority opinions" and going by tradition. On the other hand, CBS, NBC, CNN, ABC, National Public Radio, and [Life ]{.class_1790}and [Time ]{.class_1790}magazines are engaged in deliberate perversion of the truth and outright lying. This is done by what they call (coyly) "double speak." The term [itself ]{.class_1790}is "double speak." It is a synonym for outright, bald‑faced lying. You have to be TWO faced ([double]{.class_1790}) to speak with a forked tongue. No major news outlet is occupied with disseminating truth in any form.

If you would like to see what real "double speak" is in the news media, obtain the cassette tapes from our bookstore on "The Federal Jungle," "Sin, Sex, and Satanism," "America's Greatest Fomicating Communist," "The Catholic Pope's Concentration Camps," "The Fourth Estate," "The Whole Story," "The Prostitute Press," "The Real Bigots," and "The Star Spangled Sodomites." This documented evidence totals more than forty-five hours of material.

["Folly" ]{.class_1791}(vs. 3) is connected with dying and going to Hell (Prov. 5:23); it is also connected with ["deceiving, and being deceived" ]{.class_1791}(2 Tim. 3:13), according to Solomon (Prov. 14:8). You can spot it in 1993 among the educated class (predominately), who fulfill Proverbs 15:21, which see. They think that toleration of filth and depravity is "progress." In trying to find "the good" in all of this (vs. 3), Solomon describes the only real good in verse 24, after an excursion that runs twenty‑one verses; and this "good" has to be qualified by noting that the only man who gets any good out of it is a man who IS good (vs. 26). Note the anti‑Pauline, anti‑New Testament flavor of the entire passage. Note, especially, how the word ["sinner" ]{.class_1791}is used (vs. 26). This is the way the orthodox rabbis of Christ's day used it (John 9:16; Luke 7:37). Paul uses it this way one time in Galatians 2:15.

2:4 I made me great works; I builded me houses; I planted me vineyards:

5 I made me gardens and orchards, and I planted trees in them of all kind of fruits:

6 I made me pools of water, to water therewith the wood that bringeth forth trees:

7 I got me servants and maidens, and had servants born in my house; also I had great possessions of great and small cattle above all that were in Jerusalem before me:

8 I gathered me also silver and gold, and the peculiar []{#6z0vNAIsTD_RezYjRLYFFA310.xhtml_page_56}treasure of kings and of the provinces: I gat me men singers and women singers, and the delights of the sons of men, as musical instruments, and that of all sorts.

9 So I was great, and increased more than all that were before me in Jerusalem: also my wisdom remained with me.

This experiment with pleasure and mirth is "in depth." It doesn't leave a stone unturned. Observe that many pleasures are legal and proper; they are "legit." It is not a sin to plant trees, grow gardens, build aqueducts, plant orchards, or listen to good music. But this is the same man who said ["The plowing of the wicked is sin." ]{.class_1791}Plowing is "legit," but if it comes ahead of ["seek ye first the kingdom of God, and his righteousness," ]{.class_1791}it will damn you just as quickly as indulgence in any forbidden pleasure. It is rejection of Jesus Christ that finishes a sinner off (John 16:9), so whatever keeps you from HIM will damn you permanently.

Most of the passage is self‑explanatory. The ["wood" ]{.class_1791}of verse 6 might be called "woods" now. I asked Jack Wood (from Houston, Texas) one time, "Is your name Wood or Woods?" He replied, "Just one tree." (First Samuel 14:25 and 14:26 define the usage in the Old Testament.) The three innocent-looking ["pools" ]{.class_1791}turn out to be aqueducts (or swimming pools) about 582 feet by 107 feet and nearly 50 feet deep. The gardens with their fruit trees are "parks" ("orchards"---paradasim), a sort of worldly Eden ("paradise"). Verse 7 again points out that no silly, anonymous, little "Qoheleth" wrote the book, after the captivity. If he did, he had to be a king who had more cattle than David or Melchizedek. Solomon gathers silver and gold like dust (vs. 8), and his revenues come from what is now Armenia, Greece, Iraq, Iran, Arabia, Syria, Saudi Arabia, Egypt, India, Corsica, Crete, Cyprus, Sicily, and probably Morocco, Spain, and the Gold Coast. ["Gat"]{.class_1791} (vs. 8) is an abbreviated form for "GAThered." It means he collected men and women singers and musical instruments. Solomon collected [musical instruments.]{.class_1790} The smallest violin in the world is five and one‑half inches high. The largest guitar is eight feet, ten inches and weighs eighty pounds. The largest brass instrument, extant, is a seven and a half‑foot tuba, []{#6z0vNAIsTD_RezYjRLYFFA310.xhtml_page_57}containing thirty‑nine feet of tubing.

The highest paid classical musician, up till 1970, was the Polish piano player [Ignace Jan Paderewski ]{.class_1790}(1860--1941), who got \$33,000 for a single night's performance. He took in about \$5,000,000 in a lifetime, before 1940. (This is a modern equivalent of about \$20,000,000.) Modern demand for music is not for clean‑cut classical musicians; it is for sin‑laden, belly‑ shaking, over-sexed dopeheads. The demand is for raw sex; hence, the incomes of people like Elvis Presley, John Lennon, Madonna, or Michael Jackson would make Paderewski look like a pauper. Prince, Mick Jagger, and the Beatles (and Rolling Stones) perform before howling mobs of sex‑crazy teenagers and go the limit to do (or sing) [anything]{.class_1790} in order to make a buck, and they make the bucks. "Two Live Crew" is just one more group of greedy, covetous‑mad scumbags who would do [anything ]{.class_1790}for a buck. They are musical prostitutes.

Six hundred thousand attended the rock concert at Watkins Glen, N.Y. (July 28, 1973), causing one of the worst traffic jams in history. When it ended, one was dead, 150 hospitalized, and drugs were found all over the area.

Michael Jackson---an indefinite neuter, who achieved "integration" by a face‑lift---had a global sales record of 40,000,000 copies (1988) of a child's recording which was made with [sound effects.]{.class_1790} The [title ]{.class_1790}of the record, with the record jacket, sold it. It was called "Thriller" and didn't have one musical "thrill" on it from start to finish. This half‑white, half‑black, half‑male, half‑female, half-religious, half-atheist NEUTER was given eight Grammy Awards, in 1984, for an all time record of MEDIOCRE CRUD. There wasn't one bar of original music on "Thriller." With a scary cover picture for adolescents, it sold 40,000,000 copies. No one requested ONE page of sheet music for ONE bar of music on the record. No musician was interested in learning it or playing it.

By contrast, the greatest demand for sheet music---that is, a copy of some music that you can learn to play in your own home---is for the following pieces: "The Blue Danube," "Listen to the Mockingbird," "Let Me Call You Sweetheart," and "Till We Meet Again." Not one "disk" recorded by Elvis Presley, the Beatles, Prince, []{#6z0vNAIsTD_RezYjRLYFFA310.xhtml_page_58}Boy George, Hank Williams, Michael Jackson, Bruce Springsteen, Stevie Wonder, the Motley Crew, the Twisted Sisters, Elton John, Two Live Crew, Madonna, the Rolling Stones, or Jefferson Airplane was ever demanded as [sheet music ]{.class_1790}in enough bulk to fill one station wagon. In forty years of Rock music---with over two hundred musical groups recording day and night---no one could produce one permanent song that anyone wanted to learn. "Love Me Tender" didn't last twenty years. "Stardust" and "Begin the Beguine" made it for fifty.

The most sung song on earth is not anything that any American pop group has recorded in the last sixty years. It is "Happy Birthday to You," with "For He's a Jolly Good Fellow" as a runner‑up ([Guiness Book of Records]{.class_1790}).

Neither Michael Jackson nor Elvis Presley touched the hem of the "King's" garment. Solomon was a collector (see Prov. 30:1 and comments). He not only collected works of art (vs. 8) but ["possessions of great and small cattle" ]{.class_1791}(vs. 7). He would have picked up that Holstein that was sold (July 13, 1985) for \$1,300,000, the way you would pick up a sack of cornmeal at the Piggly‑Wiggly. The pig that cost \$6,000 (March 5, 1985) wouldn't have put a dent in his checking account, and the draft horse that brought \$47,000 on October 16, 1916 (a Belgian stallion) wouldn't have made a hole in Solomon's billfold.

There is a chicken ranch in Croton, Ohio, where someone keeps 4,800,000 layin' hens. There is a turkey farm in Norfolk, England, []{#6z0vNAIsTD_RezYjRLYFFA310.xhtml_page_59}where 8,500,000 turkeys gobble all over the place; and there is a sheep station in South Australia that grazes sixty to seventy thousand sheep, seventy thousand cattle, and 54,000 kangaroos. It is 4,084 square miles in size. That herd of cattle would not take care of one day's sacrifice that Solomon offered to the Lord (see 1 Kings 8:63). You see, modern man is not in the running when it comes to Ecclesiastes 2:7--8; not even with a pig pen in Yugoslavia (Sljeme) that processes 3,000,000 pigs a year. ["Peculiar treasures" ]{.class_1791}would have included items that today are worth millions of dollars. A German guitar (called the "chittara battente") was sold for \$25,000; it was built in 1634.
