Solomon was a "swinger." His real estate holdings would equal the combined land grabs of Ted Turner, Oral Roberts, Robert Tilton, Jimmy Swaggart, Jimmy Bakker, and the Grand Mufti of Arabia; and he didn't have to report income, outgo, collateral, escrow, expenses, insurance, or investments. No one could audit him. In addition to [that, ]{.class_1790}there is no record of him being sick one day in his life. In addition to [that, ]{.class_1790}he had access to blonds, brunettes, and redheads (and every shade in between), from the ages of sixteen to sixty; and he could get drunk anytime he felt like it without being arrested on a DWI or for disorderly conduct. Further, he was the supreme court judge of the Supreme Court of his day. No newspaper could investigate him, no detective could bug his phone, and no "narc" from the DEA could put a surveillance on him. Solomon was so far ahead of Paul Castellano, Carlos Marcello, Salvatore Leggio, John Gotti, Joe Bonnana, Tony Accardo, and Tommy Buscetta (Mafia "Godfathers") they couldn't keep up with him in a souped‑up Mercedes.

By now, the moral lesson should be obvious. There hasn't been one man on earth, in the nineteenth or twentieth century (on any continent in the world), who knew more about worldly living than the wisest man who ever lived. Once this truth is grasped, the modern American man will abandon his sand rope; for it means that all the advice given by Einstein, Planck, William Glasser, Sarte, Henry James, Bertrand Russell, John Dewey, Discovery Channel, Hollywood, the NEA, NAACP, UN, ACLU, plus the Supreme Court, the news media, and the "Harvard Five Foot Shelf of Classics" is the counsel of AMATEURS. They are [guessing. ]{.class_1790}Solomon is the man who is qualified to pass judgment on their opinions where they deal with how to enjoy life.

2:10 And whatsoever mine eyes desired I kept not from them, I withheld not my heart from any joy; for my heart rejoiced in all my labour: and this was my portion of all my labour.

11 Then I looked on all the works that my hands had wrought, and on the labour that I had laboured to do: and, behold, all was vanity and vexation of spirit, and there was no profit under the sun.

Verse 10 shows the extent of Solomon's empirical, logical, positivic phenomenalism. He didn't hold a slack rein anywhere; he "put the pedal to the metal." He floor‑boarded it; he went "the whole nine yards," etc. ["Whatsoever mine eyes desired I kept not from them." ]{.class_1791}If he wanted a double‑frosted, nut‑sprinkled, chocolate-malted, double‑dipped, ice cream sundae, he ate it. Diet be d---. [Cornelius Vanderbilt ]{.class_1790}(who left \$2,800,000 to his ten‑year‑old daughter) said, "I would give half of what I am worth to be able to eat just one meal like THAT!" (He said this to his male secretary while the two of them were watching a young collegian consuming a porterhouse steak, baked potatoes, creamed mushrooms, hot rolls and butter, and a German Chocolate cake. Vandy was munching on some "Melba" toast and eating his salad without "dressing.")

If Solomon saw a beautiful, young girl, he took her. If he liked the looks of a five bedroom, three bathroom, split-level, ranch style house, he bought the guy out. If he admired an original, hand‑tooled Porsche or Mercedes Benz, he wrote the guy out a check for \$500,000 and drove it off the lot. If he admired a tract of land worth \$500,000 an acre, he bought four acres and paid cash for it. ["Whatsoever my eyes desired\...I withheld not my heart from any joy."]{.class_1791}

No restrictions, no limitations, no rules or regulations, and no restraints. Solomon did exactly as he pleased for more than forty years. Lucky Luciano, Al Capone, Dutch Schultz, Salvatore Maranzano, Giuseppe Masseria, Salvatore Leggio, Frank Costello, Joe Adonis, Raymon Patriarca, and Sam Traficante (Mafia bosses) "never had it so good." They never touched the hem of Solomon's robes, when it came to doing as you d--- pleased for a lifetime. No one got a "contract" on Solomon; no one could make a "hit" on him ("whacked" is the expression, or "clipped"). No one could arrest him or try him, and he had the power to whack anyone he wanted to, []{#6z0vNAIsTD_RezYjRLYFFA310.xhtml_page_62}anytime he wanted to do it: see 1 Kings 2--4. The greatest authority on pleasure, luxury, and sin died more than 1,000 years before Constantine was an emperor. He left us a testament, where he testifies of "that whereof he knew." The reason why the intellectual elite waste their time with Huxley, Planck, Marx, Freud, Einstein, Hawkin, Driesch, Bateson, DeVries, Kraeplin, Froom, Tillich, Von Linne, Moller, Buddha, Feurbach, Hegel, Darwin, Schopenhauer, Hoyle, Plato, Adler, and Nietzsche is their emotional instability; they don't dare to think about God holding them accountable for their sins. Their motive for their scientific researches can be scientifically defined in two words: [EMOTIONAL PANIC.]{.class_1790}

Now, suddenly, right in the middle of rejoicing in his mirth, folly, pleasure, and laughter (vss. 1--3), a fit of depression comes on the playboy, and he says, ["All was vanity and vexation of spirit, and there was no profit \...."              ]{.class_1791}He had just said ["My heart rejoiced in all my labour" ]{.class_1791}(vs. 10), but as surely as Ecclesiastes was not "written at a sittin'," verse 11 takes us forward some years (or at least months) to a time where Solomon is sitting down and reviewing his Hedonistic explorations. The depression, then, does not come in the midst of rejoicing (see above), but in objective retrospect---"the morning after."

Months after finishing his existential tour of pleasure, laughter, mirth, and folly, Solomon comes to the conclusion that he is just another lunkhead who never got "unlunked." He has a hangover. Verse 11 is clear; the great works of verses 4--9 come under the heading of Proverbs 5:11, which Solomon also wrote. What are you going to do with three water tanks fifty feet deep? What would you do in Vanderbilt's mansion (N.C.)? He had seventeen bedrooms; would you sleep thirty minutes in each bed, from 10[pm]{.class_1797} till 6:30[am]{.class_1797}? Do you know what you would do? Why, all you could do would be what Arlin Horton, Bob Jones III, and Nebuchadnezzar could do: survey your vast kingdom and, while talking piously about "giving God the glory and the thanks," say in your heart: ["is not this great\...that I have built for the house of the kingdom by the might of my power, and for the honour of my majesty?" ]{.class_1791}(Dan. 4:30).

Of course you wouldn't say THAT out loud. You would have to say "God has been so good to us!" or "My, how God has blessed us," []{#6z0vNAIsTD_RezYjRLYFFA310.xhtml_page_63}etc. Something "religious" has to be said to cover up the land grabs, the subverting of city officials, the compromises with Bible versions, the money deals, the legal trickery, the waste of money taken from missionaries, the censoring of literature that would expose the rottenness of your kingdom, and the attacks made on Christians in private correspondence that never got published. Ah, yes! There is a great deal more to twentieth-century Christian "Fundamentalism" than the educators would have you believe. "Covetousness," as a disease (Ecc. 1:8), is not cured by buying up a square mile of land, fifty houses, and running families off their property while trying to seize control of local churches. A Christian educator's greed for money and land cannot be satisfied by taking money that should have gone to missionaries, and spending it on tiled bathrooms, water tanks, power plants, underground wiring, motels, landscaping, apartments, chimes, and sports arenas, while paying off high‑priced lawyers. ["The love of money is the root of all evil." ]{.class_1791}(See comments on that verse in [The Bible Believer's Commentary on the Pastoral Epistles,]{.class_1790} 1991).

When Solomon got through "swinging," he found out that all he could do was LOOK at what he had done or think about it.

"Then I looked on all the works that my hands had wrought."

His belly showed how well he had satisfied his appetite. His clothing and jewelry showed how much loot he had confiscated. His bank account showed how much he had "laid back" (Luke 12) for many years to come, and his glamorous harem showed how insatiable his lust had been. And there it was! Now what?

Nothing; [ahead of him is death]{.class_1790} (vss. 12--19).

What he had labored to build will be someone else's property.

He will leave his wives and concubines for some other man to cohabit with; he will leave his gold and silver for some other man to spend; he will leave his orchards and gardens; he will leave his swimming pools and vineyards; and he will have to put up his CD's (and videos) and let someone put him to bed with a shovel.

"How much did he leave at his death?"

"He left it all."

Ditto the Rockefellers, Kennedys, Bourbons, Hapsburgs, []{#6z0vNAIsTD_RezYjRLYFFA310.xhtml_page_64}Romanoffs, Carolingians, Tudors, Hohenzollerns, and the Bushes, Reagans, Hugheses, and the heads of AT&T, GMAC, Wal‑Mart, Penny's, Denny's, Howard Johnson, Holiday Inn, Whataburger, McDonald's, Coca‑Cola, Kentucky Fried Chicken, Pizza Hut, Taco Bell, Church's Fried Chicken, Wannamakers, Woolworth's, Kresge, IBM, Exxon, and Pelletier's.

You can't take it with you. ["We brought nothing into this world, and it is certain we can carry nothing out" ]{.class_1791}(1 Tim. 6:7).

2:12 And I turned myself to behold wisdom, and madness, and folly: for what can the man do that cometh after the king? even that which hath been already done.

13 Then I saw that wisdom excelleth folly, as far as light excelleth darkness.

14 The wise man's eyes are in his head; but the fool walketh in darkness: and I myself perceived also that one event happeneth to them all.

15 Then said I in my heart, As it happeneth to the fool, so it happeneth even to me; and why was I then more wise? Then I said in my heart, that this also is vanity.

16 For there is no remembrance of the wise more than of the fool for ever; seeing that which now is in the days to come shall all be forgotten. And how dieth the wise man? as the fool.

17 Therefore I hated life; because the work that is wrought under the sun is grievous unto me: for all is vanity and vexation of spirit.

A space has elapsed (vs. 12). He is now going back and doing a "retake" to see if wisdom can be related to folly and madness. Laughter was ["mad"]{.class_1791} (vs. 2), so mirth and folly accompanied it; but what about ["wisdom"]{.class_1791}? That was his original game plan (1:13, 16).

The man who will be king after him---it turns out to be Rehoboam---can only do what he has done, at the maximum. He will never be able to "out do" him. Surely enough, Rehoboam [doesn't. ]{.class_1790}Rehoboam cannot even keep the gold his daddy left him (1 Kings 10:17 and []{#6z0vNAIsTD_RezYjRLYFFA310.xhtml_page_65}14:26). Solomon returns to this theme down in verses 18 and 19, but not right away. Right away, he compares wisdom and folly (vs. 13). Even if wisdom increases grief and sorrow, it still ["excelleth folly," ]{.class_1791}because sorrow and grief are capable of producing a sanctified life (7:3). Moral values suddenly raises its unwanted head in the midst of "pleasure, laughter, mirth, and folly"! (This is the same man who wrote Proverbs 1:20--23; 2:2--5; 3:13; 4:5, 7; 5:1; 7:4, and 8:1, 5, 11, 12, 14). The illustration is a man walking who doesn't have any eyes in his head (vs. 14). ["Eyes have they, but they see not" ]{.class_1791}(Psa. 115:5). But the thought has no sooner entered his head than the old, rational, Adamic intellect asserts itself and counters with, "Well, what is the difference between a wise man and a fool when it comes to dying? If one is wiser than the other what difference would that make?" None: ["As it happeneth to the fool, so it happeneth even to me\...how dieth the wise man? as the fool" ]{.class_1791}(vs. 15, 16). Observe the past tense (["so it happeneth"]{.class_1791}), for his death had not yet taken place (see p. xix). Hence, if the [NASV ]{.class_1790}and the others had been right in "I have been king\..." (see p. xix), it would still mean nothing, for Solomon could have "been" king [when he wrote it. ]{.class_1790}A fool will be forgotten after death (vs. 16), but so will a wise man, since ["that which now is in the days to come shall all be forgotten" ]{.class_1791}(cf. 1:11 and comments).

A king once asked a wise man to inscribe some motto on his palace walls that could be applied to every event that might occur in the future. The wise man inscribed five words: "This, too, shall pass away."

["How dieth the wise man?" ]{.class_1791}Just like Jim Jones and Adolph Hitler died. Just like Stalin, Truman Capote, and Andy Warhol died. When Betty Grable and Benny Goodman died, [Death ]{.class_1790}touched them one time in the heart and one time in the lungs, and they "croaked." When Jack Kennedy and Bozo the Clown died, [Death ]{.class_1790}stopped their breathing and their heart beat, and they "went west." Bloody Mary and Mae West died just like FDR and Stalin died: one touch in the lungs, one on the heart, and "that's all she wrote." They cashed in their chips. This is the sense of Ecclesiastes 3:19, which see. When Bundy took the "hot squat," Old Sparky (the electric chair) made him "ride the lightning." Then they buried his corpse like they buried the []{#6z0vNAIsTD_RezYjRLYFFA310.xhtml_page_66}corpses of Generals George Patton, Erwin Rommel, and John Pershing. They had to bury Albert Einstein and Albert Schweitzer just like they buried Judas Iscariot or Heinrich Himmler. They dug a hole in the ground, lowered them into it, and then covered them up. Then they packed dirt on top of them.

["Therefore I hated life" ]{.class_1791}(vs. 17), because he had worked like a dog to accomplish something he could not keep, something he could not take with him when he left. But note the ominous, recurring theme (["under the sun"]{.class_1791}). Someone's works are going to ["follow them," ]{.class_1791}according to the New Testament (Rev. 14:13 and 1 Tim. 5:24). Man, ["under the sun," ]{.class_1791}is not aware of this. There are works wrought under God's direction, for His glory, that are NOT ["vanity and vexation of spirit." ]{.class_1791}You will meet them on the other side of the grave---not ["under the sun"]{.class_1791}---and[ ]{.class_1791}they will not be accredited to anyone's account that survives you.

In this respect, the Bible‑believing, soul‑winning preacher has an advantage over every other calling or profession in this life, including the professions of popes, doctors, lawyers, archbishops, judges, philanthropists, priests, and scientists. The good deeds of a scientist or philanthropist may benefit two or three generations, provided the money isn't embezzled by the government and provided the generations have enough money to afford the medical luxuries of scientific advancement. (Three quarters of the earth's population cannot afford anesthesias, wonder drugs, or pain killers.) The good deeds of a lawyer or doctor to a family (or to an individual) may be in evidence in grandchildren, but when it comes to [eternity, ]{.class_1790}these deeds amount to nothing. Not so with the labors of George Whitefield, Ignatius, John Wesley, Paul, Martin Luther, B. B. Crimm, John Rice, Jack Hyles, Bob Jones Sr., Dwight Moody, or J. Frank Norris. God is still using Oliver Green and Dr. M. R. DeHaan, though both of them cashed in (see above) more than fifteen years ago.

If you killed me tonight---and believe me, 5,000 faculty members of Christian schools are praying for that to happen---I would appear on TV the following week, before more than 7,000,000 viewers. I have great‑great‑great spiritual "grandsons" in the ministry; these are soul‑winning preachers who were led to Christ by the converts of men who were led to Christ by men that I had led to Christ. []{#6z0vNAIsTD_RezYjRLYFFA310.xhtml_page_67}Somewhere on this earth, overseas, are thirty‑four young men who, between them, are leading better than one soul to Christ, per day. These souls live forever (1 John 5:11, 20). You can take them home to glory with you, in violation of ["we brought nothing into this world, and it is certain we can carry nothing out." ]{.class_1791}You can take the souls of men "hence" and meet them "above the sun." No doctor, lawyer, priest, pope, judge, or educator is capable of doing the permanent good that a soul‑winning preacher can do. In my past, I have found cases where a mother got saved under my ministry and took up chalk talk work. She then led her daughter to the Lord, using one of her chalk talks, and her daughter (who is now a mother herself) is leading people right now with chalk talks. The man who led me to Christ (Hugh Pyle) has great‑great grandchildren in the ministry because he led me to Christ; I led Cecil Ford to Christ (a Catholic infantryman from "Nam"); Cecil led Barney Iha to Christ (a Japanese medic in "Nam"); and Barney has led more than two hundred children to Christ, working as a bus driver for Jack Hyles.

2:18 Yea, I hated all my labour which I had taken under the sun: because I should leave it unto the man that shall be after me.

19 And who knoweth whether he shall be a wise man or a fool? yet shall he have rule over all my labour wherein I have laboured, and wherein I have shewed myself wise under the sun. This is also vanity.

20 Therefore I went about to cause my heart to despair of all the labour which I took under the sun.

21 For there is a man whose labour is in wisdom, and in knowledge, and in equity; yet to a man that hath not laboured therein shall he leave it for his portion. This also is vanity and a great evil.

22 For what hath man of all his labour, and of the vexation of his heart, wherein he hath laboured under the sun?

23 For all his days are sorrows, and his travail grief; yea, his heart taketh not rest in the night. This is also vanity.

Psalm 39:6 matches verse 18 perfectly. The son takes over when the father dies. 2:24 There is nothing better for a man, than that he should eat and drink, and that he should make his soul enjoy good in his labour. This also I saw, that it was from the hand of God.

25 For who can eat, or who else can hasten hereunto, more than I?

26 For God giveth to a man that is good in his sight wisdom, and knowledge, and joy: but to the sinner he giveth travail, to gather and to heap up, that he may give to him that is good before God. This also is vanity and vexation of spirit.

After digesting his thoughts on the vanities, sorrows, and griefs of life, Solomon turns to Utilitarianism and Egotism. He denies what he had just said about all of man's days being sorrowful and full of travail and grief (vss. 22--23), and now says that some men have joy and "enjoy the good" of their labors (vs. 24). To do this, however, he had to bring ["God"]{.class_1791} in. ["This also I saw, that it was from the hand of God" ]{.class_1791}(vs. 24). Still, the reasoning is basically this: the highest good is to eat and drink and enjoy your work, because ["who can eat, or who else can hasten hereunto, more than I?" ]{.class_1791}[Egotism:]{.class_1790} my standard is the best one and, therefore, an absolute for all men. It works for ME ([Pragmatism]{.class_1790}), so it should work for everyone else.

It would mean that all men do [not ]{.class_1790}find grief and travail ["and vexation of spirit" ]{.class_1791}(vs. 26). ["A man that is good," ]{.class_1791}in God's sight, is dealt another hand, according []{#6z0vNAIsTD_RezYjRLYFFA310.xhtml_page_71}to verse 26. When he was sinning (1 Sam. 27:1), he had no real peace or rest (2 Sam. 12--13): all was ["vanity and vexation of spirit" ]{.class_1791}(1 Sam. 30:4--6). He is ["sitting, and clothed, and in his right mind" ]{.class_1791}(Mark 5:15).

# Chapter 3 {.heading_69}

3:1 To every thing there is a season, and a time to every purpose under the heaven:

2 A time to be born, and a time to die; a time to plant, and a time to pluck up that which is planted;

3 A time to kill, and a time to heal; a time to break down, and a time to build up;

4 A time to weep, and a time to laugh; a time to mourn, and a time to dance;

5 A time to cast away stones, and a time to gather stones together; a time to embrace, and a time to refrain from embracing;

6 A time to get, and a time to lose; a time to keep, and a time to cast away;

7 A time to rend, and a time to sew; a time to keep silence, and a time to speak;

8 A time to love, and a time to hate; a time of war, and a time of peace.

This famous passage lists twenty‑eight items which follow the number of revolutions in the moon. The moon was placed ["for signs, and for seasons" ]{.class_1791}(Gen. 1:14). This section is, obviously, a complete departure from the line of thought just recorded (2:24--26). A month or a year (or ten years) might have elapsed since the previous chapter was written. ["The signs of the times" ]{.class_1791}(Matt. 16:3) are to be discerned, although some occupations are to be carried on ["in season, out of season" ]{.class_1791}(2 Tim. 4:2). Some seasons are not revealed (Acts 1:7), while others are "known perfectly" (1 Thess. 5:1). Everything that follows is absolute truth, "relative" to nothing:

1\. ["A time to be born." ]{.class_1791}It is nine months after conception, for a human. Every animal has its own gestation period. Astrological forecasts are set up according to the time of one's birth.

2\. ["And a time to die." ]{.class_1791}Hence, David's words to Solomon (1 Kings 2:2). Jacob says, ["Behold, I die," ]{.class_1791}(Gen. 48:21). Isaac does []{#6z0vNAIsTD_RezYjRLYFFA434.xhtml_page_76}not know the day of his death (Gen. 27:2), and David misses his "time" by about twenty‑five years (1 Sam. 20:3), but the ["time to die" ]{.class_1791}finally gets all of them.

3\. ["A time to plant," ]{.class_1791}so all of the old timers plant according to the "signs." The waxing and waning of the moon effects crops. All of the hillbillies, in the Carolinas, swear by the signs of the Zodiac (Aquarius, Scorpio, Virgo, etc.) when they want to make a good crop. Regardless of your feelings about the matter, some things are certain: you cannot get a good crop of okra if you plant before the ground is warm, and pecan trees don't grow in Manitoba and Saskatchewan. The [wrong ]{.class_1790}time to plant wheat, in Kansas, is in October. The [wrong ]{.class_1790}time to plant potatoes, in Alabama (and Georgia), is in May. There is ["a time to plant," ]{.class_1791}also, in the sense that there is ["a time to plant"]{.class_1791} a nation in a territory (Jer. 18:9; 31:2), and\....

4\. ["A time to pluck up that which is planted." ]{.class_1791}The reference is primarily to [Gentile nations ]{.class_1790}(Jer. 1:10 and 2 Chron. 7:20), but it certainly applied to crops. There is a time to harvest crops. When that time is past, your garden isn't much good. Tomatoes, squash, watermelons, and grapes rot on the vine; okra gets as hard as a corn cob; corn turns brown so that only cattle can eat it; the apples and oranges rot and fall off; and the beans get so hard you can't even cook them.

5\. ["A time to kill." ]{.class_1791}It is time to kill when ordered to do so in warfare (1 Sam. 15; Rom. 13); when paying back a murderer for his contribution to society (Num. 35); when dealing with a crippled horse or a hopelessly sick dog or cat; when dealing with flies, mosquitoes, rats, cockroaches, and rattlesnakes; and (in the Old Testament) when paying off blasphemers (Lev. 24), Sabbath breakers (Num. 15), parent abusers (Exod. 21:15), and [sex perverts ]{.class_1790}(Lev. 18:22, 29).

6\. ["A time to heal." ]{.class_1791}Isaiah 39, for example. Second Kings 5, for example. Sometimes a nation is sick spiritually (Isa. 1:5--6) and needs to be "healed" (see Jer. 14:19). Sometimes a city is "sick" (see Jer. 51:8--9).

7\. ["A time to break down," ]{.class_1791}as in 2 Chronicles 26:6, 36:19, and Matthew 24:2. Old buildings sometimes have to be demolished. The []{#6z0vNAIsTD_RezYjRLYFFA434.xhtml_page_77}sinner's mental strongholds have to be "razed" to the ground. Old cars have to be smashed. There is ["a time to break down." ]{.class_1791}Note! Completely contrary to everything religious in America that is being promoted by 90 percent of its preachers. NEGATIVISM is given an equal place with the positive. In every set (vss. 1--8), the negative completes the statement: ["kill\... weep\... mourn\... lose\... hate\... war." ]{.class_1791}Without a negative pole on your car battery, your car is not going anywhere. A man who cannot [hate]{.class_1790} sin, drunkenness, sex perversion, fraud, extortion, blackmail, pornography, perverted Bible translations, and moral filth is dangerous to his community.

8\. ["A time to build up." ]{.class_1791}This is admirably demonstrated in the books of Ezra and Nehemiah. It will be found again, illustrated in the New Testament, in regards to spiritual growth (Acts 20:32) and in the Body of Christ itself (Eph. 4:12--16).

9\. ["A time to weep," ]{.class_1791}as the women in Bethlehem wept (Matt. 2:18) or as David wept in 2 Samuel 18:33 or as his men wept in 1 Samuel 30:4. There is absolutely nothing wrong with bawling your eyes out (Rom. 12:15 and James 4:9) on some occasions. Although we are not to ["sorrow\...as others which have no hope," ]{.class_1791}(1 Thess. 4:13), our ministerial example wept like a baby many times in his life (Acts 20:19, 31, and 2 Cor. 2:4). A dry‑eyed ministry is a powerless, fruitless ministry. ["Jesus wept."]{.class_1791}

10\. ["A time to laugh." ]{.class_1791}We have commented on this matter already under Ecclesiastes 2:1--2, which see. Scripturally, this will be done at the completion of our salvation (Job 8:20--21) and at the restoration of Israel (Psa. 126:2). ["He that sitteth in the heavens shall laugh." ]{.class_1791}(See comments on Prov. 1:26 in that Commentary.)

11\. ["A time to mourn," ]{.class_1791}not only as Jeremiah does over the destruction of Jerusalem (Lamentations), but as Jesus Christ does over the same matter (Luke 19:41). You can mourn over your backslidden condition, your lack of love for Christ and the Bible, and your lack of love for the souls of men. You can bewail the lost condition of your loved ones and literally hundreds of thousands of people overseas who are locked in spiritual darkness. You can mourn over your dirty, rotten sins (even if Dry Cleaners, like Arthur Watkins, E. C. Moore, Cornelius Stam, Baker, O'Hare, and Bullinger, []{#6z0vNAIsTD_RezYjRLYFFA434.xhtml_page_78}think it wrong to do it).

Notice that weeping and mourning precede laughter and dancing. The sex‑crazy, money‑mad, pagan humanists, in America, all want to laugh and dance; but they don't care to weep and mourn. Christ tried to straighten out these lopsided, positive thinkers in John 16:20, but they never got the message. "Modern man" (especially in the USA) is incapable of receiving spiritual instruction, even from the Lord Jesus Christ.

12\. ["And a time to dance." ]{.class_1791}This Bible dance is "uni‑sex": men with men, women with women (Exod. 15:20 and 2 Sam. 6:14), AND THE BODIES DON'T TOUCH.

Dancing, in the Bible, takes place on such occasions as a sinner getting right with God (Luke 15:25), a people being delivered from Africans (Exod. 15), and glorifying God for restoration of worship (2 Sam. 6). Obviously, these dances have nothing to do with the African "art form" that goes on in Exodus 32. The modern dance (see comments in that Commentary) is an African dance; its main emphasis is on fornication or adultery (called sex by news media double‑speak). The shimmy‑shammy, belly‑dancing, the bumps and the grinds, or "contemporary" dances are Hamitic; the music accompanying them is "Rock" and "Roll," which, as any real expert on contemporary music knows, is a reference to literal, physical fornication (see p. 39 and comments). If you did not know that, you know it now. You are no longer innocent. All modern dances (the Limbo, the Twist, break dancing, the Jitterbug, the Fox Trot, the Mambo, the Samba, the Rhumba, and the Tango) are "dirty dancing." They are African dances.

This phenomenon simply reemphasizes what we have pointed out on at least 500 other occasions (see [The Bible Believer's Conunentary Series)]{.class_1790}:[ ]{.class_1790}that Scripture is usually the last place that a critic of the [Authorized Version ]{.class_1790}looks when he is called upon to expound the Scriptures.)

3:16 And moreover I saw under the sun the place of judgment, that wickedness was there; and the place of righteousness, that iniquity was there.

17 I said in mine heart, God shall judge the righteous and the wicked: for there is a time there for every purpose and for every work.

18 I said in mine heart concerning the estate of the sons of men, that God might manifest them, and that they might see that they themselves are beasts.

19 For that which befalleth the sons of men befalleth beasts; even one thing befalleth them: as the one dieth, so dieth the other; yea, they have all one breath; so that a man hath no preeminence above a beast: for all is vanity.

20 All go unto one place; all are of the dust, and all turn to dust again.

21 Who knoweth the spirit of man that goeth upward, and the spirit of the beast that goeth downward to the earth?

22 Wherefore I perceive that there is nothing better, than that a man should rejoice in his own works; for that is his portion: for who shall bring him to see what shall be after him?

The first reference (vs. 16) is to the Old Testament law courts, where the Levites acted as judges (Deut. 17:8--12). A perfect example of the first clause is the debacle that took place when Mrs. Ahab made a land grab for her husband, Ahab, in 1 Kings 21. False witnesses were present there, exactly as they were present at the midnight kangaroo court where Jesus was tried (Matt. 26).

In the second clause, we have David on the throne, as a man "after God's own heart," who is ["as an angel of God" ]{.class_1791}(2 Sam. 14:17). David was one of the three greatest types of Christ in the Bible. But what is present ["on the throne"]{.class_1791}? Lying, adultery, tempting a man to get drunk, a frame‑up, and a murder. Prophetically speaking, one will find wickedness manifest (by the ton) at the White Throne Judgment (Rev. 20) and the Judgment Seat of Christ (Rom. 14; 2 Cor. 5). This truth matches verse 17. God will judge the ["righteous" ]{.class_1791}[]{#6z0vNAIsTD_RezYjRLYFFA434.xhtml_page_91}(in the Old Testament sense) at the Judgment Seat of Christ. At this ["place of righteousness," ]{.class_1791}will be found the evil deeds of the saint (2 Cor. 5:10). God will judge ["the wicked" ]{.class_1791}at the Great White Throne. Although Solomon omitted "a time for judgment" (see pp. 63--72) in his moon‑list (vss. 1--8), it now shows up (vs. 17): ["As it is appointed unto men once to die, but after this the judgment." ]{.class_1791}The ["time" ]{.class_1791}and ["purpose\...for every work"]{.class_1791} has already been determined by God. Both righteous and wicked were destroyed at the Passover; wicked or righteous, the firstborn did the dying.

Verse 18 was taken so literally by Darwin and other monkey men (Lenin, Stalin, Hitler, Huxley, Einstein, and 90 percent of all the college professors in America and Europe), that he linked the men and the beasts together by heredity and blood line. Such a belief is a pre‑Christian era belief called "Naturalism." It was the staple diet of every deluded, pagan philosopher from 600 B.C. to the time of Christ. Naturalism (if followed through) produces NIHILISM (see vs. 20). You go from nothing to nothing; zip to zero. If there is no point in your being here, there is certainly no point in your departure from here. "Life is in session! Are you present!?"

Solomon's request (["that God might manifest them"]{.class_1791}) is based on physical things, and physical things only: physical life and death (vs. 19). He implies that there is a difference in the destination of spirits, but he does not profess to know, for certain, if this is so (Agnosticism). It is obvious that there has to be a difference, because he has just stated that God will ["judge the righteous and the wicked." ]{.class_1791}When? The judgment to which he points (Ecc. 12:14) is AFTER death.

Still, there is remarkable substance to the request. Men are so much like beasts that, in a dozen respects, there is no difference between them at all. As a matter of fact, the things they have in common are so many and so outstanding that, throughout the Scriptures, God continually refers to men as animals:

1\. They are [dogs ]{.class_1790}(Phil. 3:2; Rev. 22:15).

2\. They are [wolves ]{.class_1790}(Matt. 7:15; Acts 20:29).

3\. They are [serpents ]{.class_1790}(Matt. 10:16; 23:33).

4\. They are [eagles ]{.class_1790}(Isa. 40:31).

5\. They are like [doves ]{.class_1790}[]{#6z0vNAIsTD_RezYjRLYFFA434.xhtml_page_92}(Isa. 59:11).

6\. They are like [bulls ]{.class_1790}(Psa. 22:12).

7\. They are like [dragons ]{.class_1790}(Job 30:29; Micah 1:8).

8\. They are like [sheep ]{.class_1790}and [goats ]{.class_1790}(Matt. 25).

9\. They are [fishes ]{.class_1790}(Matt. 13:47; and 4:19).

10\. They are [oxen ]{.class_1790}(1 Cor. 9:9).

11\. Christ is a [Lion ]{.class_1790}(Rev. 5:5).

12\. But He is a [Lamb]{.class_1790} (Rev. 5:12).

13\. Satan is a [leopard ]{.class_1790}(Rev. 13:1--3) and a lion (1 Pet. 5:8).

14\. Men are like [bears ]{.class_1790}(Isa. 59:11; Prov. 28:15).

15\. Women are likened to [pigs ]{.class_1790}(2 Pet. 2:22; Prov. 11:22).

["Man be born like a wild ass's colt," ]{.class_1791}(Job 11:12).

When one considers these matters from the Biblical standpoint of the new birth, the only thing that separates an unregenerate man from a skunk or a rattlesnake is that his SPIRIT is different (1 Cor. 2:11--12), and he can communicate with WORDS. After that, all differences cease. Every unsaved man is driven and controlled by the three basic animal instincts that are common to all beasts. Everything that man does, from armed combat and murder to praying for widows and giving donations to charity, comes under one of three headings: self‑preservation, self‑propagation, or self-gratification.

In layman's language, Number 1 means "Me first, you next." ["All that a man hath will he give for his life" ]{.class_1791}(Job 2:4).

Number 2 means "Sexual activity of some kind."

Number 3 means "Enjoyment: doing the things you like to do and feeling the feelings you like to feel."

All animals operate by the same three basic principles. They raise families and try to be comfortable; ditto, any unsaved man on earth. If he doesn't raise a family, then he is described in Ecclesiastes 4:8--11. Men and beasts not only have "the same breath" (vs. 19), they have one and the same set of instincts by which they live.

"So that a man hath no preeminence above a beast."

No wonder Darwin and his monkey‑men retinue (98 percent of all the college professors and high school teachers in the United States of America) got confused.

Men and animals drowned in the flood; both were killed at the []{#6z0vNAIsTD_RezYjRLYFFA434.xhtml_page_93}Passover; both perished in the destruction of Israel and Judah. Under the law, you could be defiled by just touching the body of a dead man. A man once said, "The destiny of nations is determined by whether or not they compare themselves with animals or contrast themselves with animals." Herr Hitler demanded "splendid blond BEASTS of prey." He got them. Every federal school in your state teaches that black children are animals who came from animals. This means that the "values clarification" your child (black or white) gets, simply reduces him to a [jungle biped. ]{.class_1790}The product of animals, led by animal instincts, is JUNGLE WARFARE.

["That which befalleth the sons of men." ]{.class_1791}A man and a dog get run over by a car on the Interstate. They both stop breathing. They both stop pumping blood. Both of them are lying still. What do you do? You pick the man up, and pick the dog up, and carry them off the highway. You then dig one hole in the ground for the dog, and one for the man; then you bury the dog and the man, and both of them rot in the dirt. ["All are of the dust, and all turn to dust again" ]{.class_1791}(vs. 20).

What does all of this mean? It means that whoever coined (or borrowed) the phrase, "Man is the measure of all things," was as cracked as the Liberty Bell. The worms get man. You can suck up "the measure of all things" in a vacuum cleaner before his body has been lying in an open field for twelve months. And ["who knoweth the spirit of man that goeth upward"? ]{.class_1791}Not many. Not one evolutionist or humanitarian (or one Agnostic or one Nihilist) on land, sea, or air. The book says, ["then\...the spirit shall return unto God, who gave it" ]{.class_1791}(Ecc. 12:7), but the animal's spirit returns to dust with his physical body. In the New Testament, the Christian's spirit (["that which is born of the Spirit is spirit"]{.class_1791}) and soul are ["absent from the body, and\...present with the Lord" ]{.class_1791}(2 Cor. 5:1--8); but the unsaved man's soul descends into Hell, when his spirit returns ["unto God who gave it."]{.class_1791}

Not knowing either of these New Testament truths for certain, Solomon assumes he is correct in saying as much as he has said. So he assumes he is right in saying that the "summum bonum" (the supreme good) for man (back in vss. 12 and 13) is to "eat, drink, etc." He repeats this in verse 22, and then adds ["for who shall bring him to see what shall be after him?" ]{.class_1791}[]{#6z0vNAIsTD_RezYjRLYFFA434.xhtml_page_94}(see comments under vs. 11). Easy; easy if you have the New Testament. Note: ["He will guide you into all truth\...and he will shew you things to come\...God hath revealed them unto us by his Spirit\...the testimony of Jesus is the spirit of prophecy\...." ]{.class_1791}But here, Solomon is not referring so much to the great prophetic themes of Scripture (as revealed in the New Testament) but rather to questions like "what will go on after you're dead"? (See Ecc. 1:11.) How will your widow and kids make out? Will a depression take place? Will one of your children wind up in prison? Who will get your property? Solomon leaves his own question unanswered, and once again, there is a long gap in the written record between this question and the next discourse.

At this point, we may expect the Alexandrian Cult to go completely to pieces at the seams, again; sure enough, they do. On the other hand, the dead man is through with it once and for all. 4:4 Again, I considered all travail, and every right work, that for this a man is envied of his neighbour. This is also vanity and vexation of spirit.

5 The fool foldeth his hands together, and eateth his own flesh.

6 Better is an handful with quietness, than both the hands full with travail and vexation of spirit.

["Again, I considered" ]{.class_1791}shows further notes which were not considered at the time he wrote verses 1--3. Kennedy, even though "it worked" for Lee. While praising Mahatma Gandhi and King Jr. for starting riots that destroyed 10,000 businesses and caused the deaths of thousands of people, the same humanists would condemn Adolph Hitler for putting into practise "what worked" for him. You see, they have their own flexible moral standards, so what is right can be [wrong]{.class_1790}[]{#6z0vNAIsTD_RezYjRLYFFA557.xhtml_page_99}, and what is wrong can be [right, ]{.class_1790}depending upon what you want to do to promote yourself. A man is envied for doing [right]{.class_1794} (1 John 3:12); that is why Cain murdered his brother. That is why Saul tried to murder David, and that is why the elder brother got so put‑out with his daddy. ["The fool foldeth his hands together, and eateth his own flesh" ]{.class_1791}(vs. 5). See Isaiah 9:20 and Amos 4:6. The hyperbole implies that if you don't work, you won't have anything to eat but your own body. Folded hands don't do any work. (See extensive comments in [The Bible Believer's Commentary on Proverbs: ]{.class_1794}Prov. 12:24, 27; 18:9; 19:24; 21:25, and 22:13.) Notice three kinds of hands. The first man is working with both hands (vs. 6); the second man is not working with either hand (vs. 5); and the third man has one ["handful." ]{.class_1791}[Overwork is ]{.class_1794}condemned, along with underwork. One handful ["with quietness" ]{.class_1791}is better than ["both the hands full with travail and vexation of spirit."]{.class_1791}

Again, all the corrupt Bibles---including the [NKJV]{.class_1790}---have erased all reference to any man's spirit being "vexed" by anything. A man going through grief, travail, and sorrow goes through with no ill effects on his ["spirit," ]{.class_1791}if you go by the flustered lampoons of the Bible called [RVs, ASVs, NASVs, NRSVs, NIVs, NKJVs, ]{.class_1790}and [NEBs.]{.class_1790}

(You know what to do with the "if.")

The same author (Solomon) wrote, ["Better is a dry morsel, and quietness therewith, than an house full of]{.class_1791} [sacrifices with strife." ]{.class_1791}Again, the same author (not some rinky-dink speaker or "Koheleth") said, ["Better is little with the fear of the LORD than great treasure and trouble therewith." ]{.class_1791}The same author (not "do‑jigger Qoheleth") wrote, ["Better is a dinner of herbs ]{.class_1791}\[there is the ["handful"]{.class_1791}\][ where love is, than a stalled ox and hatred therewith."]{.class_1791}

I have been in both types of homes. I have eaten with the rich and the mighty, the wealthy and affluent. I have seen bear skin rugs []{#6z0vNAIsTD_RezYjRLYFFA557.xhtml_page_100}on the floor, art studios on the third floor, roast pheasants on each plate, and waiters called into the dining room by pressing a button on the floor under the table. I have flown in private airplanes to private restaurants (built on private air strips) where the lowest priced lunch was \$12.00---in 1970. I have eaten so many meals in plush Griswald, Mariott, and Holiday Inn motels that I have become an expert on waiters and waitresses. I have "eaten out" on an average of 100 times a year, for the last forty years. I have eaten in the wooden shacks of Alabama, North Carolina, and Mississippi, where some of them had no screen doors or windows; many had no locks on the doors, and often there were holes in the floor where you could see the chickens scratching the dirt under the house. I have eaten in prison mess halls, army mess halls, army field kitchens, and at picnic tables. I have lunched with young Christian couples just starting out on the pilgrimage together, and some of them lived like cliff dwellers in tenement houses that had no windows on the south, east, or west side. I have eaten in tiny, confined apartments in Los Angeles and Philadelphia, where the "front yard" was not even 8 by 15 feet, and there was no back yard at all. I have felt the presence of God in these "ghettos" and shacks like I had one foot in the vestibule of heaven, and (conversely) I have felt the power of Satan like I was falling into the bottomless pit in some of the homes that would sell on the market today for \$400,000. M‑O-N‑E‑Y doesn't spell success, and it doesn't spell spirituality (see 1 Tim. 6:5, 10, which has been altered in the[ ASV, NASV,]{.class_1790} [RSV, NRSV, RV, NIV, ]{.class_1790}and [NKJV]{.class_1790}).

4:7 Then I returned, and I saw vanity under the sun.

8 There is one alone, and there is not a second; yea, he hath neither child nor brother: yet is there no end of all his labour; neither is his eye satisfied with riches; neither saith he, For whom do I labour, and bereave my soul of good? This is also vanity, yea, it is a sore travail.

9 Two are better than one; because they have a good reward for their labour.

10 For if they fall, the one will lift up his fellow: but woe to him that is alone when he falleth; for he hath not another to help him up.

11 Again, if two lie together, then they have heat: but how can one be warm alone?

12 And if one prevail against him, two shall withstand him; and a threefold cord is not quickly broken.

What follows are some thoughts on the comparative merits of living alone or else getting married and raising a family. In verse 12, an application can be made outside of marriage to friends or relatives who stick together. But the best comment on the passage is to be found in Psalm 127:5, where the subject matter is your immediate family.

The "lone wolf' (vs. 8) does what he does for [himself. ]{.class_1790}If he is given credit for doing it for mankind, as a philanthropist or inventor, it must never be forgotten that self‑gratification is an animal instinct. Some men get as much self‑gratification out of "making the world a better place to live in" as they would in a sex orgy or while pocketing the jackpot from a one‑armed bandit. As a matter of fact, many of the "do‑gooders" do good to justify their own sins or to atone for them. They figure that by air conditioning the hog pen (Luke 15) and deodorizing the smell of it, they have earned their fare to heaven.

Now, you would think that if a man had no family responsibilities, he could be satisfied pretty easily, but this is not the case. ["Neither is his eye satisfied with riches." ]{.class_1791}Nothing is more pitiful on this earth than a rich, lonely, single, old miser whose best friends are a group of opportunists who are waiting for him to leave them something in his will. As one has so truthfully said: "There is nothing more repulsive on earth than watching an old, worn‑out sinner still trying to court this world, long after she had turned him down." If the single man makes any sacrifices to achieve fame and fortune---["and bereave my soul of good"]{.class_1791}---all is still ["vanity and vexation of spirit." ]{.class_1791}Ecclesiastes 2:21 and 2:15 will finish him off.

["Two are better than one." ]{.class_1791}I believe it. I believe it, having experienced Proverbs 21:9 and 21:19 first hand. I have lived the single life (1921--1944, 1959--1972, and 1987--1989), and I have lived the married life (1944--1959, 1972--1987, and 1989--), and I believe the married man, with children, has the best life of it. When the woman I married (AFTER I was saved) deserted me, I found []{#6z0vNAIsTD_RezYjRLYFFA557.xhtml_page_102}myself living on an acre of wooded land, completely fenced. It had three storage rooms on it, fruit trees, a wading pool, and space to garden. The house was partially brick and contained three bedrooms, two full baths, dining room, kitchen, living room, den, and sauna. I had just finished raising two families. The first had three boys and two girls; the second had two girls. So I took on three more sons to raise. I have never regretted it. I am not about to die in a three bedroom, two bath, house, on an acre of land, with nobody living in it but ME. I like a house full of laughter, music, noise, fussing, fun, confusion, prayer, Bible, and kids: kids and dogs. ["Two are better than one" ]{.class_1791}(vs. 9). The ["good reward" ]{.class_1791}not only comes from being able to do more work than one person, but God will reward each one for the sacrifices made for the other (his or her mate). Note that Solomon has switched from no rewards for labor (2:11--12) to a reward. Moral, natural reasoning, ["under the sun," ]{.class_1791}by the natural man, apart from the supernatural revelation of God, eventually crisscrosses its own path, thus becoming more contradictory than the Bible itself.

Verse 10 is self‑explanatory. Verse 11 is self-explanatory and is demonstrated in 1 Kings 1:1--4, in David's case. In verse 12, an additional statement is made: ["and a threefold cord," ]{.class_1791}meaning that there is not only an advantage in "two on one," but "three on one" is just as formidable. "Safety in numbers" is the modern adage.

4:13 Better is a poor and a wise child than an old and foolish king, who will no more be admonished.

14 For out of prison he cometh to reign; whereas also he that is born in his kingdom becometh poor.

15 I considered all the living which walk under the sun, with the second child that shall stand up in his stead.

16 There is no end of all the people, even of all that have been before them: they also that come after shall not rejoice in him. Surely this also is vanity and vexation of spirit.

The first two verses are strange things to record at this point, for neither of them is remotely connected with what has just been said. []{#6z0vNAIsTD_RezYjRLYFFA557.xhtml_page_103}They constitute a separate group of notes. Verse 14 is remarkably fulfilled in the case of Joseph (both clauses in the verse, because the famine showed up in seven years). But the ["old and foolish king, who will no more be admonished" ]{.class_1791}is not the Pharaoh of Joseph's restoration; that Pharaoh is a type of God the Father. (See notes on Gen. 41 in [The Bible Believer's Commentary on Genesis,]{.class_1790} 1970.)

A child can be poor and wind up in New Jerusalem; a child can be rich (Luke 16) and wind up in Hell, begging for water. A friend of mine, in Mississippi, said, "We wuz so poor (he said "per") that daddy ate four acres of black‑eyed peas at one sittin!" (Man, that's "poah!") Another friend of mine, from North Carolina, said, "Our ground was so poor, it couldn't even raise a fuss."

The ["old and foolish king" ]{.class_1791}is not identified, but the Scriptures would point to Solomon himself (1 Kings 11:3--8) as the subject of the statement (Job 32:9). If you make the one coming out of prison ["the old and foolish king," ]{.class_1791}you really have a mess. There are no ["old and foolish" ]{.class_1791}kings who come out of prison to reign anywhere. Mannaseh gets out (2 Chron. 33:13),[ ]{.class_1790}but he is not foolish when he is old: look at 2 Chronicles 33:12--15. Jehoiachin gets out, in 2 Kings 25:27, but he doesn't come out to reign, for no one is ["born in his kingdom." ]{.class_1791}He doesn't have any kingdom. Undoubtedly, there is a prophetic reference in the passage that no one has picked up yet (Ecc. 12:11). When they do, it certainly will not be any master of any assembly at BJU, PCC, Liberty University, Howard, Mercer, Judson, Stetson, Tennessee Temple, BBC, Wheaton, Fuller, Moody, or the seminaries of Ft. Worth, Dallas, Louisville, and New Orleans.

God doesn't waste time feeding angel's food cake (Psa. 78:25) to leeches and buzzards.

In verse 15, the ["second child" ]{.class_1791}would be the successor to the throne, who would ["stand up" ]{.class_1791}after the first heir to the throne was dead. Jamieson supposes the reference is to Rehoboam. He takes ["the old and foolish king" ]{.class_1791}to be Jeroboam, on the ground that, although Jeroboam did not come out of ["prison," ]{.class_1791}he fled to Egypt to avoid going to prison (1 Kings 11:40). But one can see, in one snapshot, that this is really stretching the application out of shape.

["There is no end of all the people." ]{.class_1791}Mankind is an ant pile. []{#6z0vNAIsTD_RezYjRLYFFA557.xhtml_page_104}There are over 5,600,000,000 people alive on this earth today (1993). They plan to kill each other off at a rate of 2,000 a day (abortion) so the survivors can preserve the spotted owl, the red mango, the rain forests, the baby whales, and bald eagles. There were 300,000,000 people in the U.S.A. in 1992, with more than twice as many in one city (New York) as could be found in the whole state of Alabama. There are more Africans in New York City than there are Africans in the largest city in Africa (Johannesburg). One hundred seventy thousand people are born daily, so a population of around 6,000,000,000 is expected by the year A.D. 2000. At present, the Chinese have 1,000,000,000 people, which is a larger population than Russia and the U.S.A. combined. In order to provide housing for American citizens, every city in America, with a population of 250,000 or more, must build 2,000 houses every two months (thirty‑three a day), till A.D. 2000. ["There is no end of all the people."]{.class_1791}

If you or you family (or one of your friends) died tonight, you could bet your bottom dollar that there would survive you, at least 5,000,000,000 people who knew nothing about your death or even what your name (or theirs) was. They wouldn't even know when or where you were born, where you lived, or what you did one time in ten to seventy years of living. One year after you are dead, there will probably be less than one hundred people, on this earth, who will even remember when you died. This planet is an ant hill.

["No end of all the people," ]{.class_1791}now, means: 16,207,000 in New York City, 11,324,000 in Tokyo, 11,000,000 in Shanghai, and 10,000,000 in Peking. Paris, Buenos Aires, and Los Angeles add between 7,000,000 and 9,000,000, apiece, to this menagerie. The Portuguese colony of Macao (southern coast of China), in 1986, had 392,000 people on it, living in 6.2 square miles. That is 63,225 people per square mile. In an area of 55,126 square miles in Bangladesh, there are 103,200,000 human beings, 1,882 people per square mile; that is one person for every 120 feet. Each individual would have a space 8 by 15 feet in which to live.

"There is no end of all the people."

Oh, how many times I have observed this Solomonic truth in the air terminals of Atlanta, Chicago, Fort Worth, Los Angeles, Miami, []{#6z0vNAIsTD_RezYjRLYFFA557.xhtml_page_105}New York, Munich, Moscow, Memphis, and Kansas City! How many times have these perishable eyes gazed out at mobs of people, numbering from 5,000 to 50,000, realizing that I could not call out the name of one person in the crowd. I have been thronged by strange faces in the meat markets of the Philippines, the streets on the Ginza in Tokyo, in the shopping centers in Frankfurt and Nuremberg (Germany), and in the underground railway stations in Tokyo, Katsura, and Nikko (Japan). I have waded through crowds of Russians, Mexicans, Japanese, Filipinos, and Germans. And I have sat in the bleachers in hockey rinks, football stadiums, ballparks, circus big tops, and church auditoriums.

Oh God! ["What is man, that thou art mindful of him?"]{.class_1791}

To me, one of the greatest mysteries of the Book is why God would take time out to save me or anyone else down here on this ant hill. (See [The Full Cup, ]{.class_1790}1992). I have not unraveled this mystery even after going through every verse in the Book 135 times.

["They also that come after shall not rejoice in him" ]{.class_1791}(vs. 16). This is taken to be ["the second child" ]{.class_1791}who inherits the throne (vs. 15). Jamieson would have to apply this to Rehoboam's successor (Abijah), if he meant what he said about verse 14; but he must not have meant it, for he makes the SECOND child Rehoboam. Rehoboam was the FIRST child (see 1 Kings 12--13). Rehoboam is the first immediate heir to Solomon's throne.

The general truth is clear:

1\. The ["old and foolish king" ]{.class_1791}is rejected by his subjects.

2\. The ["poor and wise child," ]{.class_1791}who becomes king, is rejected by his subjects.

3\. The ["second child," ]{.class_1791}who then takes the throne, is later rejected by the same subjects.

This pattern would begin, best, by starting with Saul, but David does not come ["out of prison"]{.class_1791};[ ]{.class_1791}at least, not a real one. None of the reigns are successful, in the sense that the following generation rejoices in the "late" king's reign.

# Chapter 5 {.heading_69}

5:1 Keep thy foot when thou goest to the house of God, and be more ready to hear, than to give the sacrifice of fools: for they consider not that they do evil.

2 Be not rash with thy mouth, and let not thine heart be hasty to utter any thing before God: for God is in heaven, and thou upon earth: therefore let thy words be few.

3 For a dream cometh through the multitude of business; and a fool's voice is known by multitude of words.

Observe the "breaks" (vss. 8, 9, 18). Verses 1 and 2 have to do with the Mosaic Law (see Deut. 23:21). Jephthah feels bound by verse 4, so he pays his vow; it costs him the life of his only child. In that case, it was Jephthah's ignorance of the Law that caused him to follow through, for the Law makes an allowance for a vow made in ignorance; see Leviticus 5:4. Verses 5 and 6 of Leviticus 5 show what Jephthah could have offered [instead ]{.class_1790}of his daughter.

In regards to verse 1, Solomon wrote, ["The sacrifice of the wicked is an abomination" ]{.class_1791}(Prov. 15:8).[ ]{.class_1791}Undoubtedly, Solomon knew the history of Saul (1 Sam. 13:12). Jeremiah 6:20 and Isaiah 1:11--12 deal with these same matters. One of the most remarkable "undesigned coincidences" in the Bible occurs at this point, which Solomon could not possibly have had in mind when he wrote. You see, the Catholic Mass is called a sacrifice ("The Sacrifice of the Mass"), and the fools who give it ["consider not that they do evil." ]{.class_1791}There is no daily, weekly, monthly, or yearly sacrifice of any physical kind, in this age, for any Christian (Heb. 10:8--12). If you see one being conducted, you are watching a pagan, Baalite ritual, being conducted by self‑appointed Nicolaitanes who are totally and completely out of the will of God as revealed in the New Testament (Heb. 9-- 10). Deism or Theism is the philosophy of verses 2, 4, 6, and 7. A New Testament Christian should be more ["ready to hear" ]{.class_1791}the words of God (1 Thess. 2:13; Gal. 3:1--5; and Rom. 10:14) than to watch a cannibal ritual sacrifice from the heart of Africa. The man of []{#6z0vNAIsTD_RezYjRLYFFA618.xhtml_page_108}verse 2 has ignored the warning which Solomon gave in Proverbs 29:20. Proverbs 18:13 is also an appropriate warning: ["Let thy words be few." ]{.class_1791}Observe how all of this matches James 2; 1 Peter 3:10; Proverbs 21:23, 10:18, 17:27, and 29:20. (Extensive comment will be found in [The Bible Believer's Commentary on Proverbs, ]{.class_1790}1981.)

["For a dream cometh" ]{.class_1791}(in the sense of nightmares), and can be caused ["to be dreamed"]{.class_1791} (Jer. 29:8). Pilate's wife has trouble with a dream; Pharaoh dreams twice; and Nebuchadnezzar has two dreams, separated by about twenty years. In all four cases, it takes a Hebrew prophet (not a Greek scholar or a Chaldean scientist) to come up with the right interpretation. God comes to Abimelech in a dream by night, showing that before the Bible was completed, God made a habit of revealing Himself in this fashion. Note especially, Numbers 12:6. Jacob dreams (Gen. 28:12), and his son Joseph dreams (Gen. 37). The Midianite soldier has a dream (Judg. 7:13) the night before his whole army is wiped out. And the author himself (Solomon) is spoken to, by God, in a dream (1 Kings 3:5). The Angel of the Lord appears to Joseph in a dream (Matt. 1:20), and then He speaks to the wise men who came to Joseph's house (Matt. 2:12). Dreams, in the Bible, are not taken lightly.

However, in the context (["cometh through the multitude of business"]{.class_1791}), Solomon is probably speaking of a hair‑brained idea that someone takes to be an inspiration. The best twentieth-century example is Michael King's "I had a dream," which produced a national nightmare in the schools, from shore to shore. When the Justice Department and the National Guard troops carried out Michael's "dream," they produced a system that sports 4,000 assaults, yearly, on teachers and students, the discarding of the Bible and prayer from the public schools, and 200,000 functional illiterates yearly, from 2,000 high schools. Michael Luther King's dream was like "I just dream about going to Hawaii," or "I dream of a day that I will win the state lottery," etc. No night vision is involved, and God Almighty is no more connected with such dreams than sunlight is connected with a bellyache.

The ["dream," ]{.class_1791}here, is something the vower (or sacrificer) has in mind, which he hopes will come true (see Jer. 23:25). He is []{#6z0vNAIsTD_RezYjRLYFFA618.xhtml_page_109}ambitious (note vs. 7). In the literal sense, a modern man's dreams are caused by ceaseless activity throughout the day; especially when they do not involve common manual labor (see 5:12). Mental and emotional labors are the source of nightmares. Scripturally speaking, any interpretation of any modern dream would have to be an interpretation that lined up with the Scriptures. In this respect, the correctors of the [Authorized Version ]{.class_1790}of the Holy Bible are "up a creek without a paddle" or "crippled too high for crutches," for they all confess (every one of them) that they have never seen one copy of the Scriptures (or one verse of Scripture) a day in their lives (2 Tim. 3:16). They further confess (100 percent of the Cult; all of them) that no copy of the Scriptures is available to a living soul on the face of this earth. They would sure have a time of it trying to interpret a dream.

5:8 If thou seest the oppression of the poor, and violent perverting of judgment and justice in a province, marvel not at the matter: for he that is higher than the highest regardeth; and there be higher than they.

Verse 8 would have belonged with verse 1, if it had been recorded at the same time, but it was not, so verse 8 stands out, alone, by itself. It says that three things commonly take place on this earth. The horror contained in these three routine operations (which take place in every country on this earth in every century) is incredible unless you have done a great deal of reading in the kind of literature which we mentioned under Ecclesiastes 1:18, which see.

The three statements tell us that:

1\. There is constant ["oppression of the poor."]{.class_1791}

2\. There is ["violent perverting of judgment."]{.class_1791}

3\. There is also ["violent perverting of justice."]{.class_1791}

All three of these crimes are as common, and as constant, as rain or wind. Any morning newspaper will either be reporting on one of these operations, or it will be supporting and carrying out one of them.

In the first case, the common saying is: "The rich get richer and the poor get poorer." In the Bible, it comes out as ["the rich and poor meet together: the ]{.class_1791}[Lord ]{.class_1795}[is the maker of them all" ]{.class_1791}(Prov. 22:2). Money is power, so without money, men are powerless (see comments under Prov. 19:4, 7, and 10:15). Sometimes a man is []{#6z0vNAIsTD_RezYjRLYFFA618.xhtml_page_112}poor because he won't work; sometimes he is poor because he can't get work. Many times a man is poor because he has a chronic illness or is handicapped or has a bunch of hospital bills to pay that would bankrupt Howard Hughes. Sometimes a man is poor because the IRS or the Mafia (same group) has stripped him of his savings and left him ["half dead" ]{.class_1791}on the road to Jericho.

Occasionally, a man is poor because, like the prodigal son, he was a spendthrift and threw away the wealth that God gave him. Many times, he is poor because a lawyer (or judge's "ruling") stripped him down to a barrel. Cases are rampant where an innocent man (in order to get back \$20,000 taken from him illegally) had to pay court costs and lawyers' fees of \$18,000 to get back \$2,000 of the money stolen from him. Sometimes a man is poor because he doesn't know how to handle money when he gets it; he cannot "budget" his income. Sometimes it is a combination of the cases listed above. Furthermore, sometimes a man is poor because he is "tight fisted" and won't give "cheerfully" (2 Cor. 9:6 and Luke 6:38).

But the most universal cause of poverty, or "below poverty level" living, has little to do with these things. If you want to know why you have whole nations like this (called "Third World nations" by the Communist news media, which attributes all of man's woes to Karl Marx's "distribution of wealth" thesis), it is because of mankind's universal rejection of the second commandment in the Decalogue (Exod. 20:4--5): the commandment that has been completely removed from the ten in all Roman Catholic catechisms, for all Roman Catholic churches, in every Roman Catholic country on earth. 5:9 Moreover the profit of the earth is for all: the king himself is served by the field.

10 He that loveth silver shall not be satisfied with silver; nor he that loveth abundance with increase: this is also vanity.

11 When goods increase, they are increased that eat them: and what good is there to the owners thereof, saving the beholding of them with their eyes?

12 The sleep of a labouring man is sweet, whether he eat little or much: but the abundance of the rich will not suffer him to sleep.

13 There is a sore evil which I have seen under the sun, []{#6z0vNAIsTD_RezYjRLYFFA618.xhtml_page_114}namely, riches kept for the owners thereof to their hurt.

14 But those riches perish by evil travail: and he begetteth a son, and there is nothing in his hand.

15 As he came forth of his mother's womb, naked shall he return to go as he came, and shall take nothing of his labour, which he may carry away in his hand.

16 And this also is a sore evil, that in all points as he came, so shall he go: and what profit hath he that hath laboured for the wind?

17 All his days also he eateth in darkness, and he hath much sorrow and wrath with his sickness.

Jerry Falwell's commentary ([Liberty Bible]{.class_1794}) quietly skips verse 9 and pretends it is not in the Book. ["The profit of the earth"]{.class_1791} is NOT for "all," if a king has a field tilled; he might be tilling it for [himself. ]{.class_1790}Again, it might not profit anyone after it was tilled, for look at Amos 4:6--12. "He that loveth silver shall not be satisfied with silver."

Solomon doesn't waste any time with relative truths. He is a realist who deals with reality.
