You may have noticed how the activity of the IRS increases as your income increases. (See comments on Prov. 17:19 in that Commentary.) I know of a millionaire near Amarillo, Texas, who buried five Cadillacs on his property, adjoining a major highway. When each Cadillac was one year old, he buried it, rear end first, two thirds of the way into the ground, with the hood and front wheels sticking up at an angle of about 30 degrees. You say, "What for?" Nothing; just for show. He was just "hot dogging" it. You can look at them, "Oh, mamma! Look at those cars. What's wrong with them?"

I know of another Texan, near Comfort, Texas, who bought one hundred acres of land on a large hill about three miles from the highway, and there he built (for him and his wife) a five bedroom, three bathroom, colonial brick, three story mansion, containing over 8,000 square feet on each floor. To protect himself and his wife, he put up a six‑foot metal fence around twenty acres of it, and then hired security guards to work in three shifts of eight hours each (around the clock) to protect the junk he had accumulated. You can see his mansion five miles up and down the highway, on both sides. What do people do? They drive by and exclaim, "Boy, look at THAT! Look up there!"

I know blacks in Pensacola who enjoy life more than that poor fool does, and the blacks make less than \$30,000 a year.

["He that loveth silver." ]{.class_1791}Like Cornelius Vanderbilt (1794--1877) who left \$100,000,000 in cash at his death. He asked his Christian wife and Christian doctor (Dr. Deems) to come to his death bed and hold his growing cold hands and sing for him, "Come ye sinners, poor and needy, weak and wounded, sick and sore." I have enjoyed handling \$20,000 more than Vanderbilt did in handling \$100,000,000. Here is John D. Rockefeller (1839--1937), a billionaire, or Ross Perot (a billionaire) or Henry Ford (1863--1947) or Andrew Mellon (1855--1937).

The money that Vanderbilt and Mellon amassed would have to be multiplied by eight to match today's bloated inflation. The richest man on earth, today, is a Japanese businessman named Yoshisaki []{#6z0vNAIsTD_RezYjRLYFFA618.xhtml_page_117}Tsutsumi (age: fifty‑four); he is worth \$18,900,000,000. He can only sleep in one bed at a time; lawyers and government agents are on his back, day and night; relatives dog him to death for help; he has no privacy; he cannot play racquetball or hockey---which I can, at seventy‑two years of age---and he will face judgment and hell at death. ["Riches profit not in the day of wrath" ]{.class_1791}(Prov. 11:4).

Sam Moore Walton (deceased, 1992) was only worth \$6,500,000,000 after he got through with Sam's Club and Wal-Mart; and poor, old, poverty‑stricken Ross Perot was way down on the billionaire's list with a measly net worth of \$3,000,000,000. He cannot eat hot peppers or jalapenos, he does not know how to use a mullet net, he couldn't jog three miles without falling flat on his face, and he knows about as much about God (and the Bible) as Rock Hudson or George Bush.

One of the richest businessmen whoever lived was Antonio De Angeles, a five‑foot, 290 pound "Yankee," from New Jersey. He ran the "Allied Crude Vegetable Oil Refining Co." In eight years, he managed to swindle \$175,000,000 from the public by keeping his huge salad oil tanks full of [salt water ]{.class_1790}from the ocean. After serving eight years in prison, he retired. It would be a conservative estimate to say that he had stashed away more than \$10,000,000 for a "rainy day," before they arrested him. Who needs more than \$10,000,000 to live on for twenty years, or even thirty? That is somewhere around \$300,000 to \$500,000 a year.

Eight years in prison is worth half that kind of money.

A successful businessman (who never got caught) was Anthony Moreno, who retired in luxury to Spain in 1968, after raking in \$6,400,000 in France, by forging birth certificates for welfare handouts.

["The sleep of a labouring man is sweet" ]{.class_1791}(vs. 12). This is so for two reasons (and his diet has nothing to do with it: ["whether he eat little or much"]{.class_1791}). In the first place, he is dog tired from hard work, so his mind quits when his body quits. In the second place, he has no ["abundance" ]{.class_1791}(like the ["rich" ]{.class_1791}in the same verse), so there is no sense in staying up half the night worrying about the IRS audit, the banks going broke, the savings and loan folding up, the stock market, the Dow Jones average, the value of the dollar, greedy relatives, kidnappers, or tricky investments. []{#6z0vNAIsTD_RezYjRLYFFA618.xhtml_page_118}["The abundance of the rich will not suffer him to sleep." ]{.class_1791}Rich people are noted for their use of drugs and liquor. The worker sleeps soundly and heavily.

Verse 13 is more of the same. I do not have time to write out for you, here, the biographies of W. C. Fields or John Paul Getty, two of the stingiest millionaires who ever lived, or the biographies of Frank Sinatra and Ted Turner, two of the most conceited millionaires who ever lived. There are "others" (Jimmy Bakker, the Rockefellers, Eastman, Kruger, et al.). However, I will give you one: Vincent (Big Vinnie) Teresa, a "soldier" in the New England Mafia.

Big Vinnie (one of Patriarca's boys) hauled in over \$2,000,000 a year. He ran gambling junkets to casinos, stripped suckers of their money in private poker games, fenced stolen jewelry (and restole it after selling it), loan sharked, and cleaned doctors and lawyers out of \$30,000 to \$50,000 at a lick. Vinnie fixed "banana races" (drugged race horses), stole car licenses and credit cards, drew \$10,000 to \$20,000 out of banks at one time with bad checks, set up phony passports and ID cards, stole and dumped off government security bonds, and then ran protection rackets. In twenty years, he took in over \$40,000,000.

Today, "Big Vinnie" is broke and out of work. He turned informer because a buddy, who had promised to take care of his family (while he was in "stir"), took off for Sicily with \$3,000,000 of the money Vinnie had saved up. In the twenty years he operated, Vincent Teresa never gave a charitable hand out to anyone. He wasted \$40,000,000, and now has nothing to show for it but a jail record and living day and night in fear of his life (or his family's lives). The "mob" still has a contract out on him.

["Those riches perish by evil travail" ]{.class_1791}(vs. 14).

The list of such men is endless: Joe Columbo (assassinated), Al Capone (died of syphilis), Vito Genovese (died in prison), Albert Anastasia (assassinated), John Gotti (imprisoned), Paul Castelonne (assassinated), Sam Giancana (assassinated), Angel Bruno (assassinated), Bugsy Siegel (assassinated), Lucky Luciano (died in exile), etc. Any man in the list was worth a minimum of \$2,000,000 a year. Most of them made over \$10,000,000 a year.

In expounding verses 13 and 14, all of the commentators forgot that the goods could ["perish" ]{.class_1791}[]{#6z0vNAIsTD_RezYjRLYFFA618.xhtml_page_119}by being stolen. "Bad investments" are only one side of a four‑sided proposition. For some peculiar reason, known only to a naive, gullible, Greek or Hebrew scholar, the only money that can hurt the owner is money invested unwisely. How the commentators missed the other three ways is impossible for anyone to understand who has had any experience in "living," at all. Keeping money in a bank can hurt you, and that is not an investment. You can get hurt hiding money in a mattress or in a flour can, and you don't invest either in "nothing, nowhere," when enemy troops invade your country and sack every cotton pickin'thing you kept "to your own hurt." Rich Jews in Vienna were tortured to death (1939) because the Gestapo knew they had kept plenty ["to their hurt," ]{.class_1791}and it had been invested in NOTHING.

Depositing money in a bank, that is to be robbed, is one side. Having enemy troops or thieves break and enter and rob you blind is another side, and hoarding is another side. Only one side out of four was bad investing. The commentators and scholars are operating a V‑8 on two cylinders. Typical.

Henrietta H. Green (1835--1916) kept a bank balance of \$31,000,000 in one bank, alone. She was so stingy that her son had to have his leg amputated because Henrietta wasted days looking for a FREE medical clinic. Henrietta lived off oatmeal (cold oatmeal at that), and she was too thrifty to heat any food. When she died, she left \$95,000,000 behind her, not having accomplished one decent thing for anyone on the face of this earth. She had eighty‑three years to feed her own belly. Henrietta Green was a fool beyond any blank idiot you ever met in your life, if Ecclesiastes 12:13--14 is telling the truth.

All of the money kept in the German National Bank reserves was stolen at the end of World War II. It came to \$9,878,000 in gold bullion---now worth about \$3,600,000,000---and six sacks of dollar bills amounting to \$408,840. An assistant bank manager of the National City Bank in New York cleaned the till out of \$883,660. None of it was "investment" money. The bank had demanded (absolutely illegally) that no one banking there could write out a check if they didn't keep a minimum of \$2,000 in the till. So the till was full. The New York Police Department confiscated 398 pounds of []{#6z0vNAIsTD_RezYjRLYFFA618.xhtml_page_120}heroine and cocaine (with a street value of \$73,000,000), and it was promptly "stolen" from the police department. On April of 1986, it was reported that the Roman Catholic president of the Philippines (Pres. Marcos) had embezzled over \$4,000,000,000 from his Roman Catholic compatriots. Mrs. Marcos was caught with 1,600 pairs of shoes, which she had purchased with some of the money.

You see, good and bad investments are small matters, for if they are stolen, they are all bad investments. Keep your money in a bank and the bank collapses; then the "insurer" ("Big Brother"), instead of giving you back the money you lost, bankrupts you by demanding (in one lump sum) all of the loans you made through the bank, payable on time payments. Instead, you are to pay them all up at one time to the bank that stole your income. To do this, you now have your property stolen. Moral: don't put money in a bank. Go put it in home savings and loan companies! If some thief pilfers your savings there, then Big Brother simply raises your TAXES to pay back the thief. Bad investment. Put your money in a mattress, and the house burns down; buy Security Bonds with it, and the Mafia will steal them, sell them at half price, and launder the money through Catholic banks in Venezuela, Columbia, and the Vatican Bank in Rome.

In America, crime PAYS.

A group of unsaved, liberal do‑gooders in Tallahassee, this year, levied a "street tax" (Mafia term) on all TAX FREE church-schools, on the grounds that the public needed to be protected from unearned credits and phony degrees issued by small schools. They decided to steal \$400 a year from every church school the first year and then \$2,000 the next year, etc. "Pay up or else." This educated Mafia (engaged in criminal activity) was TAXING tax‑exempt institutions by calling the tax a "fee." Maranzano, Castellone, Leggio, Buschetta, Gotti, Masseria, and Patriarca never handled it any better.

One smart bird cleaned the Los Angeles bank out of \$10,200,000 by using a computer (Stanley Mark Rifgin: born 1946). After salting away about \$5,000,000 for a "rainy day," Rifgin went cheerfully to jail (he was arrested November 6, 1958) at the age of thirty‑four. He then served seven years and retired at the ripe old []{#6z0vNAIsTD_RezYjRLYFFA618.xhtml_page_121}age of forty‑one as a free man, with a nest egg that would give Donald Trump a run for his money. In America, crime PAYS. [The news media promotes it.]{.class_1790}

The man who lives for himself is described in verses 13--17. This is the man who runs into the ["snare, and into many foolish and hurtful lusts" ]{.class_1791}(1 Tim. 6:9). He makes money his god.

1\. He comes in naked, and goes out naked (vs. 15). (See 1 Tim. 6:9).

2\. He leaves it ALL behind, so his "profit" is zero. ["What shall it profit a man, if he shall gain the whole world, and lose his own soul?" ]{.class_1791}When the rat race is over, he discovers the RATS have won it.

3\. He eats in spiritual darkness (vs. 17), and nine times out of ten, ["he hath much sorrow and wrath with his sickness" ]{.class_1791}(see Job 6:6--7). Rich men are noted for chronic illnesses, private nurses and doctors, and tables covered with bottles of pills. The man who ["will be rich" ]{.class_1791}has darkness in his heart when he is seated beneath a chandelier burning fifty 100‑watt bulbs. Ahab, in 1 Kings 21:1--4, could not see the sun if it were shining at high noon, on a cloudless day in July.

Verses 4--5, in the chapter, belong to that discipline of philosophy known as Axiology---the study of values---in particular, MORAL values. Verse 13 is a principle of Capitalism; you can make money by spending money; you make more that way than you can by hoarding.

5:18 Behold that which I have seen: it is good and comely for one to eat and to drink, and to enjoy the good of all his labour that he taketh under the sun all the days of his life, which God giveth him: for it is his portion.

19 Every man also to whom God hath given riches and wealth, and hath given him power to eat thereof, and to take his portion, and to rejoice in his labour; this is the gift of God.

20 For he shall not much remember the days of his life; because God answereth him in the joy of his heart.

This conclusion has been reached before; see Ecclesiastes 2:23 and 3:12--13. (Note Subjectivism in 2:25.)

["The preacher" ]{.class_1791}is setting the pace for the pack of Greek dumbbells who are to follow him (Plato, Aristotle, Zeno, Epicurus, Empedocles, Thales, et al.). He is fishing around for the ["summum bonum" ]{.class_1790}(the supreme good) which became the main theme of the Greek bullshooters on the Stoa (porch) when they wanted to demonstrate their ignorance in public. The Alexandrian Cult is still (2000) so taken up with this "stale crumb of Greek philosophy" (to cite Dr. Edward Hills), that the [ASV ]{.class_1790}of 1901 (and the [NASV ]{.class_1790}of 1971) attacked the Deity of Christ in Matthew 19:17, in order to reinsert this pagan bit of tomfoolery. This is the "Bible" recommended by Bob Jones Jr. and Bob Jones III (and their faculty members) from 1950 to 2000.

In this section, King Solomon concludes that, rich or poor, a man should enjoy what God gives him in this life. Furthermore, King Solomon gives God credit for making a rich man "rich" (vs. 19). (If Solomon keeps on talking like this, he will "put a chill on de meetin'" if any humanists, atheists, agnostics, or pantheists are in the vicinity. Realizing how thin‑skinned these classes of bigots are, Solomon drops "God" out of the discourse for twenty‑four verses, with only one mention of Him in 6:2. Instead, he returns to reasoning ["under the sun"]{.class_1791}). Observe, here, that Solomon is not only giving God credit for a man's ability to enjoy the riches he gets, but the ability to rejoice in the labor he does while acquiring them. Cases in point are R. G. LeTourneau, who tithed 90 percent of his income; J. C. Penny, who experienced the new birth; and Tom Landry, of the Dallas Cowboys. There are many others.

["For he shall not much remember the days of his life" ]{.class_1791}(vs. 20); that is, the bad days, the sad days, the times of depression and sorrow. He will not be able to remember them for two reasons: 1. Time flies quickly when you are enjoying fellowship with God, so ["forgetting those things which are behind" ]{.class_1791}is much easier than when you are tied down to something back in the past as a substitute. 2. The present is more real than the past when you are in fellowship with God, so your eyes, if they turn anywhere, tend to turn to the future; not the past. You "press forward." Verse 18 is []{#6z0vNAIsTD_RezYjRLYFFA618.xhtml_page_123}Epicureanism, but if God is not the author of the pleasure, it will not satisfy.

# Chapter 6 {.heading_69}

6:1 There is an evil which I have seen under the sun, and it is common among men:

2 A man to whom God hath given riches, wealth, and honour, so that he wanteth nothing for his soul of all that he desireth, yet God giveth him not power to eat thereof, but a stranger eateth it: this is vanity, and it is an evil disease.

The common evil, spoken of here, is a millionaire loaded down with publicity, honors, property, stocks, bonds, and influence, but he cannot enjoy them. Ecclesiastes 6:2 is the exception to 5:19. It is ["every man" ]{.class_1791}(5:19) except this bird, in verse 2. A man can have enough money to pay \$25.00 for a fancy meal in a restaurant and yet not have the digestive tract to be able to eat it after he has ordered it. ["A stranger eateth it." ]{.class_1791}A man may have a lucrative profession, wear ornate apparel, and have a commodious residence; but the IRS may clean him out, or invasion troops may take everything he has, including his life. It is possible for a millionaire's bank account to be wasted down to a piggy bank, paying lawyer's fees through a period of five years; sometimes the lawyers will drag it out for twenty‑five years; that's how they make a living. Ahab is "sullin" on the throne; Haman is having a "conniption fit" (cat‑nip fit), although he is "second only" to the king, in power; Nebuchadnezzar is so upset by a dream that he is ready to kill his own servants. "The mountains of worldly honor are always covered with a perpetual snow." Witness old "blue eyes" (Frankie Boy Sinatra) spending the last ten years of his life lounging around at cocktail parties, with a glass in his hand, staring out into space, and mumbling to himself like a mission bum sitting on a park bench. He was worth \$15,000,000 a year. I have known "niggers" in Alabama and Georgia who got more out of life drinking an "R.C." and eating a "Moon Pie," while fishing off a railroad trestle for croakers.

[The ability to enjoy life comes from God]{.class_1790} (1 Tim. 6:17).

If you will pardon the personal reference, I believe that God gave []{#6z0vNAIsTD_RezYjRLYFFA711.xhtml_page_125}me the ability to enjoy life so far above and beyond the average millionaire's capacity, that I wouldn't consider stooping down to get into his league. (See [The Full Cup,]{.class_1794} an autobiography, 1992.) I have gotten more out of throwing a mullet net into the ocean, on a fall night, than Johnny Carson or Dean Martin got out of a celebrity performance. I have relished the luxury of going out on a hockey rink, on skates, at the age of seventy‑one to "keep the gate." I never got on ice skates till I was sixty years old. When I did, I wound up playing goalie in more than eight hundred games in the next twelve years. You talk about [enjoying ]{.class_1794}the good life! Three houses paid for, three churches paid for, seventeen cars paid for, ten children raised, without one of them winding up on liquor or drugs, and all of them believing the Book from cover to cover. You talk about enjoying life! Why, what on earth would Bill Cosby, Johnny Carson, Michael Jackson, or President Bush know about it? On the way, the Lord gave me 8,000 souls, called more than 200 young men to preach, and then gave me about 250 days a year, for forty‑three years, without one real care in the world or one real gripe or complaint. With the exception of two years (1960 and 1988) I wouldn't want to "redo" one week of my life. I'll bet you there isn't a millionaire on earth who could say that [honestly]{.class_1794} and[ ]{.class_1794}mean it. Why, bless my soul, I'll bet you I have enjoyed a bowl of smokey green pea soup and a piece of black bread more than John Lennon or Ringo ever enjoyed the biggest lobster dinner they ever had in a lifetime. ["The joy of the ]{.class_1791}[Lord ]{.class_1795}[is your strength."]{.class_1791}

6:3 If a man beget an hundred children, and live many years, so that the days of his years be many, and his soul be not filled with good, and also that he have no burial; I say, that an untimely birth is better than he.

4 For he cometh in with vanity, and departeth in darkness, and his name shall be covered with darkness.

5 Moreover he hath not seen the sun, nor known any thing: this hath more rest than the other.

6 Yea, though he live a thousand years twice told, yet hath he seen no good: do not all go to one place?

7 All the labour of man is for his mouth, and yet the []{#6z0vNAIsTD_RezYjRLYFFA711.xhtml_page_126}appetite is not filled.

8 For what hath the wise more than the fool? what hath the poor, that knoweth to walk before the living?

Verse 3 is like Ecclesiastes 5:17. Nothing is right outside when things are not right [inside ]{.class_1790}(Jer. 22:19). The burial matters are in Isaiah 53:9; Jeremiah 8:2, and 22:19. The Old Testament Jew considered an honorable burial to be of the greatest significance (see such places as 1 Sam. 31:13; 2 Sam. 4:12, 21:12--14). The statement tells us that not even a long life guarantees happiness or success, nor does a multiplicity of children, if ["his soul be not filled with good." ]{.class_1791}Two things, then, are evident: 1. If he is a wicked man, with a soul full of wickedness, then his status amounts to nothing (see 2:26 and 3:12). 2. If his ["soul"]{.class_1791} cannot enjoy what God has provided for his body (see vs. 2 and Luke 12:20) then, again, his status amounts to nothing. Hence, such a man is compared with an ["untimely birth" ]{.class_1791}that comes to nothing. The[ "he"]{.class_1791} of verse 4 is the untimely birth, as described also in Job 3:16--20. The dead baby does not see the sun nor "know anything" (vs. 5), so he has ["more rest than the other"]{.class_1791}; i.e., the man described in verses 2 and 3. "Soul sickness" is the term coined by William James to describe verse 3. The same man is still being discussed in verse 6: ["though he live a thousand years twice told" ]{.class_1791}(see vs. 3), ["and live many years\...yet hath he seen no good." ]{.class_1791}He sees no good because his soul is not filled with good; this is the ["darkness" ]{.class_1791}spoken of in 5:17. Throughout, the rich man being discussed has made riches his god but has been unable to enjoy them after he hoarded them. He goes to the same place the untimely birth goes to: darkness (cf Job 3:16--20).

Verse 7 states the great basic fact of all human life on earth; the MOUTH is the means of life and death. This truth is an absolute truth and is relative to nothing. Man's trouble began with his mouth (Gen. 3). That is where Eve's trouble began (Gen. 3:2). The words ["eat" ]{.class_1791}or ["eaten" ]{.class_1791}occur seventeen times in the third chapter of the Bible, making it completely unique among all the so‑called "scriptures" of the other religions. If the only evidence you had that Biblical Christianity was totally different from all other religions on the face of the earth was Genesis 3, it would do the job. Why would any []{#6z0vNAIsTD_RezYjRLYFFA711.xhtml_page_127}religious book on earth begin with a discussion about what you put in [your mouth?]{.class_1790} The [Shastas ]{.class_1790}don't. The [Puranas ]{.class_1790}don't. The [Tripitaka ]{.class_1790}doesn't. The [Talmud ]{.class_1790}doesn't. Mary Baker Eddy's [Key ]{.class_1790}certainly doesn't. None of the books on White Magic or Black Magic (the [Kaballa, ]{.class_1790}the Tarot cards, etc.) do. The [Book of Mormon]{.class_1790} doesn't. My, what a strange Book! "EAT, eat, eat, eat, eat, eat, eaten, eat, etc." ["All the labour of man is for his mouth." ]{.class_1791}You work to stay alive; you stay alive by [eating. ]{.class_1790}Get the message? ["Death and life are in the power of the tongue: and they that love it shall eat the fruit thereof" ]{.class_1791}(Prov. 18:21).

Your mouth and your tongue (James 3:5--6) are the means by which you live (Rom. 10:9--10) or die. You [die ]{.class_1790}because everything you put in your mouth comes from the [ground]{.class_1790}, and in the third chapter of Genesis, God curses the ground (Gen. 3:17). Got the message yet? These are absolute truths that are binding on every atheist, scientist, agnostic, psychiatrist, humanist, polytheist, pantheist, Jew, Catholic, Mohammedan, anarchist, nihilist, and Buddhist on the face of this earth, male or female. Six thousand years of "scientific progress" hasn't changed the impact of these truths; 6,000 years of "progress" never affected one of them. All the scientists (if they are going to live) have to eat to live; all of them die and they all die because what they ate came from the [ground ]{.class_1790}(Gen. 3:17). They labor for their mouths, just like all illiterate Negritoes and Fuzzy‑wuzzies have done for centuries. Further, they still have an ["appetite." ]{.class_1791}This means that not only are man's eyes and ears insatiable (see 1:8), but so, also, is his BELLY. If you just ate a meal, you will be hungry again in less than twenty hours after you read this print. (And probably in less than ten hours after you read it!)

To show you how voracious the ["appetite" ]{.class_1791}is, consider this jungle‑bunny's stomach, in South Africa, where they found the leftovers of fifty‑three toothbrushes, two razor blades, two telescoped aerials, and 150 handles off disposable razors ([Guiness Book of]{.class_1790} [Records]{.class_1790}). Michael Lotito, of Grenoble, France, surpassed all eaters (1950). He began eating [glass ]{.class_1790}and [metals ]{.class_1790}back in 1959, and in the next twenty years he consumed ten bicycles, a supermarket cart, seven TV sets, six chandeliers, and a Cessna light aircraft (eaten at Caracas in Venezuela). Michael found out he could ingest two []{#6z0vNAIsTD_RezYjRLYFFA711.xhtml_page_128}pounds of METAL, per day, without getting sick.

A great appetite was demonstrated by Dr. Ronald Alkana (University of California, Dec. 7, 1973) when he ate seventeen large bananas in two minutes. Reg Morris, of Burntwood, England (Dec. 10, 1986), gave him some competition by swallowing down thirty frankfurters in sixty‑four seconds. Tommy Green (Annapolis, July 6, 1985) gulped down 288 oysters in one minute and thirty‑three seconds. (That is six pounds of oysters.)

There also have been some world champion cooks who catered to gluttons (Prov. 23:21). For those who like giant helpings, we have a hamburger that weighed 5,100 pounds; it was served up at Coral Springs, Florida (July 9, 1988). Then there was a pancake, tailor‑made for Paul Bunyan. It was made at Lefaiver, Ontario (June 26, 1988) and weighed 2,000 pounds (that is one ton); it was thirty feet in diameter. For pizza lovers, a pizza was cooked in Tallahassee, Florida, which was 100 feet in diameter. And the longest sausage ever produced rolled out of Wolverhampton, England (June 18, 1988). It took fifteen hours and thirty‑three minutes to roll it out; it was (believe it or not) 13,125 miles long (Guiness [Book of Records]{.class_1790}).

Jamieson wrongly assumes that the wise man (in the next verse) does have his ["appetite" ]{.class_1791}satisfied, so he reads it as "what advantage does the wise man have over the fool, and what other advantage does the godly, poor man have over him\...etc." But all of this is snipe hunting, at night, among the sea oats. No wise man has his appetite filled more than twelve hours at a shot. Take his meals away from him for three days, and he will have an appetite to match a bear's appetite. The text is saying that when it comes to satisfying your carnal appetite for food, the wise man has nothing ["more than the fool." ]{.class_1791}They are both in the same boat, like they were back in Ecclesiastes 2:15, 19. (The [Wycliffe ]{.class_1790}commentator cannot handle verses 6, 7, or 8, so he just omits them.) In the case before us, the "poor man"[ ]{.class_1791}may be able to conduct himself properly throughout life---"I only make \$50.00 a week, and I live a good Christian life!" "Well, sure, on that salary I guess that is about the only kind of a life you could live!"---but he has the universal problems: 1. He dies and goes back to the dust, just like any godless rich man mentioned. 2. He labors all of his life to satisfy an appetite which will not be []{#6z0vNAIsTD_RezYjRLYFFA711.xhtml_page_129}satisfied here.

6:9 Better is the sight of the eyes than the wandering of the desire: this is also vanity and vexation of spirit.

10 That which hath been is named already, and it is known that it is man: neither may he contend with him that is mightier than he.

11 Seeing there be many things that increase vanity, what is man the better?

12 For who knoweth what is good for man in this life, all the days of his vain life which he spendeth as a shadow? for who can tell a man what shall be after him under the sun?

A popular saying is, "A bird in the hand is worth two in the bush," which comes from the German original: "A sparrow in the hand is better than one on the roof." Solomon has just been "downing eyesight" (5:11), but now he recommends it; at least, it is better than daydreaming and coveting things you don't have. This is Rationalism.

["The wandering of the desire" ]{.class_1791}is created, stimulated, developed, aggravated, and magnified one hundred times as much, since 1950, as in any time before that. 1\. The inability to enjoy riches after obtaining them.

3\. A physical appetite that cannot be permanently satisfied.

4\. The wandering of the mind, coveting THINGS that a man can't get his hands on.

5\. The inability of man to successfully contend with his Maker, who made him out of dust.

These are the ["many things that increase vanity" ]{.class_1791}(text). Someone spouting out a lot of "words" (see any modern, corrupt translation) is not in the discussion.

# Chapter 7 {.heading_69}

7:1 "A good name is better than precious ointment; and the day of death than the day of one's birth."

The saying stands by itself, although it turns out to be the first in a series of "betters" that are suggested in Axiological researches (vss. 2, 3, 5, 8, and 10). For a remarkable illustration of the verse, compare ["it is more blessed to give than to receive" ]{.class_1791}with Matthew 26:7. Since no man can outdo God when it comes to [giving ]{.class_1790}(Rom. 11:35), Christ does not allow Mary to out give Him. He gives her the ["good name," ]{.class_1791}and it ["is better than precious ointment,"]{.class_1791} which she gives Him (Matt. 26:7---see text above).

You cannot out give God.

["And the day of death\...." ]{.class_1791}This is called "negative thinking." In Christ's case, no Christian was ever commanded to commemorate His birth. It is the pagan Gentile rulers who are hung up on birthdays: see Pharaoh in Genesis 40:20 and Herod in Mark 6:21. You are commanded to commemorate Christ's DEATH (1 Cor. 11:26). Be careful to observe that the good reputation, which is supposed to accompany the ["good name," ]{.class_1791}is not always based on reputation at all, or even character. Paul's name was a death sentence (2 Cor. 2:16); it was a stinking stench to Pharisees, Judaizers, and Nero. Christ's [reputation, ]{.class_1790}among the religious leaders of His day, was that of a demon possessed (John 7:20) blasphemer (Mark 14:64). A consecrated, Bible‑believing, soul‑winning Christian, in this day (1960--2000), can go down in history as a trouble‑making, hell‑raising leader of a dangerous cult. The people who will place this label on him will be the faculties and staff members of the major Conservative and Fundamental Christian colleges, seminaries, and universities: ["jealousy is the rage of a man" ]{.class_1791}(Prov. 6:34). (For documentation, see [The History of the New Testament Church,]{.class_1790} Vol. 2) Conversely, a bloody killer, like Pope John Paul, Nelson Mandela, Joe Stalin, or Pope Pius XII, can come out with a ["good name"]{.class_1791} like the names of Jack Kennedy, John Lennon, Mother Teresa, Elvis Presley, Michael Jackson, Michael L. []{#6z0vNAIsTD_RezYjRLYFFA782.xhtml_page_141}King Jr., Gorbachev, Madonna, and other news media gods.

There are two lists of good names in history. There are two different "Who's Who" in history, if the New Testament is telling the truth in Romans, Galatians, and Ephesians. I have not yet listed one ["good name" ]{.class_1791}in the last paragraph. [God's list ]{.class_1790}of good names would look like this: Peter, James, Moses, John, Elijah, David, Joseph, Paul, Chrysostom, Polycarp, Ignatius, Paton, Jacob Spener, Jonathan Goforth, John Paton, Harlan Popov, Richard Wurmbrand, John Wesley, George Whitefield, Frank Norris, Bob Jones Sr., Lester Roloff, Sam Jones, Hudson Taylor, Adoniram Judson, William Booth, Martin Luther, and Charles G. ["Friendship of the world is enmity with God" ]{.class_1791}(James 4:4).

7:2 It is better to go to the house of mourning, than to go to the house of feasting: for that is the end of all men; and the living will lay it to his heart.

3 Sorrow is better than laughter: for by the sadness of the countenance the heart is made better.

4 The heart of the wise is in the house of mourning; but the heart of fools is in the house of mirth.

5 It is better to hear the rebuke of the wise, than for a man to hear the song of fools.

6 For as the crackling of thorns under a pot, so is the laughter of the fool: this also is vanity.

Where a funeral is in progress, there is a ["house of mourning," ]{.class_1791}somewhere. Verse 3 is Stoical philosophy: stiff upper lip, grin and bear it. Verse 3 matches Proverbs 15:13. Isaiah 22:12--14 is a comment on verse 4. ["The living will lay"]{.class_1791} the funeral of the dead man ["to his heart" ]{.class_1791}(see 2 Sam. 1:12, 11:26; 1 Kings 13:30, []{#6z0vNAIsTD_RezYjRLYFFA782.xhtml_page_142}14:18, etc.). Death forces us to THINK. It makes philosophers out of every adult on two legs. "They that truly study philosophy, study, rightly, nothing but death." Matters are really laid to heart when the deceased is closely related to (and loved by) his survivors (Gen. 37:34; 50:3, 10, etc.). If ["sorrow is better than laughter," ]{.class_1791}then wisdom has finally been justified, for ["he that increaseth knowledge increaseth sorrow" ]{.class_1791}(Ecc. 1:18), according to Solomon's original thought pattern. Wisdom does excel ["folly" ]{.class_1791}(see 2:13). As the [outside ]{.class_1790}of a man is affected by his [inward condition ]{.class_1790}(see 5:17), so his [outward appearance ]{.class_1790}can also affect his inner condition. ["By the sadness of the countenance the heart is made better." ]{.class_1791}This is real sadness, however, not the disfigured face of the fasting Pharisee mentioned in Matthew 6:16.

We have commented on ["laughter" ]{.class_1791}(vs. 6) under Ecclesiastes 2:2. Here we learn that a man's heart can reside ["in the house of mirth," ]{.class_1791}whether his body is present there or not; ditto with the ["heart of the wise" ]{.class_1791}(vs. 4). This means that inside man, his meditations can be on vain, fleshy, trivial pleasures (["as he thinketh in his heart, so is he"]{.class_1791}), or else his heart can be sober, meditating on the great themes of life, death, sin, sanctification, God, judgment, heaven, hell, righteousness, Jesus Christ, and the Bible. If you need any "background music" (see vs. 5) for these two types of thinking, they are certainly available.

The thinker of verse 4---the fool who is in ["the house of mirth"]{.class_1791}---should obtain the recordings of Bunk Johnson, Sidney Bechet, Louis Armstrong, Bunny Berrigan, Jack Teagarden, Leadbelly, and Jelly Roll Morton. Then he should add to these, the platters made by Jimmy and Tommy Dorsey, Artie Shaw, Benny Goodman, Glenn Miller, Woody Herman, Stan Kenton, and Harry James, along with some vocals by Frank Sinatra, Doris Day, Patti Page, Nat King Cole, Bing Crosby, Kay Starr, Fats Domino, Aretha Franklin, Rosemary Clooney, Jo Stafford, Perry Como, and Dinah Shore. To round off the balanced program, he should get the cassettes put out by Too Live Crew, Prince, KISS, Michael Jackson, Janis Joplin, Mick Jagger, the Rolling Stones, the Beatles, the Motley Crew, the Twisted Sisters, Hennan's Hermits, Chuck Berry, Jerry Lee Lewis, Tom Jones, Tina Turner, and Stevie Wonder. That will do it. He now is completely stocked up on ["the song of fools," ]{.class_1791}[]{#6z0vNAIsTD_RezYjRLYFFA782.xhtml_page_143}of, by, and for the world.

The other thinker in verse 4 (["the heart of the wise"]{.class_1791}) should immediately collect the works of Bach, Haydn, Mozart, and Handel, and lighten them up with some works by Bocherini, Vivaldi, Staumitz, Albinoni, Cuperan, Telemann, and Pachelbell. Then he should obtain the eight symphonies Franz Peter Schubert wrote, the nine that Beethoven wrote, the four that Brahms wrote, and the six that Tschaikovsky wrote. This anti‑ thesis to ["the song of fools" ]{.class_1791}should be topped off with a dozen (or more) concertos for flute, oboe, viola, violin, French horn, and piano by Mozart, Beethoven, Mendelssohn, Brahms, and Vivaldi.

Music is the universal language: it speaks.

But in the passage, ["the song of fools" ]{.class_1791}is not contrasted with "the song of the wise," but with ["the]{.class_1791} [rebuke of the wise." ]{.class_1791}In the Bible, this is [preaching ]{.class_1790}(see 2 Tim. 4:2), not teaching (see p. 344). The reference is to [Biblical preaching. ]{.class_1790}If there is the slightest doubt in your mind about it, compare 2 Timothy 4:2 with Titus 1:3 and 2:15. This means that any man can learn more (that is true) sitting at the feet of a Bible-believing preacher for an hour (see Mary: Luke 10:40--41) than he can by spending thirty hours listening to highly paid entertainers singing about love, sex, fornication, marriage, sex perversion, drugs, suicide, sorrow, and social issues. To illustrate, simply line up what a man could learn listening to the sermons of Billy Sunday, Dwight Moody, Bob Jones Sr., Sam Jones, Martin Luther, Charles H. Spurgeon, Oliver Green, and Tim Lee, and compare it with what he could learn (that was SO) listening to 400 hours of Dinah Shore, the King Sisters, Patti Page, Doris Day, Perry Como, Frank Sinatra, Bing Crosby, Rudy Vallee, Vic Damone, Mel Torme, Connie Francis, Eddie Fisher, Brenda Lee, the Judds, Tammy Wynette, Loretta Lynn, Marty Robbins, Buck Owens, Hank Williams, and the Andrew Sisters.

One good, Bible‑thumping, sin-condemning, pulpit-pounding, bark‑ripping, hide‑tearing SERMON is worth any ten gold platters (or "uranium albums") that any dope‑headed, fornicating Grammy award winner ever produced in a lifetime.

["As the crackling of thorns under a pot" ]{.class_1791}(vs. 6). See Joel []{#6z0vNAIsTD_RezYjRLYFFA782.xhtml_page_144}2:5. The sound is hollow, it is thin and high-pitched, and it "snaps." It has no substance. The fire, burning the ["thorns," ]{.class_1791}will burn the fool, if we are to believe David (2 Sam. 23:6).

By now, we have quite a list of things that turn out to be nothing but ["vanity"]{.class_1791}:

1\. The works ["done under the sun"]{.class_1791} (1:14).

2\. The enjoyment of pleasure (2:1).

3\. Wisdom (2:15).

4\. The leaving of your goods to someone else (2:21).

6\. A man's physical life (3:19).

7\. A man being envied for doing right (4:4).

8\. A man who lives for himself (4:7).

9\. The failure of a leader to be appreciated (4:16).

10\. The love of money (5:10).

11\. The inability to enjoy wealth (6:2).

12\. Coveting, by letting your desires wander all over the place to lust after various things (6:9).

13\. The unsatisfied appetite (6:7).

14\. ["The laughter of the fool"]{.class_1791} (7:6).

That is a fourteen point message. No wonder that, at the conclusion of his sermon, the preacher cries out: ["vanity of vanities\...all is vanity" ]{.class_1791}(Ecc. 12:8). He began with this text (1:2), so he ends with it; his message is homiletical.

7:7 Surely oppression maketh a wise man mad; and a gift destroyeth the heart.

8 Better is the end of a thing than the beginning thereof: and the patient in spirit is better than the proud in spirit.

9 Be not hasty in thy spirit to be angry: for anger resteth in the bosom of fools.

10 Say not thou, What is the cause that the former days were better than these? for thou dost not inquire wisely concerning this.

If a man really studies what is going on, on this earth (Ecc. 7:13), []{#6z0vNAIsTD_RezYjRLYFFA782.xhtml_page_145}he becomes deeply disturbed about the injustices we mentioned in 4:1 and 5:8. Further, he will eventually (if he has any red blood in him) become ANGRY, just like the Lord Jesus Christ (Mark 3:5). Christ doesn't sin (Eph. 4:26) when He gets mad, but He gets mad enough to throw furniture around and slap animals and men with a whip (John 2:15). Although the primary application of verse 7 is that the wise man would lose his wisdom and become "mad," in the sense of Ecclesiastes 2:2, 12, and 9:3, still both meanings are true. Since this is the truth, the word has been erased, immediately, from the [RV, RSV, NRSV, ASV, NASV, NIV, NEB, NWT, ]{.class_1790}and [NKJV. ]{.class_1790}(Observe how the ["New" KJV ]{.class_1790}constantly lines up with the unsaved Liberals in the NCC ([RSV ]{.class_1790}and [NRSV]{.class_1790}) and the Jehovah's Witnesses "begotten God" ([NASV]{.class_1790}) in John 1:18, while destroying the God‑honored text. However, this bribe (in Taylor's [Dead Dodo]{.class_1790}) still has no affect on the wise man's ["heart," ]{.class_1791}because Taylor has performed heart surgery and taken the man's heart out of him; only his "understanding" is affected (see Ecc. 3:11 and comments).

Isn't it amazing how the only thing these Alexandrians LOVE is cutting up the word of God, and the only things they HATE is someone who finds this out? The ["gift" ]{.class_1791}[]{#6z0vNAIsTD_RezYjRLYFFA782.xhtml_page_146}of verse 7 is a bribe, like you find it in Proverbs 15:27 and 29:4. But it destroys the ["heart" ]{.class_1791}because ["as he thinketh in his heart, so is he." ]{.class_1791}This explains the trouble Kenneth Taylor had with the text. When these destructive apostates start messing with a [King James Bible, ]{.class_1790}it looks like a four‑year‑old trying to juggle two dozen double‑edged razor blades.

Verse 8 is true of Paul's life and of Christ's life, and of the life of any real Christian (see Phil. 1:21 and 2 Cor. 5:1--10). Murphy's law says, "Anything that begins bad, gets worse." The second clause is apparent. A good illustration of it will be found in Romans 2:7--8, and 12:12. ["Be not hasty in thy spirit."]{.class_1791}. This is preaching, not teaching, as many of the apostate Fundamentalists theorized. Comments will be found in Proverbs 12:16 and James 1:19--20. (See also the comments under Eph. 4:26 in [The Bible Believer's Commentary on Galatians--Colossians, ]{.class_1790}1974.)

["Say not thou" ]{.class_1791}(vs. 10). The verse is the theme song of a philosophy called "Phenomenalism," which (briefly) is the teaching that no past experiences are any good; none of them can be used as a foundation, because things change so fast that each person has to discover "truth" for himself---i.e., what he wants to use as an alibi for his own sins.

This, of course, is suicide. It is saying that [experience ]{.class_1790}doesn't count because it isn't YOUR experience. This attitude is the contemporary philosophy being taught (1990) incognito in all public schools. Its early exponents (Mill, Bacon, Hobbes, Hume, Bentham) were replaced by pragmatists like Bertrand Russell, John Dewey, Biovanni Gentile, and William James, who led America into the pits.

Verse 10 has to be a warning, because, in the first place, men tend to glamorize, or color, the past with hues much "rosier" than the original painting. (See comments on Exod. 14:11--12 in [The Bible Believer's Commentary on Exodus.]{.class_1790}) At a distance, things look better. Thus, you are liable to fail to thank God for the present or start griping about the present, when, in actuality, it is [better ]{.class_1790}than your past. In the second place, if your inner peace is better now than it was, it is only because of your relationship with God; that is what has made things better. Government, weather conditions, and economic factors may control your physical benefits, but the []{#6z0vNAIsTD_RezYjRLYFFA782.xhtml_page_147}[spiritual benefits ]{.class_1790}are controlled by God. The most outstanding case I know, of this thing, would be the American Civil War (1861--1865). In that war, the [winner ]{.class_1790}(the North) came out ahead economically and politically; spiritually, they lost their shirt and their "drawers." Rome always comes out on the winning side (WWI, WWII, Vietnam, etc.) since she can straddle both sides of a conflict until victory is sure; then she will move perceptibly toward the winner. After the Civil War, the pope took over the entire northeastern United States (Vermont, New Hampshire, New York, New Jersey, Maryland, Connecticut, Massachusetts, and Rhode Island); thus the "land of the pilgrim's pride" \[and the First and Second Great Awakening\] became the most pagan, depraved, dope‑ridden, demon‑occupied nest of witches in America. Since Ohio, Michigan, Illinois, Indiana, Wisconsin, and Minnesota were also "preserving the Union" in blue, the Vatican swallowed them whole. Biblical Christianity [disappeared ]{.class_1790}from Yankeeland within forty years of 1865. It is still thriving in North Carolina, Tennessee, and Texas and it has not been completely stomped out in Alabama, Georgia, Mississippi, Arkansas, and Louisiana, although TV and the press are working on it.

Washington, D.C., is now the murder capital of the world---twelve murders a day---while Jeff Davis' hometown (Montgomery, Alabama) had to be RETAKEN by troops, in 1965, when George Wallace was the governor. The "loser" came out with less than one murder a month, and the "winner" came out with twelve a day. The "winner" came out with the pope, witchcraft, the Mafia, Christian Science, financial disasters (New York, Detroit, etc.), and an ignorance of the Book that would only match the populaces of Haiti, Spain, Cuba, and Mexico. Worth, Miami, Jacksonville, etc.) and every Christian leader in America who was connected with anything that even slightly resembled a revival (Jack Hyles, Bob Jones Sr., John R. Rice, Billy Graham, and Jerry Falwell). The winner came out with "Hail Mary" and a string of beads, and the loser came out with prayer and a [King James Bible. ]{.class_1790}This explains the persistent impact of "the old‑time religion" in North Carolina, Alabama, Georgia, Tennessee, []{#6z0vNAIsTD_RezYjRLYFFA782.xhtml_page_148}South Carolina, Mississippi, Arkansas, Texas, and Florida, to this day.

A Southerner, from 1866 to 1890, could holler all he wanted to about "the good ole' days" in Dixie, before the war; but the "good ole' days," SPIRITUALLY, came after the war. A church can be flat broke, and it is "rich" (Rev. 3:17--19); it can be rich as Rockefeller (Rev. 2:9) and imagine itself in the "poverty level."

Now, to show you how shallow and superficial the godly scholars are, with whom we have been dealing, study the remarks on the text by the [Layman ]{.class_1790}commentator (Johnson), the [Broadman ]{.class_1790}commentator (Wayne Peterson), the [New Bible ]{.class_1790}commentator (George Hendry), and the [Wycliffe ]{.class_1790}commentator (plus [Dummelow, Jamieson, Ellicott, Williams, ]{.class_1790}and [Lange]{.class_1790}). The superficial and naive scholars were so intent on talking about "rebelling against God's foreordained times and plans in the present," that they forgot the first fundamental law of ADAM: the law of human collapse. With the passage of time there is always constant entropy and deterioration (Second Law of Thermodynamics). The former days, for almost any civilized nation, refer to times when men had principles and character, but as time passed by, these collapsed and degenerated (see 2 Tim. 3:1--7 for this law as it applies to this present age: the Church Age).

You are to ["ask for the old paths," ]{.class_1791}not the ones of your day and time. The warning in Ecclesiastes was only a rationalistic warning saying that it was not good to live in the past while complaining about the present; that is all the "doctrine" there was in the verse.

7:11 Wisdom is good with an inheritance: and by it there is profit to them that see the sun.

12 For wisdom is a defence, and money is a defence: but the excellency of knowledge is, that wisdom giveth life to them that have it.

13 Consider the work of God: for who can make that straight, which he hath made crooked?

14 In the day of prosperity be joyful, but in the day of adversity consider: God also hath set the one over against the other, to the end that man should find nothing after him.

["To them that see the sun," ]{.class_1791}in contrast with those that cannot see the sun (6:5). ["Wisdom," ]{.class_1791}in verse 12, ["is a defense," ]{.class_1791}in the sense that it can defend the owner from all kinds of mental and emotional attacks, as well as physical attacks. Proverbs 25:28 likens a man with no wisdom (self‑control, in that case) to a city that can be attacked and broken into and sacked. ["Money is a defense" ]{.class_1791}in the same sense, for it can buy security measures, post guards, pay off lawyers and judges, buy food and clothing (to defend you from starvation or the weather), or help you out of various jams. Wisdom, however, has an advantage over money in that since ["the fear of the Lord is the beginning of wisdom." ]{.class_1791}Wisdom can keep you from getting killed. It can give you LIFE. A rich man, no matter how rich he is, can have his soul required of him in one night because he doesn't fear God; his income cannot "buy off" the grim reaper. In the sense of the New Testament, this ["wisdom"]{.class_1791} would be Christ (Prov. 8:12--36; 1 Cor. 1:24; Col. 2:3). The last clause (["that wisdom giveth\...etc."]{.class_1791}) is the predicate nominative of ["excellency." ]{.class_1791}That is, the most excellent knowledge tells you something; it tells you ["Wisdom giveth life to them that have it." ]{.class_1791}Wisdom can save your life when you don't have money, while it is possible to lose your life (and your billfold) if you don't have any wisdom. The ["life," ]{.class_1791}however, is like the one in 1 Thessalonians 3:8 (see Prov. 11:4 and comments in that Commentary). A literal case is given in Ecclesiastes 9:13--15. In history, this turns out to be Hezekiah (Isa. 37--38).

From a spiritual standpoint, wisdom imparts life; money only defends it.

["Who can make that straight, which he hath made crooked?" ]{.class_1791}Answer: Isaiah 42:16. He can. Only God can straighten out the Devil, and He can do it, even if the Devil is a ["crooked serpent" ]{.class_1791}(Isa. 27:1). God can straighten out nature, although nature doesn't have a straight line in it, as any landscape painter []{#6z0vNAIsTD_RezYjRLYFFA782.xhtml_page_150}knows.

Verse 14 is one of the greatest verses in the Bible. It has two applications. The first one is to an unsaved man; he is given advice that will enable him to take a philosophical view of adversity. The second one is to the saint who needs the same view; however, the saint can go beyond this. Paul rejoices ["in the day of adversity," ]{.class_1791}and David thanks God that he has been afflicted (see 2 Cor. 12:10 and Phil. 2:17). Solomon gives the two opposing "days" to prove that one cancels out the other, leaving man no place where he can hang his hat. The New Testament Christian, however, is given the "days of adversity" to learn:

1\. All events are controlled by his Father (Rom. 8:28).

2\. The adversity is dished out in mercy and is controlled by God (Job 1:12, 2:6).

3\. It will be limited (1 Pet. 5:10, Heb. 12:5--6).

4\. It is purifying (Phil. 3:10, Heb. 12:11), and it will be the source of rewards (Rom. 8:17; 2 Tim. 2:12).

Solomon knows nothing about these matters at all. All he can do is show the agnostic how to handle trouble. "If there is no bright side, polish up the dark side." God makes it impossible for any man to predict his own personal future in detail. Jesus can warn Simon Peter of "things to come" (Luke 22:31), Judas can read his own death warrant, written 500 years before he was born (Zech. 11:13), and God showed Paul the time of his death (2 Tim. 4:6--10). But with prosperity and adversity alternating constantly, no man can say if what is ahead of him (["after him"]{.class_1791}) is going to be good times or bad times (boom or bust). It might be either or both. What Solomon calls ["time and chance" ]{.class_1791}(9:11--12) pops up and converts adversity into prosperity, and vice versa. For a shocking example, read Job 20--30, where prosperity collapses completely, and Genesis 40--41 where prosperity pops up, converting total bankruptcy to riches, overnight. Neither operation was predictable.

7:15 All things have I seen in the days of my vanity: there is a just man that perisheth in his righteousness, and there is a wicked man that prolongeth his life in his wickedness.

16 Be not righteous over much; neither make thyself over wise: why shouldest thou destroy thyself?

17 Be not over much wicked, neither be thou foolish: why shouldest thou die before thy time?

18 It is good that thou shouldest take hold of this; yea, also from this withdraw not thine hand: for he that feareth God shall come forth of them all.

19 Wisdom strengtheneth the wise more than ten mighty men which are in the city.

20 For there is not a just man upon earth, that doeth good, and sinneth not.

21 Also take no heed unto all words that are spoken; lest thou hear thy servant curse thee:

22 For oftentimes also thine own heart knoweth that thou thyself likewise hast cursed others.

["All things have I seen in the days of my vanity" ]{.class_1791}(vs. 15). ["There is a just man\...and there is a wicked man\...."]{.class_1791}[ ]{.class_1801}Nothing could be more true. The only thing wrong with the text is that no real Christian could ever be too ["righteous"]{.class_1791}; he could only be too self-righteous. If he was really ["righteous," ]{.class_1791}he would be ashamed of his own righteousness, however right, and he would not even be conscious of it. Job knew this (Job 9:21) more than one thousand years before []{#6z0vNAIsTD_RezYjRLYFFA782.xhtml_page_154}Solomon wrote Ecclesiastes. A sinless life is what God wants from a Christian (1 Thess. 4:3--4), whether He gets it or not (1 John 1:8--10). Sinlessness, however, has no such limited challenges to it as how to get rid of cigarettes, beer, drugs, pornographic magazines, long hair, "shorts," makeup, "matador britches," and "excess jewelry." It would include:

1\. A constant attitude of prayer.

2\. A forgiving spirit towards enemies.

3\. A careful guarding of the mouth against gossip and slander.

4\. A lack of self‑consciousness and a deep sense of God's presence.

5\. A deep sympathy for anyone enduring any kind of sorrow and suffering.

6\. An ability to rejoice with a brother when he gets a victory or blessing that YOU did not get!

7\. No spending of any money without asking God what to buy and where to buy it and how much to spend.

8\. Giving cheerfully above the tithe.

9\. Supporting a family, if you have one.

10\. Praying for your pastor, if you have one.

11\. Speaking up publicly and boldly for Jesus Christ in front of His enemies, your friends and relatives, and government officials!

12\. Being on time at appointments.

13\. Not overeating or oversleeping.

14\. Not coveting someone's house or land or his money.

15\. Paying bills when due.

There are about seven more items, but those will give you some idea of what we are talking about when we speak of righteousness in the New Testament, according to Paul (1 Tim. 2:10; 5:10; 6:18; 2 Tim. 3:17; Titus 2:7, 14; 3:8, and 3:14). That is the "Pauline Gospel" of the "Grace of God," in the "Dispensation of Grace," under "Sovereign Grace." It has more WORKS in it than the Ten Commandments written on the tables of stone.

Modern, "doubly separated," Christian fundamentalism is usually nothing but a set of rules or regulations passed by []{#6z0vNAIsTD_RezYjRLYFFA782.xhtml_page_155}"Congresses" (like those in Col. 2:21), which amount to little more than will‑worship (see comments in that Commentary). A doubly-separated Fundamentalist, who makes twenty alterations in the text of Hebrews because he can't understand it or brands Bible‑believing Christians as "Ruckmanites" or splits local churches over matters of authority so the scholars at some school can control the pulpit, is no more righteous (or separated) than Judas Iscariot.

Examples of wicked man, dying before their time, are Shimei (1 Kings 2:46), Er and Onan (Gen. 38), and Sisera (Judg. 4). Uzzah (2 Sam. 6:7) fulfills verse 16. Out in the world, "Mad Dog" Vincent Coll, Bugsy Siegel, and Vincent "the Schemer" Drucci are good examples of verse 17. Drucci (1885--1927) was a hit man for the northside Chicago mob (O'Bannion). Al Capone sent other hit men (twice) to whack Drucci, but he outshot them both times. Still, he got blown away before he was thirty‑five years old. When he was thirty‑two years old, he was arrested for carrying a weapon and hauled off to jail in the back seat of a patrol car, under the watchful eye of a tough, young cop named Danny Healy. On the way to the station, Drucci---a hot head like Coll, Barbosa, Siegel, and others---began to cuss the cop out. "Nobody talks to me that way, copper! You \*%!! \$%. I'll get you for this. I'll sit on your doorstep. Go on, you kid copper. I'll fix you for this!" Healy put a loaded .38 against Drucci's rib cage and said, quietly, "Shut up." On went the "fool": "You take that roscoe off me, or I'll kick the hell out of you!" Healy kept the gun on him. "I'll take you and your \$\*&%. I'll fix you!" Healy cocked the hammer and said, softly: "Shut up." At this point, Drucci smacked Healy in the face and tried to wrest the pistol from his grip---a sort of "Rodney King" type of operation. Healy blew three holes through him. Drucci died "before his time."

When they got to the police station, the mob lawyer was already on hand, ready to "spring" Drucci. He couldn't spring him; he was deader than a hammer. They gave the corpse to the lawyer, who immediately demanded---a sort of Rodney King type of operation---that the chief try Healy for murder. The police chief laughed at him and said, "We're havin' a medal made for Healy."

Things were different in those days (1925--1933).[ ]{.class_1790}In [those days, ]{.class_1790}it was safe to walk on city streets at night. The Civil Rights Act (1964) []{#6z0vNAIsTD_RezYjRLYFFA782.xhtml_page_156}put the lives and property of every law‑abiding American in jeopardy.

Let me tell you how it was [before ]{.class_1790}the "Civil Rights Act" installed apartheid in America (where black, female, homosexual, and criminal "minorities" could control the majorities on the streets, in the clubs, schools, churches, and law courts). Before the news media pushed through the Civil Rights Act, it went like this:

[Johnny Broderick]{.class_1790} (5 feet, 9 inches, 185 pounds) was called "The Boffer." He was a police officer, the only man with whom Jack Dempsey said he would be afraid to tangle in a bare fist fight. In dealing with a six‑foot, two‑inch collegiate "champion boxer," in a bar, Johnny knocked him slap out with one punch; he was out for fifteen minutes. Bellvue Hospital kept X-rays of Johnny Broderick's fists; all the knuckles on them had been broken at least twice, and three of them had been busted seven times. (Police brutality, etc.) On one occasion, Broderick seized three mobsters and pitched them through a plate glass window and then arrested them for "malicious destruction of property."

Unfortunately (for them), there was no news media who would take their "minority" side against the majority. If the scene had been videoed, the public would have applauded the action. Things were different in those days; you couldn't resist arrest---a sort of Rodney King operation---without paying the piper.

Johnny Broderick's counterparts were Jack "Legs" Diamond, "Dutch" Schultz, Bugsy Siegel, Lucky Luciano, Vito Genovese, and Albert Anastasia ("Murder Inc."). When he was sent to arrest (and bring in) Jack "Legs" Diamond, Johnny simply hauled him out of a theatre, knocked him down on the pavement with his fists, and then picked him up bodily and jammed him (head first) into a large garbage can on the main street. And there he left Jack "Legs" Diamond, kicking his legs in the air, before a laughing crowd. When asked why he had not brought "Legs" in, Johnny said, "Shoot, some crooked lawyer would have gotten him off the hook in an hour." As a consequence, Jack was so humiliated, by being made a laughing stock of the whole city (including his own gang), that he had to "fold up his tent" and leave New York. Later, he got "hit."

Things were different in those days. In those days (before the []{#6z0vNAIsTD_RezYjRLYFFA782.xhtml_page_157}Civil Rights Act), a middle‑aged woman could walk through Central Park at midnight, by herself, without Mace or a guard dog on a leash. Apartheid changed all of that.

Johnny Broderick wouldn't drink or smoke, and he refused to go and see [Little Caesar ]{.class_1790}(a gangster movie) because of the effect it would have on his children. He died, peacefully, in bed, at the age of eighty‑two.

Verse 18 sheds some light on verses 10 and 14, for it shows that in spite of Solomon's pessimistic, naturalistic, humanistic thinking, he has something in the back of his mind about which he is not really preaching. ["He that feareth God shall come forth of them all" ]{.class_1791}(vs. 18) is a statement to show that the "wise and foolish," "the righteous and the wicked," and "the rich and the poor" (7:15; 6:2, 8; 7:4; 5:12, 16, and 4:8, 13), plus all those named so far, have someone present who will come out ahead of them all; [it is a man who fears God. ]{.class_1790}Jamieson wrongly ascribes ["them all" ]{.class_1791}to only two classes: the ones mentioned in verses 16 and 17. Thus he "contexted" the passage out of its application (see the discussion on Psalm 12, in [The Bible Believer's Commentary on the Psalms, ]{.class_1790}1992). To stop the other destructive critics from falling into this trap, the [AV ]{.class_1790}translators placed an ["also" ]{.class_1791}in verse 18, so you could see that the first clause (["take hold of this"]{.class_1791}) was a reference to verses 16 and 17. Then, there followed ["also from this," ]{.class_1791}which is an added statement that you are to keep in your hands (see Titus 1:9 and Psa. 149:6). What you are to hang on to is the fact that the man who fears God will come out ahead of the over‑righteous, the over‑wicked, the wise, the foolish, the rich, the poor, the married, the single, and anyone else mentioned between chapter one and chapter seven.

For ["the fear of the LORD," ]{.class_1791}see Job 28:28 and Proverbs 1:7, 29, in those Commentaries. Verses 19 and 20 are completely dislocated from the contexts in which they appear; therefore, any attempt to limit their application to verse 18 or verse 21 will be a disaster. No man in the National Geographic Society has found out what is in the heart of the earth; he conjectures it is molten nickel. (I have heard two other conjectures.) I know a man who swears that the earth is hollow, and I have it on the authority of a man (who never lied!) who died and went down, and came back up again, that the souls of men are underground---some of them in torment (Luke 16:28) and some ["comforted." ]{.class_1791}And some twentieth-century nuclear physicist thinks Solomon was a dumbbell for not knowing about sedimentary, metamorphic, and igneous rocks, or the magma layer? Suppose you found out that deep in the earth was a core or a mantle, and [didn't ]{.class_1790}find there was a Bottomless Pit, Sheol, Abraham's Bosom, and Paradise. What then? In 1960, Dr. Blackwood, of the United States Department of the HEW, said, "No scientific instrument has ever penetrated more than two or three miles below the earth's surface."

"It was far from me\...who can find it out?"

But why stop with the earth's core or its mantle or its ocean beds? Why not see if you can find out what is going on up on Jupiter, Venus, Mars, Saturn, or Mercury, by sending up a satellite camera? [They did. ]{.class_1790}Now what do they know? Not one cotton pickin' thing that solves [one problem ]{.class_1790}man has had on this planet for 6,000 years of recorded history. Suppose you really succeeded in finding out what was true about something ["deep" ]{.class_1791}and ["far off." ]{.class_1791}What then? The bathyscaphe Trieste descended 35,820 feet into the Marianna Trench (Jan. 23, []{#6z0vNAIsTD_RezYjRLYFFA782.xhtml_page_163}1960); that is 6.78 miles down. They descended to find out that which is ["exceeding deep." ]{.class_1791}What did they find? They found a temperature of thirty‑seven degrees, which tells nobody anything; they found that the pressure was 16,883 pounds per square foot, which sheds light on nothing; and they spent about \$2,000,000 that didn't solve [one problem ]{.class_1790}on earth since Cain knocked Abel's brains out.

So you know the crust of the earth is a granite mantle, and the inner core is liquid (or the outer core is!). What then? You have found out the earth weighs six sextillion, 588 quintillion tons, which means\...? The inside of the earth is probably heating up, the surface is 196,950,000 square miles, and its volume is 259,000,000,000 cubic miles, which means\...? It means that if you've got the world on your shoulders, you've got a "crick" in your neck.

What did you find out? Having found it out, what can you do with it, except make a living teaching it to people who can't do anything more with it than you could? What did any psychotic physicist, since Einstein, ever discover about "mesons," "quasars," "quarks," or "black holes" that could even slow down international terrorism, national bankruptcy, or the drug traffic?

"Galaxy M‑82 had a tremendous explosion way back in 1,500,000 B.C., and a 'pulsar' was discovered in 1967, with its pulse coming every 1.3373019 seconds!" Boy! That ought to stop ten murders a day in Washington, D.C. Man! Lay that one on the Catholic terrorists in South Ireland, and peace will come overnight; right? The universe is 15,000,000,000 years old (or 16,000,000,000, or 17,000,000,000, or 18,000,000,000, or 19,000,000,000, etc., give or take a few million years; science is very "exact"); and our sun has an expected lifetime of 11,000,000,000 years (or 9,000,000,000 or 10,000,000,000 or 12,000,000 000, etc.). Now? Now, nothing. Go as ["far off' ]{.class_1791}as you want to and get facts. Learn that the mass of the sun is 332,946 times the earth, and that it burns up 4,500,000 tons of hydrogen every second. Ain't that marvelous? Now, what will []{#6z0vNAIsTD_RezYjRLYFFA782.xhtml_page_164}you do with that information? Prove that the source of all light, heat, and energy on earth is evolving?

But why not go way, way, WAY out to ["seek it out"]{.class_1791} (Ecc. 8:17)? How about as ["far off" ]{.class_1791}(Ecc. 7:24) as the stars? You can see 3,000 with the naked eye, and the nearest one (after the sun) is Alpha Centauri, which is at a distance of 25,000,000,000,000 miles. How is that for ["far off"]{.class_1791}? Now you can learn that our solar system revolves around the center of a galaxy once every 200,000,000 years, at a speed of about 170 miles per second. Boy, are we ever gettin' us some "smart." Ain't education wonderful? We know how big the largest meteorites are. We know about the largest craters, the highest moon mountains, the temperature of the moon, the largest sun spots, the longest eclipse duration, the closest approach of a comet to earth, what a black hole and a super nova are, and what kind of atmospheres are to be found on Jupiter, Venus, Mars, and Saturn. We have gotten the whole act together. Now, are we ["wise"]{.class_1791}?

Face it: in 2,000 years of scientific research and fantastic breakthroughs, you did nothing but create some jobs so that suckers could be conned out of their money to learn what you think you found out. Wouldn't you say that such a response is characteristic of people with low I.Q.'s?

Man looked in the wrong place (Rom. 10:6--7). The answers he got left him just as stupid as when he started, and just as unenlightened as in the days of Alexander the Great. 8:16 When I applied mine heart to know wisdom, and to see the business that is done upon the earth: (for also there is that neither day nor night seeth sleep with his eyes:)

17 Then I beheld all the work of God, that a man cannot find out the work that is done under the sun: because though a man labour to seek it out, yet he shall not find it; yea farther; though a wise man think to know it, yet shall he not be able to find it.

# Chapter 9 {.heading_69}

9:1 For all this I considered in my heart even to declare all this, that the righteous, and the wise, and their works, are in the hand of God: no man knoweth either love or hatred by all that is before them.

2 All things come alike to all: there is one event to the righteous, and to the wicked; to the good and to the clean, and to the unclean; to him that sacrificeth, and to him that sacrificeth not: as is the good, so is the sinner; and he that sweareth, as he that feareth an oath.

3 This is an evil among all things that are done under the sun, that there is one event unto all: yea, also the heart of the sons of men is full of evil, and madness is in their heart while they live, and after that they go to the dead.

4 For to him that is joined to all the living there is hope: for a living dog is better than a dead lion.

5 For the living know that they shall die: but the dead know not any thing, neither have they any more a reward; for the memory of them is forgotten.

6 Also their love, and their hatred, and their envy, is now perished; neither have they any more a portion for ever in any thing that is done under the sun.

The first three words indicate that something must be said about verse 17 in the previous chapter. But if you feels like ah do, deys' g'win to read '10,000 white troops trampled to death'!"

On another occasion (WWI), a colored Major---in nearly the same circumstances---is reported to have said to one of his captains: "According to de orders, we ain't supposed to retreat till de enemy gets widin 100 yards. Ah's a little bit lame, so ah's gettin' started NOW!"

If you really want to see the philosophy of verse 4 illustrated in detail, read the conversation that took place between a Yankee officer and colored enlisted man on the hurricane deck of a Yankee gunboat, right after the Battle of Fort Donnelson (1862). ([Life, Love, and Laughter, ]{.class_1790}Bible Baptist Bookstore, 1992, pp. 152, 163.)

To those not meditative enough to study Buddhism (and for those unwilling to die), the world offers the next two best substitutes: DRUGS and LIQUOR.
