Through thirty years of teaching at PBI (1964--1993), I have counted the [efforts ]{.class_1790}of my pupils to be worth [one‑third]{.class_1790} of their total grade, at the end of each semester. A man flunking Greek or Hebrew, can pass the 70 mark by his attitude, and his [effort ]{.class_1790}put forth to pass those subjects. We call this "attitude," but what it amounts to is the EFFORT the student puts forth to master the work, pay attention in class, maintaining cheerfulness in the face of adversity, and being steadfast and loyal to Christ and his own calling. I count EFFORT to []{#6z0vNAIsTD_RezYjRLYFFA1126.xhtml_page_223}be more important than money, education, clothes, food, equipment, good grades, soul‑winning, intelligence, talent, reputation, blood line, or even character. (I picked up that peculiar "value judgment" somewhere around the age of fifteen; I do not remember having it taught to me by anyone.) In 1949, I heard Bob Jones Sr. say: "It is a sin to do less than your best." In 1950, I heard him say: "All things being equal, a Christian should be able to outdo a sinner in anything he does." I believe that. I believe that applies to writing, art, teaching, music, bodybuilding, preaching, the military, and all sports.

I like to watch a distance runner getting hyper‑ventilated (or hyper‑dehydrated) 100 meters from the "wire," and then finish the race staggering off and on the track, till he (or she) drops from third place to tenth place. I like to watch some young buck climb halfway up a six‑foot wire fence, trying to field a fly in softball and, then, after missing it, fall flat on his face. I like to see a kid "reach for one" on a ping‑pong game, in the basement, and bang his head slap into a furnace pipe, while trying to return the ball.

EFFORT: that is what impresses me. I don't know (nor care) who else it impresses, but it has always impressed me more than anything. A man who becomes rich or successful, famous or honored, without effort, means no more to me than Michael Jackson getting a Grammy award or Bill Clinton winning an election. I am always more fascinated with the effort than the results.

"All glory to God to the hero who wins the prize!"

The world has cried for a thousand years.

But what of the [failure ]{.class_1790}who tries and dies

With his EFFORTS bathed in his tears?

Oh, great is the hero who wins him a name,

But greater far, many a time,

Is some pale‑faced fighter who dies in shame,

With his back to the wall and his feet on the line!"

"Do it with thy might."

I always loved "Felix the Fourth." Felix was a Cuban postman from Havana. He wanted to race in the Olympics, being held in St. []{#6z0vNAIsTD_RezYjRLYFFA1126.xhtml_page_224}Louis, Missouri (1904). Felix had no money, so he worked his way over to New Orleans on a banana boat. He then jogged from New Orleans to St. Louis---in his postman's shoes---and got there just in time to enter the race. "Just in time," meant he had TWO HOURS rest before the race started. He was so bushed he placed FOURTH in the race; after jogging more than 450 miles.

Effort, man! Effort!

(It is a good thing that I was not the deciding judge for that race; I would have given Felix the gold, no questions asked. As far as I am concerned, HE won it.)

I will always be partial to Charles Zimmy. He had no legs, but when he was past seventy‑five years of age he swam the Hudson River from Albany to New York City (130 miles).

"Do it with thy might."

Nothing on earth is more disgusting to me than someone like Mark Spitz, who won four gold medals swimming the Olympics. He did this without cutting one lock of his pretty long hair. (Any swimmer knows that hair collects weight in the water, and the last thing you need, swimming in water, is weight.) Spitz could have cut one half a second (or more) off every lap he swam if he had "burred," or "cue balled," his pretty head. Mark was in love with his hair. He couldn't mutilate it, so he got by with his second best, and the world cheered him as a hero (1972). He was a loafer: no real effort. I am not surprised that he dropped completely out of sight, as a hero, and never prospered in one undertaking after 1972, for the next twenty years. No real effort.

9:11 I returned, and saw under the sun, that the race is not to the swift, nor the battle to the strong, neither yet bread to the wise, nor yet riches to men of understanding, nor yet favour to men of skill; but time and chance happeneth to them all.

12 For man also knoweth not his time: as the fishes that are taken in an evil net, and as the birds that are caught in the snare; so are the sons of men snared in an evil time, when it falleth suddenly upon them.

The "returning," of verse 11, is another one of those places like Ecclesiastes 5:18, 8:17, and 4:1. He is returning to his thoughts after a considerably long interval. ["The race is not to the swift" ]{.class_1791}although that is the way to bet. ["Nor the battle to the strong," ]{.class_1791}although in ancient combat the odds were certainly in his favor. ["Neither yet bread to the wise," ]{.class_1791}although they can nearly always make a living. ["Nor yet riches to men of understanding," ]{.class_1791}although if they are worldly wise (Luke 16:19) they usually make out quite well.[ "Nor yet favour to men of skill," ]{.class_1791}although the rule is otherwise (see Prov. 22:29). ["But time and chance happeneth to them all" ]{.class_1791}(vs. 11).

The problem is that ["time and chance" ]{.class_1791}fall ["suddenly" ]{.class_1791}(vs. 12) on the victim. There is no time for preparation and there is no warning because ["man also knoweth not his time" ]{.class_1791}(vs. 12).

1\. No matter how swift the horses are (Isa. 30:16), if the swift are running to mischief (Prov. 6:18), they will be overtaken. Asahel was swifter than Abner (2 Sam. 2:19--23). It cost him his own life: ["the race is not to the swift."]{.class_1791}

2\. The ["strong" ]{.class_1791}man in 1 Samuel 17:4 was, obviously, Goliath, and the ["strong" ]{.class_1791}army, in 1 Kings 20:27, outnumbered Israel about ten to one. In both cases, the ["strong" ]{.class_1791}got clobbered.

3\. Micaiah had plenty of wisdom (1 Kings 22:14), but all he got from it was "bread of affliction" (1 Kings 22:27). Elijah had to be fed by ravens (1 Kings 17:3--5), although he had ten times as much wisdom as his kingly persecutor (Ahab).

4\. Paul was certainly a man of understanding. He died flat broke; as broke as any pauper in an alms house in the nineteenth century.

5\. To "update" things, observe that when men of skill show up (Norman Rockwell, Howard Pyle, Frank Frazetta, Karl Evers, Frank McCarthy, Paul Detlefson, and Maxfield Parrish---any one of whom could out paint Picasso, Warhol, Gauguin, Mondrian, Pollock, Kooning, Goya, Braque, or Miro, blindfolded---they are not even recognized by the news media as artists. Everyone of them (the first list) lived and died with the blot of "illustrator" tagged on him, simply because he could out draw and out paint and out think the artists. The amateurs who were shown favor---the second list---could not even DRAW, let alone paint. Their talent had nothing to do with []{#6z0vNAIsTD_RezYjRLYFFA1126.xhtml_page_226}their value as artists. It had to do with "good press." The news media, critics, and writers read talent into talentless works.

McCarthy's western pictures are superior to any of Remington's paintings, and Evers' seascapes would put Winslow Homer's seascapes up on dry land. Maxfield Parrish's handling of landscapes would make Turner's landscapes look like cartoons. When it comes to original ideas, composition, light and shadow, brush technique, and perspective, Norman Rockwell could out‑paint any impressionist or expressionist (or avant garde) who ever picked up a palette. Franzetta (who paints for science‑fiction magazines) can handle anatomy and texture (of marble, stone, cloth, metal, and animals' skins) like no modern artist in the last one hundred years could handle them. But all of these "men of skill" were, unfortunately, connected with commercial art. This is "verboten" among left‑wing, fornicating, welfare radicals who think they are philosophers because they are BROKE. If a man cannot paint or draw---say, someone like Miro, Kooning, Beckmann, Roualt, Picasso, Modigliania, Klee, or Mondrian, et al.---the PRESS must convert him into an artist.

You see, nobody would pay \$100 for the junk that Van Gogh turned out. No one did the entire time he was alive. He became a multimillionaire after he was dead (and probably in Hell) more than fifty years. Picasso (apart from the press) was a cartoonist who majored in [glorified doodling.]{.class_1790} It is the Soviet-Catholic press that sold the public on the idea that Picasso was an artist. They did a good job. That is how Pablo became a millionaire: he fit into the news media [politically correct ]{.class_1790}position: a Communist Catholic. He couldn't paint a barn or draw flies. Modern Art sells on the basis of mental gymnastics performed by professional writers and critics who are intent on reading something (anything) into the ghastly scribbling and wallpaper designs they view, since God knows there isn't enough evidence of "talent" in the mess to package into a match folder.

Van Gogh's tremendous artistic appeal (see page 177) has nothing to do with genius or talent, or even [proficiency]{.class_1790}. It has to do with a book that Irving Stone wrote about him, called [Lust for Life,]{.class_1790} followed by forty years of undeserved publicity on the grounds that []{#6z0vNAIsTD_RezYjRLYFFA1126.xhtml_page_227}psychotic, left‑wing radicals are heroes and leaders. Van Gogh's value lies in the fact that he was a suicidal maniac, without one ounce of common sense or inspiration and he lived the life of a frustrated, fornicating neurotic. He put this mental condition on canvas. In the twentieth century, this is the kind of mentality that is [politically correct]{.class_1790}. Van Gogh did not paint the ear he cut off; he did not paint the hand he nearly burned in two; he did not paint the self‑inflicted gunshot wound in his belly, but his paintings (if you can call them that) reveal, partially, his "lifestyle." (You can find it reproduced by inmates of insane asylums, who mess with paints.) Van Gogh found no answers to anything: not one problem in life, including ANY of his own personal problems. As a [man]{.class_1790}, he was a total failure, and, as an [artist]{.class_1790}, he was a tragic clown. This accounts for his value in 1993. If you have a Van Gogh and a Picasso (a Marxist Roman Catholic) you are [politically ]{.class_1790}correct. An ear cut off, and given to a whore, doesn't mean that you are [talented. ]{.class_1794}Nor does a picture of a bull in a China shop, during a power failure, make you able to paint the "bombing of Guernica." ["Time and chance" ]{.class_1791}are deadly. An American POW in Korea (1945), who had been on the Death March, and survived []{#6z0vNAIsTD_RezYjRLYFFA1126.xhtml_page_228}Cabanatuan, the Davao Penal Colony, and "The Tennis Court," etc. was killed, AFTER the war was over, by a falling case of tomatoes from an American plane engaged in dropping food.

Audie Murphy (1925--1971), the Congressional Medal of Honor winner, was killed May 31st (Memorial Day) of 1971, in an airplane crash. He burned to death in this crash which occurred near Martinsville, Virginia. In the war, he had fired a 50‑caliber machine gun from a half‑track that was on fire, and did it so effectively that he held up a whole German battalion for over an hour. ["Time and chance" ]{.class_1791}got him at the ripe old age of forty-five. The original "Rocky" (Rocky Marciano: 1924--1969) could whip anything that walked on two legs. Computerized boxing (worked out in the 1980's) gave the "gold belt" to Marciano in fights with Jack Dempsey and Cassius (Mohammed Ali) Clay. But[ "time and chance" ]{.class_1791}knocked Rocky slap out of the ring at the age of forty‑five. He was killed (Sept. 1, 1969) in a plane crash near Jasper, Iowa. Will Rogers (1885--1945) was also killed in an airplane crash.

Sometimes ["time and chance" ]{.class_1791}catch up with the sons of men while on the highway. General George S. Patton (1885--1945) got it in a seven‑seater, 1938 Cadillac "75 Special," near Mannheim, Germany, at a speed of about 30 m.p.h.. He died the twenty‑first of December. Joseph P. Kennedy Jr. (1915--1944) and Knute Rockne (1888--1931) both died in air crashes. The author of [Gone With the Wind ]{.class_1790}(Margaret Mitchell: 1900--1949) was hit by a car while walking across Peachtree Street in downtown Atlanta. She survived, in a coma, for five days, and then died August 16, 1949: she never reached her fiftieth birthday.

George Bernard Shaw (1865--1950), a practical atheist and Bible mocker, slipped and fell while trimming shrubs in his garden. After two operations, a kidney infection killed him. The Great Wallenda (Karl Wallenda: 1905--1978) was walking across a 300‑foot wire strung between two hotels, in San Juan, Puerto Rico, about one hundred feet above ground. He had walked the tight rope since he was ten years old. Two gusts of wind came up (["time and chance"]{.class_1791}). He knelt on the wire to wait till the swaying stopped; it didn't. A moment later, he fell one hundred feet to his death (["an evil time when it falleth suddenly upon them"]{.class_1791}).[ ]{.class_1791}He landed on []{#6z0vNAIsTD_RezYjRLYFFA1126.xhtml_page_229}the roof of a taxi and bounced off onto the cement.

Your chances of meeting the grim reaper are as follows:

Per capita, you are most likely to lose your life in America in the following places: West Virginia, District of Columbia (the capital), Florida, Missouri, Arkansas, and Pennsylvania; in that order. You are most likely to lose it in a car wreck in New Mexico, Wyoming, Nevada, Arizona, and Montana; in that order. However, those figures are per 10,000 population. The real places to get "wasted" are New York City (over 1,000,000 blacks), Washington, D.C. (over 200,000 blacks), Detroit (over 200,000 blacks), Miami (Mafia), Houston (drug traffic), Las Vegas (Mafia), and Los Angeles (drugs). But for instant death, as soon as possible (dropping dead before you are thirty‑five years old), the place to move to is AFRICA. There, your life expectancy will be twenty‑five years old (Gabon), twenty‑nine years old (the Chad), thirty‑one years old (in Togo), thirty‑two years old (Burkino Faso), thirty‑three in the Central African Republic, and thirty‑four in West Cameroon. Here, the population is 99 percent black.

The second highest killer among young people (14 to 24), barring auto accidents, is SUICIDE. In the U.S.A., one hundred people (per day) commit suicide (3,650 a year), which now beats Denmark, Japan, and Austria. Most of the 3,650 are under twenty‑five years of age. This is the fruit of teaching evolution in the schools (no goal, no purpose; life is an accident) by the divine fiat of the NEA and federal judges. Somewhere, between 1347 and 1355, more than 75,000,000 people were suddenly killed by ["time and chance." ]{.class_1791}They just "popped off' (as the British say), and compiled a total of deaths larger than both World Wars (1914--1918; 1939--1945). The Bubonic Plague []{#6z0vNAIsTD_RezYjRLYFFA1126.xhtml_page_230}(the Black Death) did them in. "Chance" hit New York and New Orleans in 1832; 2,251 perished in New York and 6,000 in New Orleans. Cholera did the work. By "chance," an epidemic of influenza closed out World War I, and this disease did away with more people than the total military casualties of BOTH sides that had fought. In the last year of that war (1918), 20,000,000 people died of influenza: 500,000 of them were United States citizens.

A famine (1959--1961) finished off 30,000,000 Chinese, while another 900,000 of their countrymen perished in a flood (the Yellow River). That is more loss of life than the American armies suffered in the war in Vietnam, the Korean War, and World War I, combined.

"Time and chance happeneth to them all."

A volcano erupted in Indonesia (April 7, 1815) and snuffed out the lives of 92,000 people. An avalanche in Peru (May 31, 1970) eliminated 18,000 more. You can't tell when an avalanche or a volcano is going to demonstrate its power (Ecc. 9:12).

If you want to take your chances, your chances of staying alive are as follows: people live longest in Sweden, but it had the highest suicide rate in Europe for ten years running (1960--1970). People live longest in Sweden, then in Norway, and then in Denmark. P.S. Denmark surpassed Austria and Japan in suicides back between 1987 and 1989.

["As the fishes that are taken in an evil net, and as the birds that are caught in the snare" ]{.class_1791}(vs. 12). 9:13 This wisdom have I seen also under the sun, and it seemed great unto me:

14 There was a little city, and few men within it; and there came a great king against it, and besieged it, and built great bulwarks against it:

15 Now there was found in it a poor wise man, and he by his wisdom delivered the city; yet no man remembered that same poor man.

16 Then said I, Wisdom is better than strength: nevertheless the poor man's wisdom is despised, and his words are not heard.

17 The words of wise men are heard in quiet more than the cry of him that ruleth among fools.

18 Wisdom is better than weapons of war: but one sinner destroyeth much good.

Again, there is a gap between the thinking going on in verses 11 and 12 and this section. It could have been "jotted down" anytime.

The case given (vss. 14--15) almost matches 2 Samuel 20:15--22, or 2 Kings 18--19, but not quite. The man who delivers Jerusalem by his ["wisdom" ]{.class_1791}is a rich man (Hezekiah), although he follows Isaiah's instructions; but Isaiah is not poor. ["Abel" ]{.class_1791}is delivered by a wise woman, not a wise man (2 Sam. 20), so the analogy is not exact. The woman delivers Abel-Bethmaachah by negotiations, and Hezekiah delivers Jerusalem by prayer. Solomon says he knew about the matters that took place in verses 14--17. How could he have known them?

When Jamieson hits the passage, his crankcase falls out, the driveshaft drops down, and the wheelbearings go rolling down the highway like a pinball machine. He says, "The parable here represents the Israel of God, poor, judged by the world, indeed, in worldly goods, but rich in heavenly wisdom and might. Though despised now, the true Church of God has in it Christ as her wisdom\...etc." Jamieson reduces it to a spiritual, New Testament parable. His exposition is about as far "off base" as the bleachers.

The problem, again, is ignorance; Jamieson cannot locate the incident in Scripture, so he threw it out. It is apparent that Jerusalem is not a "little city" in Jeremiah's day or Hezekiah's day. Jeremiah does NOT get the city delivered after it is ["besieged," ]{.class_1791}and has []{#6z0vNAIsTD_RezYjRLYFFA1126.xhtml_page_232}["built great bulwarks against it."]{.class_1791}

But Jamieson (and those like him) have forgotten that Solomon has been hobnobbing with the wisest men of his time and every major ruler of his time within 1,000 miles. Here, he is drawing from personal experience through a lifetime of dealing with the rulers of Syria, Arabia, Mesopotamia, North Africa, Phoenicia, Greece, and Asia Minor. An actual case might not have been within 200 miles of Jerusalem. The commentators, in their haste to drag the reader down to their level of ignorance, forgot that ["all the kings of the earth" ]{.class_1791}came to Solomon. Who would be fool enough to think they didn't bring any information with them or that Solomon wouldn't have pumped them for information? The man whom they came to see ["spake three thousand proverbs," ]{.class_1791}and one of them is Proverbs 29:8: look at it.

["Yet no man remembered that same poor man\...the poor man's wisdom is despised, and his words are not heard\...the words of wise men are heard," ]{.class_1791}(vss. 16--18).

# Chapter 10 {.heading_69}

10:1 Dead flies cause the ointment of the apothecary to send forth a stinking savour: so doth a little folly him that is in reputation for wisdom and honour.

2 A wise man's heart is at his right hand; but a fool's heart at his left.

3 Yea also, when he that is a fool walketh by the way, his wisdom faileth him, and he saith to every one that he is a fool.

4 If the spirit of the ruler rise up against thee, leave not thy place; for yielding pacifieth great offences.

(Crippled man in hospital, talking with a visitor.)

"Had a plane crash the other day! Had to bail out!"

"Oh man, that was BAD!"

"No, it was good. I had a parachute."

"Oh, good! Good thing you did!"

"No, it was bad; my chute didn't open."

"Oh! That was BAD!"

"No, it turned out all right. I saw a haystack under me, coming down."

"Oh, GOOD! Thank goodness for the haystack!"

"No, it was bad, because there was a pitchfork in the stack."

"Oh, that's read bad!"

"No, it was GOOD. I missed the pitchfork."

"Whew! That was good."

"No, it was bad; you see, I missed the HAYSTACK!"

11:1 Cast thy bread upon the waters: for thou shalt find it after many days.

College graduates (and those who believe the slop they put out in the newspapers, magazines, and books, and via radio and TV), think like ANIMALS (see Ecc. 3:18), while inventing vocabularies to make you []{#6z0vNAIsTD_RezYjRLYFFA1562.xhtml_page_287}think they are higher than animals. They are not: they are brutes, controlled by brute instincts. They are related to animals, according to their own profession, and are, therefore, EXEMPT from personal accountability to God. Judgment for sins AFTER death is the one Biblical truth that no modern man can accept. His life will not allow it. If he [does ]{.class_1790}allow it, he will immediately convert the coming judgment into a fiasco where the Bible‑rejecting, Christ‑denying, sex-crazy, money-mad, self-justifying, religious egotist will give an account to a mammoth, hugging, kissing, forgiving, permissive Santa Claus who has no more convictions about morals than the sinner facing him. The coming judgment is based on ABSOLUTE RIGHTEOUSNESS: [God's ]{.class_1790}(Rom. 10:1--5) versus [man's ]{.class_1790}(Job 22:3 and 40:8). ["Truly the light is sweet, and a pleasant thing" ]{.class_1791}(vs. 7). Absolutely true (1 Tim. 6:17). "It's good to be alive," as the saying goes. If circumstances are so tragic that, like Job, you wish to go back into darkness (Job 3), try life without being able to see the sun; that is, try it as a [blind man, ]{.class_1790}and see if that improves anything; it doesn't. ["The days of darkness" ]{.class_1791}(vs. 8) will not be anymore cheerful simply because you are blind. ["The days of darkness" ]{.class_1791}are described in the next chapter. Even if a man lives out the ["threescore and ten" ]{.class_1791}with rejoicing (vs. 8), the ["days of darkness" ]{.class_1791}are coming. True, these matters are variable. I have seen godly old Methodist ministers go, rejoicing, up into their nineties, and then only see about ninety days of darkness. I have seen saints go up to eighty‑eight years of age, in nearly perfect health, and then die in their sleep, without any anesthesia, oxygen mask, pacemaker, private nurse or a hospital bill. Again, I have seen the saints stagger and twist through life on crutches and in braces for fifty years and then still have to put up with old age.

["All that cometh is vanity" ]{.class_1791}(vs. 8). All the clocks that tick, all the chimes that strike, and all the afternoon shadows point to the approaching darkness. [Prophetically ]{.class_1790}speaking, the references (here) are all to the Great Tribulation (see 12:2--5). The Church Age matches Psalm 90:6, and Christ does not "renew His youth" till this age is over (Psa. 110:3). Naturally, 100 percent of the revisors, commentators, linguists, and professors miss the application. (What else would you expect from hypocrites that [use ]{.class_1790}a Bible they don't [believe ]{.class_1790}[]{#6z0vNAIsTD_RezYjRLYFFA1562.xhtml_page_288}in? The laws of Biblical exposition and Biblical exegesis are as fixed as the laws of Thermodynamics. You mess with the Book and God messes with your mind. It is just as [natural ]{.class_1790}for a saved Greek or Hebrew scholar (who professes to believe in ALL of the fundamentals) to miss two hundred Scriptural references that deal with Biblical truth as it is for an [atheist ]{.class_1790}in the ACLU to miss John 3:16.)

Verse 9 is Existentialism: "Man is what he makes himself," "The meaning of life is found in decisions which make UNMEANINGFULNESS 'meaningful'," etc. "You become a 'god' by becoming responsible for your decisions." This is Victor Frankl, of the Third School of Psychiatry in Vienna (1950--1970). The verse appears to be Playboy philosophy, at first glance, but a "double‑take" will show you that Solomon is just using this philosophy [temporarily; ]{.class_1790}for, after telling the young man to walk in the ways of his EYES (see Ecc. 2:10), he says ["put away evil from thy flesh" ]{.class_1791}(vs. 10). This would match Job's use of his eyes (Job 31:7). ["Let thy heart cheer thee" ]{.class_1791}(vs. 9), but ["remove sorrow from thy heart" ]{.class_1791}(vs. 10). ["Walk in the ways of thine heart" ]{.class_1791}(vs. 9), but ["the heart is deceitful above all things, and desperately wicked" ]{.class_1791}(Jer. 17:9). Have a good time, young man, and do what you want to, BUT! But don't forget that ["God will bring thee into judgment" ]{.class_1791}(vs. 9). The verse is not as "playboyish" as it looks. No reader of [Playboy ]{.class_1790}(or [Hustler, Penthouse, Playgirl, Genesis,]{.class_1790} and [Variations,]{.class_1790} for that matter) likes to think about facing God in judgment after death; no, not for five seconds.

["Remove sorrow from thine heart" ]{.class_1791}will have to be a reference to getting things out of the heart that will cause sorrows: mainly, [sin]{.class_1790}. Jeremy Bentham's famous "checks on immorality" are comely at this point. Bentham (1748--1832), a professing Phenomenologist (or Utilitarian), decided that he would rewrite the Ten Commandments for mankind, so they would be more "readable." Bentham was an Atheist and an Evolutionist: i.e., [an animal materialist]{.class_1790}. After discarding the Divine set of "checks" on immorality, Bentham decided to curb his animal instincts and appetites (and those of his students) with four checks that would []{#6z0vNAIsTD_RezYjRLYFFA1562.xhtml_page_289}keep lust, covetousness, and fornication down to a minimum. These were:

1\. Religious sanctions.

2\. Physical sanctions.

3\. Political sanctions.

4\. Popular sanctions.

All of this malarkey is a long way of saying you should consider the results of your actions---the [effect ]{.class_1790}of your actions---in the contemporary situation ("Situation Ethics") in which you find yourself.

1\. Will it get you "in Dutch" with the priest, or your godly mother?

2\. Will it get you sent to the emergency ward or the VD clinic?

3\. Will it cause you to get arrested?

4\. Will it offend some important person you are trying to set up for a "loan"?

All Jeremy did was water down Romans 12, 13, 14, and 1 Corinthians 3, 4, 5, 6, and 1 Thessalonians 5, in order to write his own little Bible. This would make his BRAIN the final, religious authority, on earth, instead of [God]{.class_1790}. Typical Alexandrian stuff (back in 1770). The result of this "reevaluation" of God's Moral Majority, and the redistribution of that authority to an [atheist]{.class_1790}, helped to bring about modern, American morality; i.e., a total and permanent breakdown of all morals in every social group, every class of people, every ethnic group, and age group. Jeremy Bentham's cute, little, "goody‑two‑shoes" philosophy could no more check the animal instincts in man ([self-preservation,]{.class_1790} [self-propagation,]{.class_1790} and [self-gratification]{.class_1790}) than sand crabs could "check" a tidal wave. Bentham was a fool. So was any fool, after 1770, who believed him.

Kant's famous "Categorical Imperative" was another dead fish, weighed on the same scales. It was constructed along exactly the same lines: mental deficiency, Bible rejection, a desire to play God, and a lack of knowledge of human nature. In short, ["man at his best state" ]{.class_1791}(see Psa. 39:5).

Neither Kant nor Bentham (nor Hegel, Descarte, Spinoza, Santayana, Sarte, Russell, or Einstein, for that matter), believed that God Almighty would hold him accountable for his egotistical lying []{#6z0vNAIsTD_RezYjRLYFFA1562.xhtml_page_290}AFTER death (Heb. 9:27).

["Childhood and youth are vanity" ]{.class_1791}(vs. 10). Because both are characterized by self‑will, self‑pity, and self‑centeredness. "Mamma, I'm tired," "Mama, I'm cold," "Daddy, I'm hungry," "When do we get there?" "Why do I have to take a nap?" "Why do I have to go to bed?" "I want one too!" "Why can't I have one now?" These innocent relics of childhood eventually matriculate into youth, and then they come out as: "Why can't I go to the rock concert?" "What is wrong with short‑shorts?" "But, I like tanktops!" "Why can't I have a car now?" "He gets more allowance than I do," "I don't like my teacher," "I don't want to finish school," "Why do I have to go to church?" When we are teenagers, we worry about what our peers think about us; when we are forty years old, we quit worrying about what our peers think about us; and when we reach seventy, we realize that none of our peers were thinking about us at all. They were thinking about themselves: just like [we ]{.class_1790}were.

GOOD NEWS for the young man: follow your eyes and do what you want to do in your heart; rejoice and "go for it," (vss. 7, 9).

BAD NEWS for the young man: God is going to judge you for everything you look at and lust for in your heart. If you are smart, you will count the cost and quit sinning.

# Chapter 12 {.heading_69}

12:1 Remember now thy Creator in the days of thy youth, while the evil days come not, nor the years draw nigh, when thou shalt say, I have no pleasure in them;

2 While the sun, or the light, or the moon, or the stars, be not darkened, nor the clouds return after the rain:

3 In the day when the keepers of the house shall tremble, and the strong men shall bow themselves, and the grinders cease because they are few, and those that look out of the windows be darkened,

4 And the doors shall be shut in the streets, when the sound of the grinding is low, and he shall rise up at the voice of the bird, and all the daughters of music shall be brought low;

5 Also when they shall be afraid of that which is high, and fears shall be in the way, and the almond tree shall flourish, and the grasshopper shall be a burden, and desire shall fail: because man goeth to his long home, and the mourners go about the streets:

6 Or ever the silver cord be loosed, or the golden bowl be broken, or the pitcher be broken at the fountain, or the wheel broken at the cistern.

7 Then shall the dust return to the earth as it was: and the spirit shall return unto God who gave it.

We have pointed out before (under Ecc. 11:8), how this passage, [prophetically, ]{.class_1790}refers to Daniel's Seventieth Week. Here, we treat it in its standard form; as a poetic and figurative description of the infirmities and handicaps of old age.

["Remember now thy Creator in the days of thy youth" ]{.class_1791}(vs. 1).

Bob Jones Sr. (1882--1968) did. He got saved before he was six years old: ditto John R. Rice (1896--1981). Josiah obeyed the verse (2 Kings 22:1--2) and so did Timothy (2 Tim. 3:15). All of these obeyed the admonition. Millions of youths do not (Job 20:11, 13:26, and 36:14). The ultimate goal of [all ]{.class_1790}[]{#6z0vNAIsTD_RezYjRLYFFA1627.xhtml_page_292}public education in America, since 1933 (guided by the ACLU and the NEA), has been to remove every trace of God from the curriculum from grade one to postgraduate school. The NEA doesn't want one youth to [think ]{.class_1790}about his Creator---let alone "remember" Him---from the cradle to the grave. The idea is to copy Karl Marx's setup for Russia, so that a whole populace will be raised as [Atheists:]{.class_1790} this is called "humanism" in the news media. If you want to see what such a venture produces, go (today) to Bulgaria, Romania, and the Ukraine, and see the RESULTS of that kind of public education. Seventy years of Communism---it was never anything but a totalitarian, welfare state system, from start to finish (1920--1990)---destroyed the social life, the economic life, the religious life, and the family life of more than 400,000,000 people. It was done through a concentrated, systematic effort in public education (through the schools) to "cast off the reins" of God Almighty (Psa. 2), and liberate the populace. [That is the task that secular education is devoted to in America, today. ]{.class_1790}They can outdo any Marxist in Russia, in 1992. The NEA, in America, doesn't want one youth in America to remember his Creator from birth to death: his "god" is to be humanity. (Marx called humanity the "people.") In America, Marxism is "alive and well," as a matter of fact, it is [flourishing.]{.class_1790}

["Nor the years draw nigh, when thou shalt say, I have no pleasure in them" ]{.class_1791}(vs. 1).

Youth is heat without light; old age is light without heat. With old age comes loss of enjoyment (2 Sam. 19:35) and, often, bitterness (see documentation in two‑hour series of cassettes called "Without Hope and Without God." These document the lives of Peter Tschaikovsky, Oscar Wilde, Errol Flynn, Elvis Presley, Marilyn Monroe, Edgar Allen Poe, Ernest Hemmingway, Jack London, and two dozen others). Disease and death are the companions of old age.

A TV commentator was interviewing an "old-timer" who had just turned the century mark. After he had "booked" the 100-year‑old for "victim reactions," he tried for an "actualization" of a "reality piece" (news media doublespeak; circa 1990). "Sir, I am only thirty-eight years old, and you are celebrating your 100th birthday today. Is that correct?" "Yes‑siree," said the ancient one, "this year ah hit []{#6z0vNAIsTD_RezYjRLYFFA1627.xhtml_page_293}the 100 mark!" "Well, sir, I hope I will be able to interview you next year, again, at this same time!" The old timer answered, "Well, ah don't know why not! You look like yer in pretty good health."

To a sixty‑five year old: "How you doin' man?"

"Wal, ahm still kickin, but ah ain't raisin' much dust!"

To an octogenarian: "Do you still drink much coffee?"

"Nossir. I spill most of it."

No man has ["pleasure" ]{.class_1791}in days that are filled with visits to the clinic, Medical Center, and outpatient office. No man enjoys amputations, test scans, implants, exploratory surgery, cobalt treatments, sleepless nights, and the exorbitant fees charged by the greatest extortioners in history---the American hospitals and doctors. ["Thou shalt\...have no pleasure in them." ]{.class_1791}They will not be like the days you spent swimming on the beaches, fishing off the piers, hunting in the woods, eating out at the Chinese restaurants, dancing at the discotheque, picnicking with the family, sight‑seeing in the national parks, attending operas and classical concerts, or cooking‑out in the backyard.

["While the sun, or the light, or the moon" ]{.class_1791}(see Rev. 6 and Acts 2 for the prophetic import) ["be not darkened." ]{.class_1791}In this case, covered with clouds like the clouds of Ecclesiastes 11:4: trouble, problems, trials, dangers, threats, testings, opposition. The sun is a type of Jesus Christ, ["the light of the world." ]{.class_1791}When the world comes between the sun and the moon (a type of the Bride of Christ: Song of Sol. 6:10) the sun is eclipsed. The "stars" are the [soul‑winners, ]{.class_1790}in Daniel 12. Thus, all of the devotional and spiritual expositors miss their own "ready‑made line," which they used a thousand times in Job, Psalms, and Ecclesiastes to dodge the doctrinal ramifications of verses. Strange, isn't it, how many times these milky expositors run to a New Testament [spiritual ]{.class_1790}application to avoid an Old Testament [doctrinal ]{.class_1790}truth, and, then, faced with a real place to show their spirituality, they can find no application whatsoever. Strange, isn't it? It would almost make one think they are CARNAL. (See the remarks about the ["city" ]{.class_1791}under Ecclesiastes 10:15, for example.)

Old age is not always a time of spiritual victory or cheerfulness, not even in a Christian. "When it rains, it pours," so the "clouds []{#6z0vNAIsTD_RezYjRLYFFA1627.xhtml_page_294}return after the rain" (vs. 2), not "after the sunshine." There is no sunshine between downpours. An "overcast" holds till the next storm comes. Did you know it is hard to keep your mind on the Body of Christ, soul‑winning, and the Lord, Himself, when your body is aching from head to foot, and you are running a fever of 102[0]{.class_1804}, while the devil is using your nerves for tom‑toms to play Danse Macabre on? All should be bright at the deathbed of a child of God, but often it is not; at least, not in the twentieth century. Those of us who have pastored thirty‑five to forty years know better. We have been at the twentieth-century deathbeds.

["The keepers of the house" ]{.class_1791}can be identified as the [arms ]{.class_1790}or the [legs. ]{.class_1790}The legs hold up "this old house," to keep it from falling. On an athlete, the first thing that goes is his legs; usually KNEES first, although the ankles sometimes go first. Belshazzar give us a fine illustration in Daniel 5:6 of the ["keepers of the house" ]{.class_1791}about to let the house drop down into a dung hill (Ezra 6:11). Other commentators make the ["keepers" ]{.class_1791}the arms and hands, which protect the body, as "guards." The hands (especially) ["tremble" ]{.class_1791}(see the coffee drinker, above). ["The strong men" ]{.class_1791}can be the [legs, ]{.class_1790}if the arms are the ["keepers." ]{.class_1791}But legs don't "bow." It is man's BACK that bows; it is his spinal column, containing the central nervous system. I would take ["the strong men," ]{.class_1791}in this passage, to be a reference simply to strong MEN. These [men]{.class_1790}---the pro‑football and hockey players, the wrestlers and weightlifters---will, eventually, "hunch over."

["And those that look out of the windows be darkened," ]{.class_1791}because they are having trouble with cataracts or glaucoma or, sometimes, blindness. ["And the doors shall be shut in the streets." ]{.class_1791}Shut and LOCKED, in the case of American cities, after the 1964 Civil Rights Act. In doing personal work with Harold Rawlings, in St. Louis (1964), we found two unlocked front doors in [twenty ]{.class_1790}visits. Eighteen of the locked doors kept the safety chain on AFTER they opened the door about three inches. Since then (1964), no one leaves a door unlocked, whether they are in the house or gone. An elderly lady, in Pensacola, said to me (back in 1979), "You know, preacher, these days we are all PRISONERS." She was a seventy‑year‑old widow, living in an apartment, downtown. She had []{#6z0vNAIsTD_RezYjRLYFFA1627.xhtml_page_295}been mugged twice in less than nine months, and the people in the adjoining apartment held weekly "pot" parties, with rock music, that lasted till 3 a.m.

The Civil Rights Act put law‑abiding people in cells, behind bars, and let loose on them every type of depraved criminal known to man. Civil Rights are for four people: women, blacks, sex perverts, and criminals. There are no "civil rights" in effect for white Protestant males or law‑abiding "straights." If a corrupt government can give key positions to women, blacks, queers, and criminals, it can control 300,000,000 people with 50,000 people. The blacks, queers, women, and felons can be CONTROLLED by the government by the fact that they are indebted (this is an old Mafia‑type operation) to the corrupt government for the special privileges given to them. They will have to take orders. This is the meaning of CIVIL RIGHTS in 1993 and 1994.

Give the jockey a more‑than‑generous "loan" of \$100,000, to pay a gambling debt or a drug debt, and then threaten to kill him if he doesn't pay it back in a certain length of time. When he begs for mercy, tell him to "fix" the next "banana" race, and you will let him off the hook. It's that simple. A black will take orders, as long as it is not a [policeman ]{.class_1790}telling him what to do. A female will take orders from a male if he is SINGLE, but not her [husband. ]{.class_1790}A queer will take any order as long as he is allowed the freedom to practise his death style. A criminal will take orders if his bail or release from prison depends on it; you [can control]{.class_1790} [these kinds of people. ]{.class_1790}All you have to do is give them special privileges, called "civil rights." The people no government can control are mature, white, MALE, Protestants who believe in discipline, hard work, initiative, and little or no government controls: those create a problem for any dictator, demagogue, or New Ager.

Senior citizens are not, as a rule, outdoor people. As a class, they spend more time indoors than outdoors, especially if they live in cities. ["The sound of grinding is low" ]{.class_1791}because there are fewer ["grinders" ]{.class_1791}(vs. 3) to chew with. ["And he shall rise up at the voice of the bird," ]{.class_1791}can be a reference to rising before sunrise (Job 7:4). ["Cock crowing" ]{.class_1791}is before morning (Mark 13:35). Again, old people do not sleep well at night; they often get up several times in the middle of the night. ["And all the daughters of musick" ]{.class_1791}[]{#6z0vNAIsTD_RezYjRLYFFA1627.xhtml_page_296}are mainly the voice (the vocal cords) and the ear. These organs produce music or listen to it. Old people are not enthusiastic congregational singers, and the few that retain their love for classical music, cannot hear it as well as they could back in their thirties and forties.

["They shall be afraid of that which is high." ]{.class_1791}([Prophetically]{.class_1790}, Rev. 6:13 and Isa. 24:12, 21, in the Tribulation). [Practically ]{.class_1790}speaking, all old people fear stairways and ladders. The chances of falling down and getting a broken hip are very good in such places. A broken hip on a sixty or seventy‑year‑old man, or woman, does not "patch up" like it does on a teenager. Many senior citizens (in the 1940's and 1950's) were afraid to ride on airplanes. ["And fears shall be in the way." ]{.class_1791}(Prophetically, Rev. 8, 9, 14, and 16). Practically, there are dangers in walking on brick pavements, over cracks in cement, and places where trash is lying around. In addition to this, are unexpected steps, high curbstones, and, in modern times, TRAFFIC. Added to these hazards (since 1964) are black muggers, rapists, sadists, and killers (plus white, sex perverts) who would kill an old man or old woman for twenty dollars, if they knew they "had it on them." No police department in America is out on the streets to PROTECT anyone, especially old men and women. They are there to see that the criminals are protected, and if any policeman makes the mistake of thinking that he is not there to guard the criminal's civil rights, he will shortly be attacked by the news media (100 percent), arrested, charged with something, and then dismissed from the police force. It has happened more than one hundred times in the last ten years.

["And the almond tree shall flourish." ]{.class_1791}In the Near East and Far East, this would be especially noticeable as the populace, there, are [brunettes; ]{.class_1790}when their black hair turns gray (Hos. 7:9) and then WHITE (Prov. 16:31), it resembles the almond tree, in bloom. ["And the grasshopper."]{.class_1791} ([Prophetically, ]{.class_1790}crop destruction in the Tribulation: Joel 1--2). The commentators convert the grasshopper into an [old man, ]{.class_1790}and then say that he not only walks like a grasshopper, but [looks ]{.class_1790}like a grasshopper. Having been a cartoonist and artist for more than sixty years, and having painted more than []{#6z0vNAIsTD_RezYjRLYFFA1627.xhtml_page_297}six hundred water colors, acrylics and oils, plus more than 2,000 pastel pictures, I somehow have failed to notice this resemblance. The day that I see a man, over sixty who resembles (or looks like) a grasshopper, will be "the day."

Perhaps the screwiest of the screwed‑up screwballs among the Bible critics, at this point, would be Kenneth Taylor ([The Living Boo‑boo]{.class_1790}). He comes on strong with his debacle: "A white‑haired, withered old man, dragging himself along; without sexual desire." The [NIV ]{.class_1790}(The Nitwits Irrational Version) picked up one-third of this (as did, also, the [RSV ]{.class_1790}and [NRSV]{.class_1790}) and says "the grasshopper drags himself along." I have been observing grasshoppers, beetles, locusts, water bugs, cockroaches, ants, and centipedes (at close range) for more than [sixty‑five years. ]{.class_1790}The only time I ever saw a grasshopper dragging himself along was after someone had "squshed" him (this is the correct spelling: "S‑Q‑U‑U‑S‑H." The only other up‑to‑date spelling is "SMUSHED," as in "I smushed him."). Grasshoppers NEVER "drag" themselves along, they HOP; that is why they are called grassHOPPERS. I cannot recall the last time I saw an "old, withered, white‑haired man" HOPPING. George Burns quit HOPPING long before he was eighty.

I think that Dodd ([NEB: ]{.class_1790}The Numbskull's Error Book) handles "the original text" just about as originally as anyone could handle it. He says, "and the LOCUST'S PAUNCH is swollen, and CAPER BUDS have no more zest"! There. How is that for real scholarship!? See? The "original Hebrew" had no ["grasshopper" ]{.class_1791}in it, it had no ["burden" ]{.class_1791}in it, and no one "desires" anything. It could be talking about someone eating "caper buds," and getting a "tire" around their middle. Marvelous, is it not, what riches can be found in the "originals," that are "obscured" in the [King James]{.class_1790} [Bible?]{.class_1790} Since all destructive critics of the [King James]{.class_1790} [Bible ]{.class_1790}allow this droll levity in their serious treatment of the "originals," may we not take the same liberties? Why not just translate "Insider stock trading will merge related shares if there is non‑doctrinaire training along with the New Age spirituality"?

The truth is, a ["burden" ]{.class_1791}is something that is heavy to carry. You learn this in the fourth grade in a place, say, like Topeka, Kansas (in 1930). When it comes to animals, the grasshopper is a very light []{#6z0vNAIsTD_RezYjRLYFFA1627.xhtml_page_298}thing alongside a bucking bronco or a Doberman Pinscher guard dog or a German Shepherd attack dog. So the grasshopper would be a very light thing to pick up and carry. You see, you have to pick them up and carry them in order to eat them (see Lev. 11:22); and they are NOT "caper buds." (Notice how all apostate Fundamentalists delight in converting John's ["locusts" ]{.class_1791}into a locust PLANT \[Mark 1:6\]. Apostate Bible critics are quite predictable; they all feed in the same hog wallow.) Old people are sometimes too weak to feed themselves. Even such a light, small, insignificant thing as a grasshopper becomes a ["burden." ]{.class_1791}Simply believe the text, as it stands, and eradicate all of the conjectures, opinions, theories, researches, ideas, beliefs, and interpretations of ALL the scholars who messed with one word in the text. That is the safe way to learn the Scriptures.

["And desire shall fail." ]{.class_1791}This is described in 2 Samuel 19:34--35, by Barzillai, the Gileadite. This is not just the "desire for sex" (as the [NEB ]{.class_1790}puts it---in keeping with the standard, sex obsessional neuroses of the twentieth century press), but the desire for exotic foods, fine clothing, worldly honor, good books, travel, and publicity. ["Desire" ]{.class_1791}(period) fails. ["Man goeth to his long home," ]{.class_1791}in contrast to his "short home"; his life here on this earth (see Job 16:22 and 17:13). ["And the mourners go about the street." ]{.class_1791}(In the Tribulation, more than 2,000,000,000 people die either by famine, war, demons, or food poisoning: see Rev. 5, 9, and 16.) ["Or ever the silver cord\...or the golden bowl\...or the pitcher\...or the wheel" ]{.class_1791}(vs. 6). There are a variety of interpretations. One is that the golden bowl is the [skull]{.class_1790}, while the silver cord is a [figure ]{.class_1790}of a silver cord holding a [lamp ]{.class_1790}up before it drops and breaks. One commentator says that the silver cord is the "spinal marrow," which is white "like" silver.
